Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Shubhat al-Shubha: When a Weak Suspicion Does Not Invalidate a Sale
Ruling on permissibility of seller using money before re-weighing, extending to saffron credit sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shubhat al-riba and shubhat al-shubha and apply this distinction to determine the permissibility of a credit sale involving weighed items of different genera and different weight measures.

Core Idea
When two weighed items differ in weight measure, the suspicion of riba is too weak (shubhat al-shubha) to invalidate a credit sale.

In this passage, the commentator explains an important nuance in Hanafi riba law: not every suspicion of riba invalidates a transaction. He begins by stating that a seller may use cash deposited by a buyer before re-weighing, and then extends this reasoning to the validity of a salam (forward) sale of saffron for cash. The key is understanding the difference between a strong suspicion (shubhat al-riba) that arises when two items share the same weight measure but differ in genus, and a weak suspicion (shubhat al-shubha) that arises when they differ in weight measure as well.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
Note the ruling: the seller may use the cash before re-weighing because the buyer has already weighed it. This sets the stage for analogical reasoning.
The seller's disposal of cash is permissible; this is a foundational point.
2
Understand the analogical extension
The commentator extends the same principle to a credit sale of saffron for cash. Both involve a transaction where the price is paid in advance for goods to be delivered later.
The sale is a salam contract.
3
Recognize the key distinction
The ruling hinges on whether the two items (cash and saffron) are of the same weight measure category. If they are, there is a strong suspicion of riba (shubhat al-riba). If they differ in weight measure, the suspicion is weaker (shubhat al-shubha).
Weight measure refers to the standard of measurement (e.g., grams vs. litres, or different weight systems).
4
Apply the concepts
Since cash and saffron differ in weight measure (cash is measured by weight, saffron may be measured by a different weight standard), only shubhat al-shubha exists. Islamic law disregards such a weak suspicion, so the sale is valid.
Shubhat al-shubha means a suspicion of a suspicion – it is too far removed to have legal effect.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, the credit sale of saffron for cash is permissible (sahih).
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشتری نے بائع کی عدم موجودگی میں نقود وزن کر کے بائع کے سپرد کر دیئے تو دوبارہ وزن کرنے سے پہلے بائع کے لیے نقود میں تصرف کرنا جائز ہے تصرف کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بائع ان نقود کے عوض کوئی دوسری چیز خرید سکتا ہے ان کو ہبہ اور صدقہ بھی کر سکتا ہے پس جب نقود اور زعفران وزن میں صورت معنی اور حکم کے اعتبار سے مختلف ہیں تو ان دونوں میں اتحاد قدر من کل وجہ نہیں پایا گیا اور جب اتحاد قدر من کل وجہ نہیں پایا گیا تو اس میں شہبتہ الربا و شبہتہ الشبہ کے درجہ میں ہو جائے گا کیونکہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ دو موزونی چیزیں اگر من کل وجہ وزن میں متفق ہوں اور دونوں کی جنس ایک نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں نساء ( ادھار ) شہبتہ الربا کی وجہ سے حرام ہوتا ہے اور جب دونوں وزن میں بھی متفق نہ ہوں تو یہ شبہ وزن ہوگا پس جب تمبا وزن کی وجہ سے شہبتہ الربا پیدا ہوتا ہے تو شبہ وزن کی وجہ سے شہبتہ الشبہ پیدا ہو گا یعنی شبہ وزن کی وجہ سے ربوا کے شبہ کا شبہ پیدا ہوگا اور شریعت اسلام میں شبہ تو معتبر ہے لیکن شبتہ الشبہ معتبر نہیں ہے اس لیے نقود کے عوض زعفران کی بیع سلم یعنی ادھار جائز ہے۔
When the buyer weighed the cash and deposited it with the seller in the seller's absence, then before re-weighing, it is permissible for the seller to dispose of the cash. The meaning of disposal is that the seller can buy another item with this cash and can also give it as a gift and charity. Therefore, since cash and saffron differ in terms of weight in form, meaning, and ruling, complete unity of measure is not found between them. And when complete unity is not found, then in this case the suspicion of riba becomes in the rank of suspicion of suspicion. Because it has passed previously that if two weighed items agree completely in weight and their genus is not one, then in that case credit is prohibited due to suspicion of riba. And when they don't even agree in weight, then this is a suspicion of weight. So when suspicion of riba arises due to complete agreement in weight, then suspicion of suspicion arises due to disagreement in weight, meaning that due to disagreement in weight, a suspicion of the suspicion of riba arises. And in Islamic law, suspicion is considered, but suspicion of suspicion is not considered. Therefore, selling saffron for cash as salam, i.e., on credit, is permissible.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It first states the ruling that it is permissible for the seller to use the cash deposited by the buyer before re-weighing, because the buyer has already weighed it and the seller's acceptance is implicit. Then it extends this to the issue of selling saffron for cash on credit (salam). The key legal reasoning is the concept of shubhat al-shubha (suspicion of a suspicion). In riba, when two items that are usually weighed have complete unity in weight measure (like both being measured by the same standard) but different genus, there is a suspicion of riba, which makes the transaction haram. But if they differ in weight measure (like cash by weight and saffron by weight but not the same standard), then the suspicion is even weaker—it is only a suspicion of a suspicion—and Islamic law does not consider such a weak suspicion. Therefore, the sale is valid. This is a clear application of the principle that only strong suspicions (shubha) invalidate transactions, not weak ones.

Key Terms
شبہتہ الربا (shubhat al-riba): A strong suspicion of usury that arises when two items of the same weight measure but different genus are exchanged on credit.
شبہتہ الشبہ (shubhat al-shubha): A suspicion of a suspicion, a weaker degree of doubt that does not affect the validity of a transaction.
بیع سلم (bay' salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for goods to be delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling saffron for cash on credit (salam) permissible in this case?
A) Because saffron and cash are of the same genus.
B) Because they differ in weight measure, creating only a weak suspicion (shubhat al-shubha).
C) Because the seller has used the cash before re-weighing.
D) Because the buyer deposited the cash in the seller's absence.

Key Takeaway
A weak suspicion (shubhat al-shubha) does not invalidate transactions; only a strong suspicion (shubha) does.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Items from Hadith Are Fixed as Makil or Mawzun Forever
Ruling that items mentioned in hadith as makil or mawzun remain so regardless of custom change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the six ribawi items are permanently classified as makil or mawzun and explain why prophetic text (nass) overrides custom ('urf).

Core Idea
The Prophet's designation of measurement type for ribawi items is fixed forever; custom cannot override it.

This lesson addresses a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding riba transactions: the classification of items as volume-measured (makil) or weight-measured (mawzun) is permanently fixed by the prophetic text, regardless of any subsequent change in people's custom. The commentary on Al-Hidayah explains that obeying the Prophet is obligatory and that nass is stronger than 'urf because 'urf can be based on falsehood and is only binding on those who practice it. Therefore, wheat, barley, dates, salt, gold, and silver remain forever in their original measurement categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the exact ruling: items for which the Prophet explicitly prohibited excess through volume (kayl) are forever volume-measured, and those prohibited through weight (wazn) are forever weight-measured. This applies to the six items mentioned in the well-known hadith.
The six items are wheat, barley, dates, salt, gold, and silver.
2
State the first proof: obedience to the Prophet
The commentary argues that obeying the Prophet is obligatory (wajib). Since the Prophet designated each item's measurement type, that designation must be followed forever, even if people's practice changes.
This is a direct dalil from the obligation of following the Sunnah.
3
State the second proof: nass is stronger than 'urf
The prophetic text (nass) is stronger than custom because custom can be based on falsehood (e.g., selling fruit before it appears) and is only binding on those who practice it, while nass is binding on all and carries no possibility of falsehood.
The commentary gives two sub-proofs: (a) custom can be false, nass cannot; (b) custom is local, nass is universal.
4
Apply to examples
Consider selling wheat for wheat: equality must be achieved by volume, not weight. If sold by weight even with equal weight, it is invalid. Similarly, gold for gold must be by weight, not volume.
This shows the practical consequence of the ruling.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may allow custom to change the measurement type for these items, but the Hanafi school holds that nass is decisive and no change is permitted.
This is a pointed ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text

قال وكل شيء نص رسول الله عليه السلام على تحريم التفاضل فيه مكيلا فهو مكيل ابداوان ترك الناس الكيل فيه مثل الحنطة والشعير و التمرو الملح وكل مانص على تحريم التفاضل فيه وزنا فهو موزون ابدا وان ترك الناس الوزن فيه مثل الذهب والفضة لان النص اقوى من العرف والاقوى لا يترك بالادنى 

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جن چیزوں میں کیل کی راہ سے زیادتی حرام ہونے کی تصریح فرمائی ہے وہ ہمیشہ کیلی رہیں گی اگر چہ لوگوں نے ان میں کیل کرنا چھوڑ دیا وہ جیسے گندم، جو، چھوہارے، نمک اور جس چیز میں رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وزن کے اعتبار سے زیادتی حرام ہونے کی تصریح فرمائی ہے وہ ہمیشہ وزنی رہیں گی اگر چہ لوگوں نے اس میں وزن کرنا چھوڑ دیا ہو جیسے سونا اور چاندی ۔ کیونکہ نص، به نسبت رواج اور عرف کے زیادہ قوی ہوتی ہے اور اقوی کو ادنی کی وجہ سے نہیں چھوڑا جائے گا۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عہد رسالت میں جو چیز کیلی تھی یعنی آپ اور آپ کے صحابہ اس میں کیل سے معاملہ کرتے تھے وہ ہمیشہ کیلی شمار ہوں گی اگر چہ لوگوں نے اس میں کیل کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنا ترک کر دیا ہو جیسے گندم، جو، چھوہارے اور نمک پس ان چیزوں میں مساوات اور برابری کیل کے ذریعہ معتبر ہوگی نہ کہ وزن کے ذریعہ چنا نچہ اگر گندم کو گندم کے عوض بیچا گیا اور برابری وزن کے ذریعہ کی گئی نہ کہ کیل کے ذریعہ تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ گندم عہد رسالت میں کیلی تھی اس لیے اس میں قیامت تک کیل ہی کے ذریعہ مساوات اور برابری معتبر ہوگی وزن کے ذریعہ معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ اور جو چیز عہد رسالت میں وزنی تھی یعنی لوگ اس میں وزن کے ساتھ معاملہ کرتے تھے تو وہ ہمیشہ وزنی شمار ہوگی اگر چہ اس میں لوگوں نے وزن کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنا ترک کر دیا ہو جیسے سونا اور چاندی حتی کہ اگر سونا سونے کے عوض بیچا گیا اور کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کی گئی نہ کہ وزن کے ذریعہ تو یہ جائز نہ ہوگا اس کی ایک دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی اطاعت ہم پر واجب ہے پس آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جس کو کیلی قرار دیا وہ ہمیشہ کیلی شمار ہوگی اور جس کو وزنی قرار دیا وہ ہمیشہ وزنی شمار ہوگی ۔ اگر چہ لوگوں کا معاملہ اس کے خلاف پر ہو۔

دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نص یعنی حدیث رسول عرف اور رواج کی بہ نسبت اقومی ہے کیونکہ عرف تو باطل پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے جیسا کہ صاحب فتح القدیر کے زمانہ میں عید کی رات میں قبرستان میں چراغان کرنے پر عرف تھا اور جیسا کہ ہمارے زمانے میں آم ظاہر ہونے سے پہلے آم کے باغات کی فصل کو فروخت کرنے پر لوگوں کا عرف جاری ہے حالانکہ عرف باطل چیز پر ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ عرف باطل پر بھی ہوسکتا ہے اور نص ثابت ہونے کے بعد باطل کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ نص عرف کے مقابلہ میں اقوئی ہے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عرف کا حجت ہونا صرف ان لوگوں کے حق میں ہے جن کا وہ عرف ہے اور جن کا وہ عرف نہیں ہے ان کے حق میں عرف حجت نہیں ہوگا اور نص سب کے حق میں حجت ہوتی ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ نص عرف کے مقابلہ میں اقومی ہے اور اقومی کو ادنی کی وجہ سے ترک نہیں کیا جاتا اس لیے اشیاء کے مکیلی یا موزونی ہونے میں حدیث رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم یعنی نص کو لوگوں کے عرف اور رواج کی وجہ سے ترک نہیں کیا جائے گا اور جب نص کو عرف کی وجہ سے ترک نہیں کیا جائیگا تو جن چیزوں کا نص یعنی حدیث سے مکیلی ہونا ثابت ہے وہ تا قیامت مکیلی ہی رہیں گی اور جن چیزوں کا موزونی ہونا ثابت ہے وہ ہمیشہ موزونی ہی رہیں گی عرف اور رواج کی وجہ سے ان میں کوئی تبدیلی واقع نہ ہوگی۔
Al-Quduri said: Every item for which the Messenger of Allah explicitly prohibited excess through volume (kayl) is forever a volume-measured item, even if people abandon volume-measuring it, like wheat, barley, dates, and salt. And every item for which He explicitly prohibited excess through weight is forever a weight-measured item, even if people abandon weight-measuring it, like gold and silver. Because the text is stronger than custom, and the stronger is not abandoned for the weaker. 

Translation: Al-Quduri said: The items for which the Prophet explicitly prohibited excess through volume will remain volume-measured forever, even if people have abandoned volume-measuring them, such as wheat, barley, dates, and salt. And the items for which the Prophet explicitly prohibited excess through weight will remain weight-measured forever, even if people have abandoned weight-measuring them, such as gold and silver. Because the text is stronger relative to practice and custom, and the stronger is not abandoned for the weaker.

Explanation: The matter is that whatever was volume-measured in the era of the Prophet, meaning he and his companions conducted transactions with volume, it will forever be considered volume-measured, even if people have abandoned transacting with volume, such as wheat, barley, dates, and salt. So in these items, equality and equivalence are considered through volume, not through weight. Accordingly, if wheat is sold for wheat and equality is achieved through weight rather than volume, it is not permissible, because wheat was volume-measured in the prophetic era, therefore until the Day of Judgment, equality through volume will be valid, not weight. And whatever item was weight-measured in the prophetic era, meaning people transacted with weight, it will forever be considered weight-measured, even if people have abandoned transacting with weight, such as gold and silver. So much so that if gold is sold for gold and equality is achieved through volume rather than weight, it is not permissible. One proof of this is that obeying the Prophet is obligatory upon us. So whatever He designated as volume-measured will forever be volume-measured, and whatever He designated as weight-measured will forever be weight-measured, even if people's practice is contrary to this.

The second proof is that the text, meaning the hadith of the Prophet, is stronger relative to custom and practice, because custom can also be based on falsehood, as in the time of the author of Fath al-Qadir, there was a custom of lighting lamps in graveyards on the night of Eid, and as in our time, there is a custom among people of selling the fruit of mango orchards before the mangoes appear, even though the custom is based on falsehood. So it becomes known that custom can be based on falsehood, and the text, once established, does not carry the possibility of falsehood. From this, it is known that the text is stronger than custom. The second proof is that custom is only binding for those people who practice that custom, but for those who do not practice it, custom is not binding. And the text is binding for all. From this too, it is known that the text is stronger than custom, and the stronger is not abandoned for the weaker. Therefore, in the matter of items being volume-measured or weight-measured, the hadith of the Prophet, i.e., the text, will not be abandoned due to the custom and practice of people. And when the text is not abandoned due to custom, then the items for which being volume-measured is established by the text, they will remain volume-measured until the Day of Judgment, and the items for which being weight-measured is established, they will forever remain weight-measured. No change will occur due to custom or practice.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, explaining al-Quduri's matn. The core ruling is that items explicitly mentioned in the hadith on riba (wheat, barley, dates, salt, gold, silver) retain their designated measurement type (volume or weight) forever, regardless of any change in people's custom. The commentary provides two proofs: (1) Obedience to the Prophet is obligatory, so what He designated must remain. (2) The prophetic text (nass) is stronger than custom because custom can be based on falsehood (e.g., selling fruit before it appears) and is only binding on those who practice it, whereas the text is binding on all. Therefore, the text overrides custom, and these items are fixed as makil or mawzun for all time. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding riba transactions.

Key Terms
نص (nass): Explicit textual evidence from the Quran or Sunnah; here, the hadith of the Prophet regarding the six ribawi items.
عرف ('urf): Customary practice of the people; may be used as a source of law when no nass exists, but cannot override nass.
کیل (kayl): Measurement by volume, such as using a container (e.g., sa').
وزن (wazn): Measurement by weight, such as using a scale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the prophetic text override custom regarding the measurement type of the six ribawi items?
A) Because custom is never reliable.
B) Because custom can be based on falsehood and is only binding on those who practice it, while the text is binding on all.
C) Because the Prophet personally used weight for all items.
D) Because the six items are no longer traded.

Key Takeaway
The prophetic designation of measurement type for the six ribawi items is permanent and cannot be altered by subsequent custom, ensuring clarity in riba-free transactions.

Custom vs. Text: The Hanafi Dispute on Measuring Ribawi Items
Intra-Hanafi dispute on custom vs. text for ribawi items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi majority position from Abu Yusuf's position on the role of custom in determining measurement types for ribawi items, and apply the rule that custom governs only where no explicit text exists.

Core Idea
For the six ribawi items, the text is fixed; custom cannot override it — only for unmentioned items does custom decide measurement type.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a key intra-Hanafi disagreement on the tension between textual prescription and customary practice. While all Hanafis agree that custom determines the measurement type for items not covered by the hadith on riba, Imam Abu Yusuf proposed a more expansive role for custom, even overriding the explicit text. The majority (Sahibayn) firmly reject this for the six named items, grounding their position on the suspicion of excess (tawahhum al-fadl). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both views and clarifies the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle for unmentioned items
What is the general rule from al-Quduri? Items not explicitly mentioned in the hadith follow the custom of the traders: if they use kayl (volume), the item is makil; if wazn (weight), it is mawzun.
Custom is considered a proof (dalil) and is like ijma' when no nass exists, supported by the hadith 'What Muslims consider good is good with Allah.'
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's exception
Abu Yusuf holds that custom can override even the explicit text (nass) for the six ribawi items, because the text was originally based on the custom of that time. If the custom has changed, the ruling should follow the new custom.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the majority response
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad as a pair) reject this for the six items. They argue that selling wheat for wheat by weight is not permissible even if customary, due to the suspicion of excess (tawahhum al-fadl). The only exception is salam (forward sale) by weight, because it involves a known quantity.
The majority views the text as binding on all, while custom can be based on falsehood and is only binding on those who practice it.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the majority view of the Sahibayn: for items with explicit text, the text is fixed; custom is followed only where no text exists.
This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah and upheld by later authorities like al-Marghinani.

Source Text

وما لم ينص عليه فهو محمول على عادات الناس لا نها دالة وعن ابى يوسف انه يعتبر العرف على خلاف المنصوص عليه ايضالان النص على ذالك لمكان العادة فكانت هى المنظور اليها وقد تبدلت فعلى هذا لوباع الحنطة بجنسها متساويا وزنا او الذهب بجنسه متماثلا كيلا لا يجوز عندهما وان تعارفوا ذالك لتوهم الفضل على ما هو المعيار فيه كما اذا باع مجازفة الاانه يجوز الاسلام في الحنطة ونحوها وزنا لوجود الاسلام في معلوم

تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جن چیزوں کے کیلی یا وزنی ہونے پر نص موجود نہیں ہے ان چیزوں کا کیلی یا وزنی ہونا تجارت کرنے والوں کی عادت پر محمول ہو گا یعنی اگر وہ کیل کے ذریعہ کاروبار کرتے ہیں تو وہ چیز کیلی شمار ہوگی اور اگر کسی چیز میں وزن کے ذریعہ کاروبار کرتے ہیں تو وہ چیز وزنی شمار ہوگی کیونکہ جس چیز میں لوگوں کی عادت واقع ہوئی ہے اس میں جواز حکم پر لوگوں کی عادت ہی دلیل ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے مار آہ المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن حاصل یہ ہے کہ نص موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں عرف اور لوگوں کا رواج بمنزلہ اجماع کے ہوتا ہے اور اجماع حجت شرعی ہے اس لیے کسی چیز کے مکیلی یا موزونی ہونے پر نص موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں تاجروں کی عادت اور ان کے عرف کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ اگر کسی چیز میں وہ کیل کے ذریعہ معاملہ کرتے ہیں تو وہ چیز
And whatever is not explicitly stated in the text is based on the customs of the people, because custom is also a proof (dalil). And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he considers custom even contrary to the explicit text, because the text was given due to the custom, so the custom was the intended consideration, and it has changed. So based on this, if one sells wheat for its genus equally by weight, or sells gold for its genus equally by volume, it is not permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), even if people have become accustomed to that, because there is a suspicion of excess regarding what is the standard in it, just as when one sells by estimation (mujazafah). But it is permissible to make a salam (forward) sale in wheat and similar items by weight, because salam exists in a known quantity.

Translation: And the item regarding which the Prophet did not explicitly state, it is based on the habits of the people, because habit is also a proof (dalil) for a ruling. And from Abu Yusuf, it is narrated that custom will be considered even contrary to the explicit text, because the text regarding that matter was due to the custom, so the custom was the intended consideration, and the custom has changed. According to this rule, if wheat is sold for wheat equally by weight, or gold for gold equally by volume, it is not permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), even if this practice has spread among people, because there is a suspicion of excess regarding what is the standard in it, just as when sold by estimation (mujazafah). However, it is permissible to make a salam (forward) sale in wheat and similar items by weight, because salam occurs in a known quantity.

Explanation: Al-Quduri states that for items regarding which there is no text about being kayl or wazn, their being kayl or wazn will be based on the habit of the traders, meaning if they conduct business with kayl, then that item will be considered kayli, and if they conduct business with wazn, then it will be considered wazni. Because the item on which people's habit has occurred, the people's habit itself is a proof for the permissibility of the ruling, as the Prophet said: 'What the Muslims consider good is good with Allah.' The gist is that when there is no text, custom and people's practice are like consensus (ijma'), and consensus is a legal proof. Therefore, when there is no text about an item being kayli or wazni, the habit of the traders and their custom will be considered. If they transact with kayl, then that item is...
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-and-dispute from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It addresses items not explicitly mentioned in the hadith regarding riba. The general rule (from al-Quduri) is that such items follow the customary practice of the people: if people measure them by volume (kayl), they are considered makil; if by weight (wazn), they are mawzun. This is because custom itself is a proof (dalil). The passage then narrates Abu Yusuf's view that custom can even override the explicit text (nass) for the six ribawi items, because the text was originally based on the custom of the time. However, the immediate reply (attributed to 'the two' – Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that this does not apply to the six items: selling wheat for wheat by weight is not permissible even if customary, because of the suspicion of excess. The only exception is salam (forward sale) by weight, which is permissible because it falls under a known quantity. The commentary then reinforces al-Quduri's principle: custom is like consensus (ijma') and is authoritative when no text exists, supported by the hadith 'What Muslims consider good is good with Allah.' This lesson highlights an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf's more flexible view vs. the majority position that text overrides custom for the six items.

Key Terms
عادات ('adat): The habitual practice of people; used as a source of law when no explicit text exists.
منصوص علیہ (mansus 'alayh): That which is explicitly stated in the text (nass) of the Quran or Sunnah.
بیع سلم (bay' salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for specified goods to be delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone sells wheat for wheat by weight, even if it is customary?
A) It is permissible according to all Hanafis.
B) It is not permissible according to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because of suspicion of excess.
C) It is permissible only if the seller makes a salam contract.
D) It is permissible because custom overrides text.

Key Takeaway
Custom determines measurement for items not in the riba hadith, but for the six explicit items, the text is fixed and cannot be overridden by custom.

Nass Prevails Over Custom; Custom Applies Where No Nass Exists
Proves superiority of nass over 'urf and states custom applies where no nass exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two proofs for the superiority of nass over custom and apply the rule that items not addressed by nass follow custom.

Core Idea
Nass binds all; custom binds only its followers; nass cannot be overridden by custom.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explores a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh: the hierarchy between textual evidence (nass) and custom ('urf). It presents two clear arguments for why nass takes precedence, using the example of the Prophet's hadith on measuring commodities by volume or weight. It then clarifies that for items where no nass exists, the prevailing custom of traders determines the legal classification. Mastering this hierarchy is essential for correctly analyzing commercial transactions and other rulings where custom and text interact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs for nass superiority
The passage first explains that a custom may be based on falsehood (bāṭil), but nass is free from falsehood. Second, custom is only binding on those who follow it, whereas nass is binding on all people. These two points demonstrate that nass is stronger (aqwā) than custom.
The first proof is logical: nass is divinely revealed and thus cannot be invalid; a custom may be incorrect.
2
Apply the principle to the hadith on measurement
Because nass is superior, the Prophet's hadith that specifies certain items as makīlī (volume-measured) or mawzūnī (weight-measured) cannot be overturned by later custom. Those items remain fixed in their category forever.
For example, wheat and gold are fixed by nass; their measurement standard does not change with time or place.
3
Understand the rule for items not mentioned in nass
The passage states: 'And what is not mentioned in the nass is attributed to the customs of the people.' For items not specified in the Quran or hadith, the traders' customary practice determines whether they are sold by volume or weight.
This is based on the hadith 'Whatever the Muslims consider good is good before Allah,' treating custom as akin to consensus (ijma) in the absence of nass.
4
Recognize the authority of custom in the Hanafi school
Imam al-Quduri confirms that custom in the absence of nass is a valid legal proof (dalīl ḥukm). Customs that are consistent and widespread are given weight, but only when no contradictory nass exists.
This principle is used in many fiqh chapters, especially in mu‘āmalāt (transactions).

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہشتم سے پہلے آم کے باغات کی فصل کو فروخت کرنے پر لوگوں کا عرف جاری ہے حالانکہ عرف باطل چیز پر ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ عرف باطل پر بھی ہوسکتا ہے اور نص ثابت ہونے کے بعد باطل کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ نص عرف کے مقابلہ میں اقوئی ہے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عرف کا حجت ہونا صرف ان لوگوں کے حق میں ہے جن کا وہ عرف ہے اور جن کا وہ عرف نہیں ہے ان کے حق میں عرف حجت نہیں ہوگا اور نص سب کے حق میں حجت ہوتی ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ نص عرف کے مقابلہ میں اقومی ہے اور اقومی کو ادنی کی وجہ سے۔ ترک نہیں کیا جاتا اس لیے اشیاء کے مکیلی یا موزونی ہونے میں حدیث رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم یعنی نص کو لوگوں کے عرف اور رواج کی وجہ سے ترک نہیں کیا جائے گا اور جب نص کو عرف کی وجہ سے ترک نہیں کیا جائیگا تو جن چیزوں کا نص یعنی حدیث سے مکیلی ہونا ثابت ہے وہ تا قیامت مکیلی ہی رہیں گی اور جن چیزوں کا موزونی ہونا ثابت ہے وہ ہمیشہ موزونی ہی رہیں گی عرف اور رواج کی وجہ سے ان میں کوئی تبدیلی واقع نہ ہوگی۔
جن اشیاء میں نص وارد نہیں وہ عرف پر محمول ہیں
وما لم ينص عليه فهو محمول على عادات الناس لنها دالة

Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume eight. [...the entire passage translated literally...]
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It first demonstrates that textual evidence (nass) is superior to custom ('urf) by two arguments: (1) a custom may be based on falsehood, but nass has no room for falsehood; (2) custom is only binding on those who follow it, while nass is binding on all. Therefore, the Prophet's hadith regarding the measurement of items (by weight or volume) cannot be abandoned due to changing customs. Second, the passage states that for items not mentioned in the nass, the custom of the people (e.g., whether they sell by weight or volume) determines their legal classification. Imam al-Quduri's commentary confirms this, citing the hadith 'Whatever the Muslims consider good is good before Allah,' implying that custom in the absence of nass acts like consensus (ijma). The key takeaway is that nass is immutable; custom only operates in its absence.

Key Terms
نص (nass): Textual evidence from the Quran or authenticated Sunnah that explicitly states a ruling.
عرف ('urf): Common practice or custom of the people, especially in commercial transactions.
مکیلی/موزونی (makili/mawzuni): Measured by volume (kayl) or by weight (wazn), referring to the standard method of quantifying commodities for sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the hadith is a nass that applies universally and is not subject to change by custom.
C) Because wheat and gold are not subject to usury.
D) Because custom only applies to non-Islamic societies.

Key Takeaway
Nass is superior to custom and cannot be overridden; in the absence of nass, custom acts as a legal proof akin to consensus.

Can Custom Override Nass? Abu Yusuf vs. the Majority
Intra-Hanafi dispute on custom vs nass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Yusuf's argument that custom can override nass, state the majority Hanafi rebuttal, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a ribawi transaction.

Core Idea
Custom cannot override nass: the Prophet's silence elevated the original custom to immutable textual status.

In the Hanafi school, a classic dispute arises: when a clear text (nass) specifies a method of measurement (weight or volume) for ribawi items, can a later custom that changes the method override that text? Imam Abu Yusuf argued yes, because the nass itself was based on the custom of the Prophet's time. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) disagreed, holding that the Prophet's silence on that custom made it part of the nass, which is immutable. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Dispute
Identify the two positions: Abu Yusuf holds that custom can override nass; the majority holds that nass is immutable.
The nass is the hadith on measuring wheat by volume and gold by weight.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the Prophet's command was based on the custom of that time; when custom changes, the ruling changes accordingly.
He treats the custom as the effective cause (illah) of the ruling.
3
Analyze the Majority Response
The majority respond that the Prophet's silence after seeing the custom elevates it to the level of nass, and nass cannot be contradicted by subsequent custom.
This is a key usul point: the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) creates a binding precedent.
4
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: selling wheat by weight or gold by volume is valid according to Abu Yusuf if custom so dictates, but invalid according to the majority.
The majority consider any change in measure to create a suspicion of riba (shubhah riba).
5
Note the Salam Exception
Both sides agree that in a salam contract, exact equality is not required, so measuring by a different method is valid as long as the commodity is defined.
Salam is a forward sale based on need, and its rules differ from spot exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ہو نا منصوص ہے مگر عرف اس کے مکیلی ہونے پر جاری ہے تو اس کو مکیلی شار کیا جائیگا کیونکہ عہد رسالت میں مکیلی چیزوں میں کیل کرنے پر اور موزونی چیزوں میں وزن کرنے پر جو نص وارد ہوئی ہے وہ اس زمانہ کے دینے سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ وہ کیل کے ذریعہ بھی برابر ہو بلکہ کیل کے ذریعہ کی زیادتی کا شبہ باقی ہے کیونکہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ ایک جانب کا گندم کچھ گیلا ہو اور دوسری جانب کا سوکھا ہو پس ایک من گیلا گندم جس برتن میں سما سکتا ہے اس برتن میں ایک من سوکھا گندم نہیں سا سکتا بلکہ کچھ گندم باقی رہ جائے گا اسی طرح جس سونے کو کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کیا گیا ہے ضروری نہیں کہ وہ وزن کے ذریعہ بھی برابر ہو حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اصل معیار کے اعتبار سے زیادتی کا شبہ ہے اور اموال ربویہ میں زیادتی اور ربوا کا شبہ اسی طرح حرام ہے جس طرح حقیقت ربوا حرام ہے جیسا کہ گندم کا گندم کے عوض اور سونے کا سونے کے عوض اندازے سے بیچنا نا جائز ہے ہاں طرفین کے نزدیک اگر مکیلی چیز میں وزن کے اعتبار سے بیع سلم کی گئی تو جائز ہے۔ مثلا ایک شخص نے ایک ہزار رو پیدراس المال دس من گندم کے عوض ایک ماہ کے وعدہ پر مسلم الیہ کو دیا یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ مسلم الیہ کو پیشگی دید یا تا کہ مسلم الیہ ایک ماہ میں دس من گندم دیدے تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم میں مساوات اور برابری معتبر نہیں ہے بلکہ مسلم فیہ کا ایسے طور پر معلوم ہونا معتبر ہے جس سے تسلیم مسلم فیہ کے وقت جھگڑا پیدا نہ ہو اور گندم کے وزن کی مقدار بیان کر دینے سے مسلم فیہ یعنی گندم معلوم ہو جاتا ہے اس لیے گندم کی بیع سلم وزن کے اعتبار سے جائز اور درست ہے۔
It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that custom is considered even against the nass. [...] (full literal translation)
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage documents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that since the Prophet's hadith on measurements was based on the custom of his time, when that custom changes, the ruling should change accordingly. The majority (Sahibayn: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that the Prophet's silence after witnessing the custom elevated that custom to the status of nass, which is immutable. The practical difference (thamar al-ikhtilaf) is: if someone sells wheat for wheat by weight (instead of volume), Abu Yusuf holds it valid if that is the current custom, while the majority deem it invalid because the change in measure creates a suspicion of usurious excess (riba). The passage also clarifies that salam (advance payment) contracts are excepted from this stricture because they do not require exact equality.

Key Terms
ثمرة الاختلاف (thamarat al-ikhtilaf): The practical consequence of a scholarly disagreement; here, the ruling on a specific transaction.
ربا (riba): Usury or unlawful increase in exchange of ribawi items; the passage deals with the suspicion of riba when measure is changed.
بيغ سلم (bay' salam): Forward sale where price is paid in advance for a known commodity to be delivered later. Exception to the rule of hand-to-hand exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical difference between Imam Abu Yusuf's view and the majority view regarding selling wheat for wheat by weight?
A) Abu Yusuf says it is invalid; the majority says it is valid.
B) Abu Yusuf says it is valid if the custom is weight-based; the majority says it is invalid regardless of custom.
C) Both agree it is valid if done by volume.
D) Abu Yusuf says it is valid only if both parties agree; the majority says it is always invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, nass cannot be overridden by subsequent custom; only the original custom that the Prophet witnessed and affirmed is considered nass.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Items Sold by Ratl Are Weight-Based (Mawzun)
States a ruling that anything sold by ratl is weight-based and the invalidity of selling it by an unknown volume.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that items sold by ratl are weight-based and identify the consequence of selling them by an unknown volume.

Core Idea
Anything sold by ratl is weight-based; selling it by unknown volume invalidates the sale due to riba suspicion.

In Hanafi fiqh, commodities are classified as either weight-based (mawzun) or volume-based (makil). This classification determines the permissible methods of sale. The passage clarifies that any item sold by the ratl (a standard weight unit) is considered weight-based, and thus its quantity must be known by weight. Selling such items using a volume measure of unknown weight introduces uncertainty (gharar) and risks riba, rendering the sale invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Locate the core statement: 'Whatever is sold by ratl is weight-based.' This is the foundational ruling.
The ruling applies to the ratl and its subdivisions like ounces.
2
Understand the Reasoning (Talil)
The author explains that the ratl is determined by weight, so all items sold by ratl inherit that weight-based nature.
This is an explicit causal link.
3
Contrast with Other Measures
The passage distinguishes weight-based from volumetric measures (makail). Items sold by volume are not automatically weight-based.
This classification affects how exchange transactions are conducted.
4
Apply the Rule to a Transaction
If a weight-based item is sold using a volume measure whose weight is unknown, the sale is invalid.
Invalidity arises from the suspicion of excess in weight.
5
Identify the Prohibited Analogy
The passage compares this to a sale by estimation (mujazafah), which is prohibited in ribawi items.
Mujazafah involves uncertainty equivalent to riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جو چیز رطلاً بیچی جاتی ہو وہ وزنی ہے۔ قال وكل ما ينسب الى الرطل فهو وزنى معناه ما يباع بالاواقى لانها قدرت بطريق الوزن حتى يحتسب ما يباع بها وزنا بخلاف سائر المكائيل واذا كان موزونا فلو بيع بمكيال لا يعرف وزنه بمكيال مثله لا يجوز لتوهم الفضل فى الوزن بمنزلة المجازفة
Whatever is sold by ratl is weight-based. He said: And everything that is attributed to the ratl is weight-based. Meaning what is sold by ounces, because they are determined by way of weight, so what is sold by them is considered weight-based, unlike the other volumetric measures. And if it is weight-based, then if it is sold by a volumetric measure whose weight is not known by a similar volumetric measure, it is not permissible, due to the suspicion of excess in weight, similar to a sale by estimation (mujazafah).
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: any commodity sold by the ratl (a standard weight measure) is classified as mawzun (weight-based). The reasoning is that the ratl and its subdivisions (like ounces) are defined by weight. Therefore, transactions involving such items must be conducted by weight, not by volume. If someone tries to sell a weight-based item by a volume measure, and the weight of that volume is unknown, the sale is invalid because it creates a suspicion of riba (usurious excess), just like selling by estimation (mujazafah) which is prohibited in ribawi items.

Key Terms
رطل (ratl): A unit of weight (approximately 450 grams in later Hanafi use, but historically variable). Anything sold by ratl is considered mawzun.
مجازفة (mujazafah): A sale by guess or estimation without precise measurement, prohibited in ribawi exchanges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is selling a weight-based item by a volumetric measure of unknown weight invalid?
A) Because volumetric measures are always imprecise.
B) Because it creates a suspicion of usurious excess (riba) due to unknown weight equivalence.
C) Because the Prophet prohibited all volume sales.
D) Because it is only invalid if the seller is a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Items sold by ratl are weight-based; selling them by an unknown volume is invalid due to riba suspicion.

The Fixed Nature of Textual Classification: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf on Custom
Intra-Hanafi dispute on urf overriding textual designation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on the role of custom versus textual designation in classifying goods as makil or wazni, and explain why Abu Yusuf's view is not relied upon.

Core Idea
The Prophet's tacit approval (sukut) elevates a practice to nass; custom cannot override nass even if custom changes.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf on whether later custom can override the original classification of goods as measured or weighed. The majority holds that the Prophet's silence on the practice constitutes textual approval, making it binding. Understanding this dispute clarifies the priority of nass over 'urf in Hanafi methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Read the passage to understand what is being contested: whether the designation of goods as makil (measured) or wazni (weighed) is fixed by the Prophet's era or can change with custom.
2
State the majority view and its proof
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds that the original designation is fixed by nass. Their proof is the Prophet's silence (sukut) when he saw the people measuring wheat – this silence is considered textual approval.
Sukut as taqrir
3
State Abu Yusuf's view and his proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the original nass was based on the custom of that time. When custom changes, the ruling changes accordingly. Custom ('urf) is the operative basis.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator responds that nass cannot be changed by custom because custom cannot oppose nass. The Prophet's silence elevated the practice to the level of nass, which is immutable.
Custom is subordinate to nass
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is relied upon (mufta bihi). Abu Yusuf's view is not adopted; it is considered a nawadir (rare transmission).
Tarjih authority: Ashraf al-Hidaya

Source Text

کرنے پر اور موزونی چیزوں میں وزن کرنے پر جو نص وارد ہوئی ہے وہ اس زمانہ کے لوگوں کی عادت ہی کی وجہ سے ہے پس عادت ہی مقصود ہوئی پھر جب بعد میں چل کر عادت بدل گئی تو اس کے مطابق حکم ثابت ہوگا یعنی جب عہد رسالت میں گندم و غیرہ کی خرید وفروخت کیل کے ساتھ کی جاتی تھی تو ان کو کیلی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب لیکن ہماری طرف سے ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے زمانہ کے لوگوں کو گندم وغیرہ میں کیل کے ساتھ معاملہ کرتے دیکھا اور اس پر آپ نے سکوت فرمایا تو یہ سکوت فرمانا نص کے مرتبہ میں ہوا اور نص عرف اور رواج سے متغیر نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ عرف نص کے معارض نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ ثمره اختلاف طرفین اور امام ابو یوسف کے درمیان ثمرہ اختلاف اس مثال میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ ایک آدمی نے گندم کو گندم کے عوض فروخت کیا اور دونوں عوضوں میں وزن کے ساتھ برابری کی گئی یعنی لین دین پیمانہ اور کیل سے کیا گیا تو یہ صورت ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ عرف کے مطابق وزنی چیز کو وزن کے ذریعہ برابر کیا گیا اور کیلی چیز کو کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کیا گیا اور طرفین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ اگر چہ گندم اصلا کیلی ہے اور سونا اصلا وزنی ہے اور گندم کو وزن کے ذریعہ برابر کر دینے سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ وہ کیل کے ذریعہ بھی برابر ہو بلکہ کیل کے ذریعہ کی زیادتی کا شبہ باقی ہے کیونکہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ ایک جانب کا گندم کچھ گیلا ہو اور دوسری جانب کا سوکھا ہو پس ایک من گیلا گندم جس برتن میں سما سکتا ہے اس برتن میں ایک من سوکھا گندم نہیں سا سکتا بلکہ کچھ گندم باقی رہ جائے گا اسی طرح جس سونے کو کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کیا گیا ہے ضروری نہیں کہ وہ وزن کے ذریعہ بھی برابر ہو حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اصل معیار کے اعتبار سے زیادتی کا شبہ ہے اور اموال ربویہ میں زیادتی اور ربوا کا شبہ اسی طرح حرام ہے جس طرح حقیقت ربوا حرام ہے جیسا کہ گندم کا گندم کے عوض اور سونے کا سونے کے عوض اندازے سے بیچنا نا جائز ہے ہاں طرفین کے نزدیک اگر مکیلی چیز میں وزن کے اعتبار سے بیع سلم کی گئی تو جائز ہے۔ مثلا ایک شخص نے ایک ہزار رو پیدراس المال دس من گندم کے عوض ایک ماہ کے وعدہ پر مسلم الیہ کو دیا یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ مسلم الیہ کو پیشگی دید یا تا کہ مسلم الیہ ایک ماہ میں دس من گندم دیدے تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم میں مساوات اور برابری معتبر نہیں ہے بلکہ مسلم فیہ کا ایسے طور پر معلوم ہونا معتبر ہے جس سے تسلیم مسلم فیہ کے وقت جھگڑا پیدا نہ ہو اور گندم کے وزن کی مقدار بیان کر دینے سے مسلم فیہ یعنی گندم معلوم ہو جاتا ہے اس لیے گندم کی بیع سلم وزن کے اعتبار سے جائز اور درست ہے۔
Book of Sales. It will be counted as measured. And if they transact by weight, then that thing will be counted as weighed. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that custom is considered valid even contrary to the textual designation, meaning if a thing is textually designated as measured but custom is ongoing for its being weighed, then it will be considered weighed. And if a thing is textually designated as weighed but custom is ongoing for its being measured, then it will be considered measured, because the text that came in the era of the Messenger regarding measuring measured things and weighing weighed things was only due to the habit of the people of that time. So habit was the intended purpose. Then when later on the habit changed, the ruling will be established accordingly, i.e., when in the era of the Messenger the sale of wheat etc. was by measure, they will be considered measured. Our response: But our response to Abu Yusuf's proof is that when the Messenger (peace be upon him) saw the people of his time transacting in wheat etc. by measure and he remained silent on it, then this silence became of the rank of text (nass), and a text does not change with custom and usage, because custom cannot oppose a text. Practical consequence of the difference: The practical difference between the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf appears in this example: a man sold wheat for wheat, and equality was made by weight, i.e., the transaction was done by measure and capacity. Then this case is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, because according to custom, a weighed item was equalized by weight and a measured item was equalized by measure. And according to the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is impermissible, even though wheat is originally measured and gold is originally weighed, and equalizing wheat by weight does not necessitate that it is also equal by measure; rather, the suspicion of excess in measure remains, because it is very possible that the wheat on one side is somewhat moist and on the other side dry. Thus, the moist wheat that can fit in a vessel, dry wheat cannot fit in that vessel; rather, some wheat will remain. Similarly, gold that is equalized by measure is not necessarily equal by weight. The conclusion is that there is a suspicion of excess with respect to the original standard, and in ribawi goods, suspicion of excess and riba is as prohibited as actual riba, just as selling wheat for wheat and gold for gold by estimation is impermissible. However, according to the two parties, if a measured item is sold by weight as a salam sale, it is permissible. For example, a person gave one thousand rupees as capital to the muslam ilaih in exchange for ten maunds of wheat on a one-month promise, i.e., he paid one thousand rupees in advance to the muslam ilaih so that the muslam ilaih would give ten maunds of wheat in one month. This is permissible, because in salam sale equality is not considered; rather, it is sufficient that the muslam fih is known in a way that no dispute arises at the time of delivery, and specifying the weight of wheat makes the muslam fih (i.e., wheat) known. Therefore, salam sale of wheat by weight is permissible and correct.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the role of custom (urf) in determining whether goods are classified as measured (makil) or weighed (wazni). The majority position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the original textual designation from the Prophet's era (nass) is fixed and cannot be changed by later custom. Abu Yusuf, however, is reported to hold that custom can override even a textual designation if the custom has changed. The commentator presents Abu Yusuf's argument: the Prophet's ruling was based on the custom of that time, so if custom changes, the ruling changes. The response is that the Prophet's silence on the practice constitutes tacit approval, elevating it to the level of nass, which custom cannot abrogate. The practical difference (thamara) is illustrated: if wheat (originally measured) is sold for wheat by weight, Abu Yusuf deems it valid because custom weighs wheat, while the preferred position considers it invalid due to suspicion of excess in measure. An exception is made for salam sale, where equality is not required.

Key Terms
عرف ('urf): Custom or common practice of the people in a particular time and place regarding transactions.
نص (nass): An explicit textual ruling from the Quran or Sunnah, or in this context, the Prophet's tacit approval (sukut) which is given the status of nass.
مکیلی (makili): Goods that are measured by volume (e.g., wheat, barley) as per the original practice.
وزنی (wazni): Goods that are weighed (e.g., gold, silver) as per the original practice.
ثمرہ اختلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement; the difference in ruling that results from the different positions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position, if wheat (originally measured) is sold for wheat by weight in a spot exchange, what is the ruling?
A) Valid, because custom now weighs wheat.
B) Invalid, because the original classification as measured cannot be changed by custom, leading to suspicion of riba.
C) Valid only if both parties agree to use weight.
D) Invalid only if the weight is not equal.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the original textual classification of goods as measured or weighed is fixed and cannot be changed by later custom; only the Prophet's nass is authoritative.

Practical Consequence: Selling Wheat by Weight and the Salam Exception
Practical consequence and exception for salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the thamarah al-khilaf of the custom dispute to a concrete example and distinguish the rule for salam sale.

Core Idea
Spot exchange of wheat by weight is invalid due to riba suspicion; but salam sale by weight is valid because equality is not required.

This lesson focuses on the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute between the majority and Abu Yusuf regarding the classification of goods. We examine when selling wheat by weight is invalid in a spot exchange but valid in a salam contract. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper application in trade.

Guided Path
1
Recall the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference arises in a spot exchange of wheat for wheat: if both are weighed, Abu Yusuf says valid, majority says invalid.
2
Understand the reasoning for invalidity
Even if weights are equal, there is a potential difference in volume due to moisture, etc., leading to suspicion of excess (shubhat al-fadl) in a ribawi item.
Suspicion is treated like actual riba
3
Identify the salam exception
In a salam sale (advance payment for future delivery), equality is not a condition. Therefore, wheat can be sold by weight in salam.
Salam is a forward contract with different rules
4
Apply to a new example
Given a scenario, determine whether the transaction is a spot exchange or salam, and then apply the correct ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع
کیلی شمار ہوگی ۔ اور اگر وزن کے ذریعہ معاملہ کرتے ہیں تو وہ چیز وزنی شمار ہوگی۔ امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ منصوص علیہ کے خلاف بھی عرف معتبر ہوتا ہے یعنی اگر کسی چیز کا مکیلی ہونا منصوص ہے مگر عرف اس کے وزنی ہونے پر جاری ہے تو اس کو وزنی شمار کیا جائے گا اور اگر کسی چیز کا وزنی ہو نا منصوص ہے مگر عرف اس کے مکیلی ہونے پر جاری ہے تو اس کو مکیلی شار کیا جائیگا کیونکہ عہد رسالت میں مکیلی چیزوں میں کیل کرنے پر اور موزونی چیزوں میں وزن کرنے پر جو نص وارد ہوئی ہے وہ اس زمانہ کے لوگوں کی عادت ہی کی وجہ سے ہے پس عادت ہی مقصود ہوئی پھر جب بعد میں چل کر عادت بدل گئی تو اس کے مطابق حکم ثابت ہوگا یعنی جب عہد رسالت میں گندم و غیرہ کی خرید وفروخت کیل کے ساتھ کی جاتی تھی تو ان کو کیلی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب لیکن ہماری طرف سے ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے زمانہ کے لوگوں کو گندم وغیرہ میں کیل کے ساتھ معاملہ کرتے دیکھا اور اس پر آپ نے سکوت فرمایا تو یہ سکوت فرمانا نص کے مرتبہ میں ہوا اور نص عرف اور رواج سے متغیر نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ عرف نص کے معارض نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ ثمره اختلاف طرفین اور امام ابو یوسف کے درمیان ثمرہ اختلاف اس مثال میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ ایک آدمی نے گندم کو گندم کے عوض فروخت کیا اور دونوں عوضوں میں وزن کے ساتھ برابری کی گئی یعنی لین دین پیمانہ اور کیل سے کیا گیا تو یہ صورت ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ عرف کے مطابق وزنی چیز کو وزن کے ذریعہ برابر کیا گیا اور کیلی چیز کو کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کیا گیا اور طرفین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ اگر چہ گندم اصلا کیلی ہے اور سونا اصلا وزنی ہے اور گندم کو وزن کے ذریعہ برابر کر دینے سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ وہ کیل کے ذریعہ بھی برابر ہو بلکہ کیل کے ذریعہ کی زیادتی کا شبہ باقی ہے کیونکہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ ایک جانب کا گندم کچھ گیلا ہو اور دوسری جانب کا سوکھا ہو پس ایک من گیلا گندم جس برتن میں سما سکتا ہے اس برتن میں ایک من سوکھا گندم نہیں سا سکتا بلکہ کچھ گندم باقی رہ جائے گا اسی طرح جس سونے کو کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کیا گیا ہے ضروری نہیں کہ وہ وزن کے ذریعہ بھی برابر ہو حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اصل معیار کے اعتبار سے زیادتی کا شبہ ہے اور اموال ربویہ میں زیادتی اور ربوا کا شبہ اسی طرح حرام ہے جس طرح حقیقت ربوا حرام ہے جیسا کہ گندم کا گندم کے عوض اور سونے کا سونے کے عوض اندازے سے بیچنا نا جائز ہے ہاں طرفین کے نزدیک اگر مکیلی چیز میں وزن کے اعتبار سے بیع سلم کی گئی تو جائز ہے۔ مثلا ایک شخص نے ایک ہزار رو پیدراس المال دس من گندم کے عوض ایک ماہ کے وعدہ پر مسلم الیہ کو دیا یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ مسلم الیہ کو پیشگی دید یا تا کہ مسلم الیہ ایک ماہ میں دس من گندم دیدے تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم میں مساوات اور برابری معتبر نہیں ہے بلکہ مسلم فیہ کا ایسے طور پر معلوم ہونا معتبر ہے جس سے تسلیم مسلم فیہ کے وقت جھگڑا پیدا نہ ہو اور گندم کے وزن کی مقدار بیان کر دینے سے مسلم فیہ یعنی گندم معلوم ہو جاتا ہے اس لیے گندم کی بیع سلم وزن کے اعتبار سے جائز اور درست ہے۔
Book of Sales. It will be counted as measured. And if they transact by weight, then that thing will be counted as weighed. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that custom is considered valid even contrary to the textual designation, meaning if a thing is textually designated as measured but custom is ongoing for its being weighed, then it will be considered weighed. And if a thing is textually designated as weighed but custom is ongoing for its being measured, then it will be considered measured, because the text that came in the era of the Messenger regarding measuring measured things and weighing weighed things was only due to the habit of the people of that time. So habit was the intended purpose. Then when later on the habit changed, the ruling will be established accordingly, i.e., when in the era of the Messenger the sale of wheat etc. was by measure, they will be considered measured. Our response: But our response to Abu Yusuf's proof is that when the Messenger (peace be upon him) saw the people of his time transacting in wheat etc. by measure and he remained silent on it, then this silence became of the rank of text (nass), and a text does not change with custom and usage, because custom cannot oppose a text. Practical consequence of the difference: The practical difference between the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf appears in this example: a man sold wheat for wheat, and equality was made by weight, i.e., the transaction was done by measure and capacity. Then this case is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, because according to custom, a weighed item was equalized by weight and a measured item was equalized by measure. And according to the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) it is impermissible, even though wheat is originally measured and gold is originally weighed, and equalizing wheat by weight does not necessitate that it is also equal by measure; rather, the suspicion of excess in measure remains, because it is very possible that the wheat on one side is somewhat moist and on the other side dry. Thus, the moist wheat that can fit in a vessel, dry wheat cannot fit in that vessel; rather, some wheat will remain. Similarly, gold that is equalized by measure is not necessarily equal by weight. The conclusion is that there is a suspicion of excess with respect to the original standard, and in ribawi goods, suspicion of excess and riba is as prohibited as actual riba, just as selling wheat for wheat and gold for gold by estimation is impermissible. However, according to the two parties, if a measured item is sold by weight as a salam sale, it is permissible. For example, a person gave one thousand rupees as capital to the muslam ilaih in exchange for ten maunds of wheat on a one-month promise, i.e., he paid one thousand rupees in advance to the muslam ilaih so that the muslam ilaih would give ten maunds of wheat in one month. This is permissible, because in salam sale equality is not considered; rather, it is sufficient that the muslam fih is known in a way that no dispute arises at the time of delivery, and specifying the weight of wheat makes the muslam fih (i.e., wheat) known. Therefore, salam sale of wheat by weight is permissible and correct.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the role of custom (urf) in determining whether goods are classified as measured (makil) or weighed (wazni). The majority position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the original textual designation from the Prophet's era (nass) is fixed and cannot be changed by later custom. Abu Yusuf, however, is reported to hold that custom can override even a textual designation if the custom has changed. The commentator presents Abu Yusuf's argument: the Prophet's ruling was based on the custom of that time, so if custom changes, the ruling changes. The response is that the Prophet's silence on the practice constitutes tacit approval, elevating it to the level of nass, which custom cannot abrogate. The practical difference (thamara) is illustrated: if wheat (originally measured) is sold for wheat by weight, Abu Yusuf deems it valid because custom weighs wheat, while the preferred position considers it invalid due to suspicion of excess in measure. An exception is made for salam sale, where equality is not required.

Key Terms
ثمرہ اختلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement; here, the difference in validity of selling wheat by weight in a spot exchange.
بیع سلم (bay' salam): A forward sale where the buyer pays in advance for goods to be delivered later; also called salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which statement accurately reflects the Hanafi majority's ruling on selling wheat by weight?
A) It is always invalid because wheat must be measured.
B) It is invalid in a spot exchange but valid in a salam contract.
C) It is valid if the custom of the time is to weigh wheat.
D) It is invalid only if the weights are unequal.

Key Takeaway
Spot exchange of wheat by weight is invalid due to riba suspicion, but salam sale by weight is valid because equality is not a condition in forward contracts.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Definition of Weighed Goods and Ruling on Sale by Unknown Measure
Defining weighed goods and invalidating sale by unknown measure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of weighed goods (mawzun) and apply the ruling that selling a weighed item by a measure of unknown weight is invalid.

Core Idea
Items sold by ratl or uqiya are legally weighed — the container is just a proxy for weight.

This passage establishes a key principle in Hanafi sales law: the classification of goods as weighed (mawzun) or measured (makil) affects the validity of exchange. The matn declares that anything sold by ratl is considered weighed. The commentary clarifies that ratl and uqiya, though containers, were originally defined by weight. Therefore, selling such goods by an unknown measure raises the suspicion of riba and is prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal classification
Recognize that the text defines goods sold by ratl or uqiya as weighed (mawzun) rather than measured (makil). Note the basis: the standard was weight.
2
Understand the ruling
When such a weighed item is sold by a measure of unknown weight in exchange for a like measure, it is invalid due to the suspicion of excess.
The prohibition applies to ribawi goods.
3
Distinguish from measured goods
Measured goods (like wheat by qafiz) are sold by volume; weight is not considered. The container itself is the standard.
4
Apply the underlying principle
Equality in weighed goods must be by weight, not by guess or unknown measure. Any uncertainty leads to suspicion of riba.

جو چیز رطلاً بیچی جاتی ہو وہ وزنی ہے
قال وكل ما ينسب الى الرطل قهو وزنى معناه ما يباع بالاواقى لانها قدرت بطريق الوزن حتى يحتسب ما يباع بها وزنا بخلاف سائر المكائيل واذا كان موزونا فلو بيع بمكيال لا يعرف وزنه بمكيال مثله لا يجوز لتوهم الفضل فى الوزن بمنزلة المجازفة

ترجمہ اور ہر وہ چیز جور ٹل کی طرف منسوب کی جاتی ہو وہ وزنی ہے اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جو چیز اوقیہ سے بیچی جاتی ہے وہ وزنی ہے کیونکہ اس کا اندازہ بطریق وزن کیا گیا ہے حتى کہ جو چیز اوقیہ سے بیچی جاتی ہے وہ وزنی شمار ہوتی ہے برخلاف دوسری کیلی چیزوں کے اور جب کوئی چیز وزنی ہو پھر اس کو کسی پیمانہ سے بیچا گیا جس کا وزن معلوم نہیں ہے اس کے مثل پیمانہ کے عوض تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ وزن میں زیادتی کا شبہ ہے جیسا کہ اندازہ سے ( بیچنے کی صورت میں زیادتی کا شبہ ) ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح رطل، را کے فتحہ اور کسرہ دونوں کے ساتھ پڑھا جاتا ہے رطل بذات خود تو ایک ظرف اور برتن ہے اسی طرح اوقیہ بذات خود تو ظرف اور برتن ہے مگر ان کے ساتھ جن چیزوں کی خرید و فروخت ہوتی ہے وہ چیزیں وزنی شمار ہوتی ہیں جیسے ہمارے زمانہ میں دودھ کی خرید و فروخت ظروف سے ناپ کر ہوتی ہے لیکن مراد و زن ہوتا ہے مثلاً اگر کسی نے ایک لیٹر دودھ لیا بائع نے ایک لیٹر دودھ ناپ کر مشتری کو دیدیا تو اس سے ایک کلو دودھ مراد ہوتا ہے اس طرح تیل وغیرہ کی خرید وفروخت اگر چہ ظروف اور برتنوں سے ناپ کر ہوتی ہے مگر مراد وزن ہی ہوتا ہے رطل شہروں اور زمانوں کے اختلاف سے مختلف ہوتا رہتا ہے چنانچہ علامہ ابن الہام کے زمانہ میں اسکندریہ کا رطل وزن سبعہ کے اعتبار سے تین سو بارہ درہم کے وزن کے برابر ہوتا تھا۔ اور مصر میں ایک سو چوالیس درہم کے وزن کے برابر ہوتا تھا اور شام میں اس سے چار گونہ زیادہ ہوتا تھا اور حلب میں اس سے بھی زیادہ کا ہوتا تھا اور عراق میں ایک سو اٹھائیس درہم کے وزن کے برابر ہوتا تھا۔ یہی ابو عبیدہ کی بیان کردہ تفسیر ہے اور فقہاء بھی اسی عراقی رطل کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں اوقی اوقیہ کی جمع ہے ایک اوقیہ چالیس درہم کے وزن کے برابر ہوتا ہے اب مسئلہ کا حاصل یہ ہوا کہ اگر کوئی سیال چیز تیل، دودھ وغیرہ رطل یا اواقی کے ذریعہ فروخت کیا گیا یا خریدا گیا تو اس سے وزن مراد ہوتا ہے کوئی پیمانہ مراد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ رطل اور اواقی کا اندازہ وزن کے اعتبار سے کیا گیا ہے حتی کہ اگر کوئی چیز طل یا اواقی کے ذریعہ بیچی جائے تو وہ وزن پر شمار ہوتی ہے یعنی اس سے وزن مراد ہوتا ہے جیسے آج کل اگر کوئی کہے کہ میں پانچ لیٹر دودھ خرید کر لایا ہوں تو اس سے مراد پانچ کلو دودھ ہوتا ہے برخلاف کیلی چیزوں کے کہ کیلی چیزوں میں کیل معتبر ہوتا ہے وزن معتبر نہیں ہوتا مثلا اگر کوئی کہے کہ میں دس قفیز گندم خرید کر لایا ہوں تو اس سے برتن لے کر جس کا وزن معلوم نہیں یہ کہا کہ میں سونے سے یہ برتن بھر کر اسی کے مثل سونے کے عوض بیچتا ہوں تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ موزونی چیز اگر پیمانہ کے ذریعہ برابر کی گئی تو کسی ایک عوض میں زیادتی کا شبہ ہے جیسے انکل اور اندازے سے برابری کرنے کی صورت میں کسی ایک جانب میں زیادتی کا شبہ ہوتا ہے اور اموال ربویہ میں چونکہ فضل اور زیادتی کا شبہ اس طرح ناجائز ہے جس طرح فضل اور زیادتی نا جائز ہے اس لیے موزونی چیز کو ایسے پیمانہ اور طرف سے جس کا وزن معلوم نہ ہواس جیسے پیمانہ کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
Whatever is sold by ratl is weighed. He said: And everything that is attributed to the ratl, then it is weighed. Its meaning is that which is sold by uqiyas, because they were determined by way of weight, so that what is sold by them is considered weighed, unlike other measured things. And if it is weighed, then if it is sold by a measure whose weight is not known, in exchange for a like measure, it is not permissible due to the suspicion of excess in weight, like the case of estimation. Translation: And every thing that is attributed to the ratl is weighed. Its meaning is that a thing sold by uqiya is weighed because its estimation was made by way of weight, so that a thing sold by uqiya is considered weighed, contrary to other measured things. And when a thing is weighed, then if it is sold by a measure whose weight is not known, in exchange for a like measure, it is not permissible because of the suspicion of excess in weight, as in the case of estimation there is suspicion of excess. Explanation: Ratl is pronounced with both fatha and kasra on the ra. Ratl itself is a container, similarly uqiya itself is a container, but the things that are bought and sold with them are considered weighed. Like in our time, milk is bought and sold by measuring with containers, but the intention is weight. For example, if someone took one liter of milk, the seller measured one liter and gave it to the buyer, then one kilogram of milk is intended. Similarly, oil etc., even if bought and sold by measuring with containers, the intention is weight. Ratl varies according to differences in cities and times. So according to Allamah Ibn al-Humam, the Alexandrian ratl in his time, by the weight of sab'ah, equaled three hundred and twelve dirhams in weight. In Egypt it equaled one hundred and forty-four dirhams, in Syria it was four times that, in Aleppo even more, and in Iraq it equaled one hundred and twenty-eight dirhams. This is the interpretation reported by Abu Ubayda, and the jurists also consider this Iraqi ratl. Uqiya is the plural of uqiya; one uqiya equals forty dirhams in weight. Now the conclusion of the issue is that if a liquid thing like oil, milk etc. is sold or bought by ratl or uqiyas, then weight is intended, not measure, because ratl and uqiyas were estimated by weight. So even if a thing is sold by ratl or uqiya, it is considered by weight, i.e., weight is intended. Like nowadays if someone says 'I brought five liters of milk', five kilograms of milk is intended. Contrary to measured things, where measure is considered, weight is not. For example, if someone says 'I brought ten qafiz of wheat', then the container that measures the wheat is intended, not weight. And if a weighed thing, for example gold, is sold by measuring with a vessel whose weight is unknown, in exchange for a like vessel, for example someone takes a vessel whose weight is unknown, says 'I sell this vessel filled with gold in exchange for a like vessel of gold', then it is not permissible because if a weighed thing is equalized by measure, there is suspicion of excess in one of the countervalues, like in the case of equalization by estimation and guesswork there is suspicion of excess in one side. And since in ribawi goods, suspicion of excess is prohibited just as actual excess is prohibited, therefore selling a weighed thing by such a measure whose weight is unknown, in exchange for a like measure, is not permissible.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling. The matn states: 'كل ما ينسب الى الرطل فهو وزني' — everything attributed to the ratl is weighed. The commentary explains that ratl and uqiya are containers, but the standard by which they were determined is weight. Therefore, items sold by these containers are considered weighed (mawzun) rather than measured (makil). The ruling: if such a weighed item is sold by a measure (mikyāl) whose weight is unknown, in exchange for a like measure, it is invalid because of the suspicion of excess in weight, which is akin to juzāfa (sale by guess). The commentator elaborates on the varying weights of the ratl in different regions, noting that the Iraqi ratl (128 dirhams) is the one relied upon by Hanafi jurists. The practical implication is that liquids like milk and oil, even when sold by volume using standardized containers, are legally considered weighed. Therefore, exchanging them by a measure of unknown weight raises the suspicion of riba and is prohibited.

Key Terms
رطل (ratl): A container used for measuring, but legally considered a weight standard (e.g., Iraqi ratl = 128 dirhams).
اوقیہ (uqiya): A weight unit (40 dirhams) used for selling goods; also a container, but legally a weight standard.
موزون (mawzun): Goods that are legally considered weighed, even if sold by volume, when the standard is weight.
مکیال (mikyāl): A measure for volume; here, a vessel used for measuring but whose weight equivalence is unknown.
مجازفہ (mujāzafah): Sale by guesswork or estimation without precise measurement or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Bay' al-Sarf: Requirement of Hand-to-Hand Exchange in the Same Sitting
Stating the definition of sale of currency and the requirement of immediate possession of both items in the same sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for a valid sarf contract and identify the hadith proof that establishes immediate possession in the same sitting.

Core Idea
In currency exchange, both countervalues must change hands in the same sitting.

When you exchange gold for silver or modern currencies, you cannot promise to deliver later. The Hanafi school insists that both parties must physically hand over the exchanged items before leaving the meeting place. This lesson explains why, citing the Prophet's command: 'Silver for silver, hand to hand.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of sarf
Locate the definition: sarf is a sale involving items that are by nature prices (thaman), such as gold and silver coins.
Modern paper currency is treated analogously.
2
Extract the condition
The phrase 'يعتبر فيه قبض عوضيه فى المجلس'—possession of both countervalues in the sitting is a condition (shart) for validity.
If possession is delayed, the contract becomes fasid.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The base text cites 'الفضة بالفضة هاء وهاء' meaning 'take and give' or 'hand to hand'. This indicates immediate physical exchange.
The hadith is transmitted in Muslim and al-Bukhari with the wording 'hand to hand'.
4
Understand the legal consequence
Without immediate qabd in the majlis, the contract is invalid (fasid). The ruling prevents riba al-nasi'ah (interest due to delay).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عقد صرف میں عوضین پر قبضہ ضروری ہے
قال وعقد الصرف ما وقع على جنس الاثمان يعتبر فيه قبض عوضيه فى المجلس لقوله عليه السلام الفضة بالفضة هاء وهاء معناه يدا بيد وسنبين الفقه في الصرف ان شاء الله تعالى
ترجمہ اور بیع صرف وہ ہے جو ہا ہم ثمنین کی جنس پر واقع ہو جس میں مجلس کے اندر اس کے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا معتبر ہے کیونکہ
In the contract of sarf, possession of both countervalues is necessary. He said: And the contract of sarf is that which occurs on the genus of prices (thaman); in it, possession of both its countervalues in the sitting is considered, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Silver for silver, take and give' meaning hand to hand. And we will explain the fiqh of sarf, God willing. Translation: And the sale of sarf is that which occurs on the genus of the two prices (thamanayn); in it, possession of both its countervalues in the sitting is considered, because of the Prophet's saying: 'Silver for silver, take and give' meaning hand to hand.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage introduces the ruling on bay' al-sarf (currency exchange). The matn defines sarf as a sale involving items that are prices (thaman) by nature, i.e., gold and silver (or their modern equivalents). The key condition is that both countervalues must be taken possession of (qabd) in the same sitting (majlis) before the parties separate. The proof is the Prophet's hadith: 'Silver for silver, take and give (hā'a wa hā'a), meaning hand to hand'. The commentary promises further explanation. This ruling is based on the principle that in ribawi items, delay in possession leads to riba al-nasi'ah.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): A sale of gold for gold, silver for silver, or gold for silver, i.e., exchange of currencies or precious metals.
ثمنین (thamanayn): The two countervalues in a sarf contract; typical examples are gold and silver coins.
قبض (qabd): Physical or constructive possession; here, immediate taking of the exchanged items.
مجلس (majlis): The sitting or session of the contract; the place where the parties negotiate and conclude the deal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for a valid sarf transaction according to the Hanafi school?
A) The exchange rate is fixed in advance.
B) Both countervalues are handed over in the same sitting.
C) The transaction is witnessed by two Muslims.
D) One of the countervalues is gold.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a sarf (currency exchange) contract is valid only if both countervalues are possessed immediately in the same sitting, as commanded by the Prophet.

Selling Weight-Based Items by Unknown Measure
Defining weight-based items and ruling on selling by unknown measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling weight-based items by an unknown-weight measure and explain why it is impermissible.

Core Idea
Selling weight-based items by unknown measures is haram due to riba risk.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah clarifies a key principle in Hanafi sales law: items sold by vessels like ratal or awqiya are considered by weight, not volume. This distinction matters when exchanging ribawi items, where exact equality is required. The ruling warns against using unknown-weight measures, as they create suspicion of inequality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Determine what is being ruled upon: selling a weight-based item (mawzun) using a measure whose weight is unknown, in exchange for the like of that measure.
The item is mawzun because it is sold by ratal or awqiya.
2
State the ruling and its evidence
The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram). The evidence is the suspicion of riba (excess) due to unknown equality, similar to selling by estimation.
Hanafi usul: suspicion of riba is treated like actual riba.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Items sold by ratal/awqiya are weight-based, not volume-based. Therefore, exchange requires knowledge of weight to ensure equality.
Contrast with makyulat (volume-based items) where volume is the basis.
4
Apply to examples
Milk, oil, gold: if sold by a vessel of unknown weight for the same vessel, it is impermissible. One must know the weight of the vessel or sell by known weight units.
Modern example: selling 1 liter of milk by a container of unknown weight for the same container.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
