Selling One Date for Two: Riba in Countable Food Items
Inter-madhhab dispute on riba in countable food items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on exchanging similar countable food items with excess and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, excess in same-genre food items is permissible only when standardized measure is absent.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on riba al-fadl. The Hanafi school allows selling one date for two dates, as long as the transaction is spot, because the effective cause of riba (standardized measure) is missing. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that any foodstuff requires equality. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of both schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed transactions
The passage discusses exchanging one egg for two eggs, one date for two dates, and one walnut for two walnuts. Recognize that these are all food items of the same genus, sold with excess in quantity.
These are classic examples of riba al-fadl disputes.
2
State the Hanafi position and its condition
The Hanafi position: such transactions are permissible if they are spot (hand-to-hand), but not on credit. Note the condition: immediate exchange (qabd) is required due to unity of genus.
Credit (nasi'ah) is prohibited even when excess is allowed.
3
Extract the Hanafi illa (effective cause)
The Hanafi illa for riba al-fadl is 'qadr ma'a al-jins' (standardized measure along with genus). Since eggs and walnuts are countable (adadi) and dates less than half a sa' are not measured, the illa is absent.
Qadr refers to standardized weight or capacity recognized by Shari'ah.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the illa is 'tu'm' (being a foodstuff). Since these items are food, equality of quantity is required; excess triggers riba.
Thus Shafi'is forbid such exchanges altogether, even spot.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow such exchanges with excess (spot), Shafi'is do not. Also, Hanafis prohibit credit in same-genus exchanges, which is consistent with both schools.
Unity of genus alone prohibits nasi'ah in Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور ایک انڈے کو دو انڈوں کے عوض اور ایک چھوہارے کو دو چھوہاروں کے عوض اور ایک اخروٹ کو دو اخروٹ کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے کیونکہ قدر معدوم ہے اس لیے ربوا متحقق نہ ہوگا اور اس حکم میں امام شافعی ہمارے مخالف ہیں کیونکہ طعم موجود ہے جیسا کہ گذر چکا ہے۔ تشریح ہمارے نزدیک ایک انڈا دوانڈوں کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے لیکن ادھار جائز نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک مطعومات میں ربا کی علت طعم ہے اور مذکورہ چیزوں میں طعم موجود ہے۔ اس لیے عوضین کے درمیان برابری کرنا ضروری ہے اور مذکورہ چیزوں میں چونکہ برابری نہیں پائی گئی ہے اس لیے ربو متحقق ہوگا اور بیچ نا جائز ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ربوا کی علت قدر مع الجنس ہے۔ اور مذکورہ چیزوں میں قدر مع الجنس موجود نہیں ہے کیونکہ انڈا اور اخروٹ تو عددی ہیں اور کھجور اگر چہ کیلی ہے لیکن نصف صاع سے کم شریعت میں کوئی پیمانہ نہیں ہے اس لئے ایک دو کھجور کیلی ہونے سے خارج ہو جائیں گی۔ پس جب مذکورہ چیز میں قدری نہیں ہیں یعنی نہ کیلی ہیں اور نہ وزنی ہیں تو ان میں فضل اور زیادتی جائز ہوگی مگر چونکہ اتحاد جنس موجود ہے اس لیے نساء یعنی ایک عوض کا ادھار ہونا حرام ہوگا۔
Translation: And selling one egg for two eggs, and one date for two dates, and one walnut for two walnuts is permissible because measure (qadr) is absent, so riba does not materialize. In this ruling, Imam al-Shafi'i opposes us because the effective cause (ta'm) is present, as has passed. Explanation: In our view, selling one egg for two eggs is permissible, but on credit it is not permissible. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is impermissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that in his view the effective cause of riba in foodstuffs is being a foodstuff (ta'm), and these items have ta'm. Therefore equality between the two countervalues is necessary, and since equality is not found in these items, riba has materialized and the sale is impermissible. Our proof is that the effective cause of riba is measure along with genus (qadr ma'a al-jins). And in these items, measure with genus is absent because eggs and walnuts are countable (adadi), and dates, although they are measured by capacity (kayl), less than half a sa' has no recognized measure in Shari'ah, so one or two dates are excluded from being measured. Therefore, when these items are not measured — neither by capacity nor by weight — excess (fadl) and increase are permissible in them. However, since unity of genus exists, nasi'ah — i.e., one countervalue being on credit — is prohibited.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding riba in the exchange of similar food items that are not standardized by weight or capacity. The author (Sharh al-Hidayah) states the Hanafi position: selling one egg for two eggs, one date for two dates, or one walnut for two walnuts is permissible in hand-to-hand transactions because the effective cause (illa) of riba according to the Hanafis is measure along with genus (qadr ma'a al-jins). These items are either countable (eggs, walnuts) or, in the case of dates, less than half a sa' (the minimum standard measure recognized by Shari'ah), so the condition of measuredness is absent. Thus, riba al-fadl (excess) is not triggered. However, because the genus is the same, riba al-nasi'ah (credit) is prohibited; therefore, the sale must be spot (hand-to-hand). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the effective cause is being a foodstuff (tu'm), so any food item, regardless of measurability, triggers riba al-fadl; thus equality of quantity is required. The Hanafi response focuses on the absence of standardized measure, which is the key differentiator. The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute, and the author explains the reasoning of both sides, then concludes with the Hanafi position that excess is permissible but credit is not.

Key Terms
قدر (qadr): Standardized measure, either by weight or capacity, recognized by Shari'ah.
طعم (tu'm): Being a foodstuff; the effective cause of riba according to al-Shafi'i.
نسیئت (nasi'ah): Deferred payment (credit) in a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is selling one date for two dates permissible?
A) Because dates are not considered food.
B) Because the effective cause of riba is measure (qadr) along with genus, and one or two dates are not measured by standard measure.
C) Because the date is a countable item.
D) Because Imam Shafi'i also allows it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the condition for riba al-fadl is standardized measure (qadr) along with genus; without it, excess in same-genus food is permissible but credit remains prohibited.

Selling One Fils for Two Fils: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Thamaniyya
Dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Two Shaikhs on selling specific fils with excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on selling one specified fils for two specified fils, and explain the reasoning based on thamaniyya.

Core Idea
Fulus are money by convention but can become commodities by mutual agreement of the parties.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is it permissible to sell one specific copper coin (fils) for two specific coins of the same type with an excess? The disagreement hinges on whether the monetary status (thamaniyya) of fulus can be nullified by the contracting parties. By the end, you will be able to articulate both sides and understand the underlying usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
First, identify that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Two Shaikhs) permit the sale of one specified fils for two specified fils, while Imam Muhammad forbids it.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, not a dispute with an outside school.
2
Identify the point of contention
The core issue is whether the thamaniyya (money status) of fulus can be nullified by the mutual agreement of the two parties. Imam Muhammad says no; the Two Shaikhs say yes.
Thamaniyya for fulus is by convention (istilah), not by creation (khilqa) like gold and silver.
3
Follow Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad argues that thamaniyya is established by universal convention (istilah al-kull), so individuals cannot cancel it. Therefore, fulus remain non-specific thaman, and selling one for two is riba.
This is analogous to selling one dirham for two dirhams, which is clearly riba.
4
Analyze the Two Shaikhs' response
The Two Shaikhs contend that thamaniyya in respect of the contracting parties is established by their own convention, so they can nullify it. Once nullified, the fulus become specific commodities (like walnuts) and the sale is valid.
They distinguish from dirhams and from unspecified fulus using different analogies.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Two Shaikhs. The practical difference: in transactions between two parties who agree to treat fulus as commodities, such exchanges are valid; otherwise, the general rule against riba applies.
Imam al-Shafi'i has two views, one agreeing with each side.

اور ربوا حرام ہے اسلئے یہ بیچ نا جائز اور فاسد ہوگی۔ دوسری صورت میں اسلئے ناجائز ہے کہ جس جانب میں ایک پیسہ معین ہے وہ اس پیسہ کو اپنے ساتھی کے سپر د کر دے گا اور اس کا ساتھی بعینہ وہ پیسہ ایک دوسرے پیسے کے ساتھ ملا کر اس کے سپرد کر دے گا، پس جس نے ایک معین پیسہ دیا تھا اس کی طرف بعینہ اس کا مال لوٹ آیا اور دوسرا پیسہ بلاعوض حاصل ہوگا اور عقد میں بلاعوض مال کا حاصل ہونا بشرطیکہ مشروط بھی ہو یہی لہوا ہے اور ملوانا جائز ہے اس لئے بیع کی یہ صورت بھی ناجائز ہوگی۔ تیسری صورت اس لئے نا جائز ہے کہ جب ایک شخص نے ایک غیر معین پیسہ ہو معین پیسوں کے عوض بیچا ۔ اور دو معین چیسوں پر کر لیا تو اس کے ذمہ میں جو ایک پیسہ واجب ہوا ہے یہ اس کی جگہ مقبوضہ دو پیسوں میں سے ایک پیسہ اپنے ساتھی کو دیدیا اور اس پاس پیسہ بلاعوض باقی رہا۔ اور بلا عوض باقی رہناہی ابواء ہے اس لئے یہ صورت بھی نا جائز ہوگی۔ چوٹھی صورت میں امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فلوس کا شمن ہونا تمام لوگوں کے اتفاق سے ثابت ہوا ہے اور جو چیز تمام لوگوں کے اتفاق سے ثابت ہوئی ہو وہ صرف بائع اور مشتری کے باطل کرنے سے باطل نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ بائع اور مشتری کو اپنے علاوہ پر ولایت حاصل نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس جب بائع اور مشتری کے باطل کرنے سے فلوس کا شمن ہونا باطل نہیں ہوا تو ان کی شمنیت باقی رہی اور جب فلوس کاشمن ہونا باقی ہے تو وہ متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوں گے ۔ اور جب فلوس متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوئے تو ان کی بیچ ایسی ہو گئی جیسا کہ دونوں عوض غیر معین ہوں۔ اور سابق میں گزر چکا کہ دونوں عوض یعنی دونوں جانب کے فلوس اگر غیر معین ہوں تو بیع نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ پس اسی
(Arabic matn:) He said: The sale of one fils for two fils, both specific (mu'ayyan), is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: It is not permissible, because the status of being thaman (money) is established by the consensus of all people, so it cannot be invalidated by the consensus of two parties. If it remains thaman, they do not become specific, so it is as if they were unspecified (bi-ghayr a'yani-hima), and like selling one dirham for two dirhams. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) [argue] that the status of being thaman in respect of the two contracting parties is established by their own consensus, since no one else has authority over them, so it is invalidated by their consensus. When thamaniyya is invalidated, they become specific by specification, and they do not become weighable (wazni) because consensus on being countable ('adad) remains, for breaking consensus in respect of count would corrupt the contract. Thus it is like selling one walnut for two walnuts. Unlike coins (nuqud) because they are created for thamaniyya. And unlike the case where both are unspecified because that is like a debt for a debt (kali' bi al-kali'), which is prohibited. And unlike the case where one of them is unspecified, because the genus alone prohibits nasi'ah. (Translation of Urdu explanation:) Explanation: Fils (copper coin) plural is fulus and aflus. There are four forms of selling fulus against fulus with differential: (1) selling one unspecified fils for two unspecified fils; (2) selling one specified fils for two unspecified fils; (3) selling one unspecified fils for two specified fils; (4) selling one specified fils for two specified fils. Among these, the first three are invalid (fasid), and the fourth is permissible according to the two shaikhs, and this is also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, while Imam Muhammad says it is not permissible, and Imam al-Shafi'i also has another saying that agrees. The first form is invalid because the fulus current in the market are all equal in value, and increase without return (riba) is prohibited. The second form is invalid because the specific coin would return to its owner plus another coin without consideration (lahw). The third form is invalid because after the transaction, one coin remains with the buyer without return (ibwa'). The fourth form: Imam Muhammad's proof is that thamaniyya of fulus is established by consensus of all, so it cannot be altered by the parties; therefore they remain thaman and do not become specific; thus it is like both unspecified, which is invalid. The two shaikhs' proof is that thamaniyya is by convention, and the parties can agree to treat them as commodities; then they become specific and the sale is like walnuts.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of one fils (copper coin) for two fils when all are specified (mu'ayyan). The matn from al-Hidayah states: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Two Shaikhs), such a sale is permissible. Imam Muhammad holds it is impermissible. The core issue is whether fulus are considered thaman (money) by nature or by convention. Imam Muhammad argues that thamaniyya is established by universal consensus (ishtilah al-kull), so individual parties cannot nullify it. Therefore, fulus remain as thaman, and like dirhams, they are not specific (ghayr mu'ayyan) when used as price; thus selling one for two resembles a loan with excess, which is riba. The Two Shaikhs respond that thamaniyya for fulus is established by the convention of the parties themselves; since no one has authority over the contracting parties regarding their own transaction, they can mutually agree to treat the fulus as commodities (like walnuts). Once thamaniyya is set aside by their agreement, the fulus become specific items by specification (ta'yin). They do not revert to being weight-based (wazni) because the general convention counts them as countable, and breaking that would corrupt the contract. Hence, the sale is like selling one walnut for two walnuts, which is permissible (as seen in the previous lesson). The explanation further distinguishes four scenarios, only the fourth (both specific) being valid according to the Two Shaikhs. The three other scenarios involve riba or prohibited speculative elements (kali' bi al-kali', lahw, ibwa'). The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute with detailed reasoning.

Key Terms
ثمنية (thamaniyya): The status of being thaman (countervalue/money) in a sale transaction.
اصطلاح (istilah): Convention or agreement among people that establishes a particular status or value.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification; making a specific item (mu'ayyan) as opposed to generic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why is selling one specified fils for two specified fils impermissible?
A) Because the fils are not specific enough.
B) Because thamaniyya of fulus is established by universal convention and cannot be nullified by the parties, so they remain thaman and do not become specific, leading to riba.
C) Because the transaction resembles lahw (play).
D) Because Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf are always wrong.

Key Takeaway
Fulus are money by convention; contracting parties can nullify thamaniyya by mutual agreement, transforming them into specific commodities and permitting an otherwise prohibited exchange.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Sale of Fulus for Fulus with Excess: Four Scenarios and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale of specified fulus for specified fulus with excess, with detailed rationales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four scenarios of selling fulus for fulus with excess, identify which are valid or invalid according to each Hanafi authority, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the fourth scenario by applying the concepts of thamaniyya and 'adadi.

Core Idea
Fulus can be treated as merchandise by mutual agreement, making their sale with excess valid, unlike gold and silver.

This lesson examines the ruling on selling fulus (copper coins) for fulus with excess (mufadala). The text from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents four scenarios and an intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad. Understanding this passage will clarify how the Hanafi school distinguishes between fulus and gold/silver in terms of thamaniyya (monetary status) and the concept of 'adadi (countability), which exempts fulus from riba al-fadl when parties agree to treat them as merchandise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
List the four cases of selling one fals for two fulus: (a) unspecified for unspecified, (b) specified for unspecified, (c) unspecified for specified, (d) specified for specified. The first three are rendered invalid in the text.
Scenarios (b) and (c) are variations where one side is specified and the other unspecified.
2
Understand why the first three are invalid
For each, grasp the specific reason: (a) riba because excess without equivalent due to equal market value; (b) the specified coin returns to the seller plus another for free, resembling gambling; (c) like a sale of debt for debt with excess.
Riba al-fadl is the key concern; the text uses the term 'ربوا' (riba).
3
State the intra-Hanafi dispute on the fourth scenario
For the sale of one specified fals for two specified fulus, Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold it valid (sahih), while Imam Muhammad holds it invalid (fasid).
This is the core khilaf in this lesson.
4
Analyze the two proofs
Shaykhayn argue that the parties can waive thamaniyya, making fulus merchandise, and being 'adadi (countable) no riba applies. Imam Muhammad argues that thamaniyya is established by universal consensus (ijma' of all people) and cannot be waived by parties alone, so fulus remain thaman and the sale constitutes riba.
The dispute hinges on the nature of thamaniyya: conventional vs. intrinsic.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the objection
The text addresses that if thamaniyya is invalidated, fulus might become weighed (like brass) leading to riba. The response: parties also agree on 'adadi, which remains, so fulus stay countable like walnuts, not weighed. This is supported by the principle that breaking agreement on countability would invalidate the contract.
This rebuttal consolidates the Shaykhayn's position.

شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عاقدین کے حق میں فلوس کاٹن ہونا خود ان کے اتفاق کر لینے سے ثابت ہوا ہے نہ کہ تمام لوگوں کے اتفاق کرنے سے کیونکہ ان پر کسی دوسرے کو ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے پس جب عاقدین کے انکار کرنے سے فلوس کا شمن ثابت ہوا ہے تو انہیں کے باطل کرنے سے باطل ہو جائیگا اور جب فلوس کا ثمن ہونا باطل ہو گیا تو فلوس سامان ہو گئے اور سامان متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتا ہے۔ مگر چونکہ ایک دو پیسے میں قدر اور معیار موجود نہیں ہے یعنی نہ کیلی ہیں اور نہ وزنی ہیں۔ اس لیے کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کرنے میں ربوا محقق نہ ہوگا اور جب ربوا متحقق نہیں ہوا تو یہ بیع جائز ہوگی ۔
ولا يعود وزنيا ... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے سوال یہ ہے کہ جب عاقدین کے حق میں فلوس کا شمن ہونا باطل ہو گیا تو ان کا وزنی ہونا بھی عود کر آئیگا کیونکہ منیت باطل ہونے کے بعد فلوس پتیل کے ٹکڑے رہے اور پتیل وزنی ہوتا ہے تو یہ ایسا ہوا گویا اس نے پیتل کے ایک ٹکڑے کو دوٹکڑوں کے عوض فروخت کیا اور یہ نا جائز ہے کیونکہ موزدنی چیز کو انداز سے سے بچنا نا جائز ہے اس لئے ثمنیت باطل ہونے کے بعد بھی ایک معین پیسہ کو دو معین پیسوں کے عوض بیچنانا جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ حالانکہ شیخین اس کو جائز فرماتے ہیں اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عاقدین نے فلوس کے اندر دو چیزوں پر اتفاق کیا تھا ایک فلوس کے ثمن ہونے پر دوسرے اُن کے عددی ہونے پر مگر جب عاقدین نے ایک دو کے عوض بیچنے پر اقدام کیا تو انھوں نے ثمنیت کا اعتبار کرنے سے اعراض کیا کیونکہ ثمن ہونے کی صورت میں ایک پیسہ کا دو کے عوض بیچنار بوا ہونے کی وجہ سے قطعاً نا جائز ہے اور ان کی اندر عددی ہونے کا اعتبار کرنے سے اعراض نہیں کیا ہے اور ان دونوں کے حق میں فلوس کا شمن ہونے سے خارج ہونا اُن کے عددی ہونے سے خارج ہونے کو بھی مستلزم نہیں ہے یعنی فلوس کے شمن نہ ہونے سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ وہ عددی نہ ہوں جیسے اخروٹ اور انڈا کہ یہ دونوں عددی ہیں مگر شمن نہیں ہیں پس اسی طرح فلوس کی ضمنیت کے بطلان پر عاقدین کے اتفاق کر لینے کے بعد فلوس کے اندر شمنیت تو نہ رہی البتہ ان کا عددی ہونا باقی ہے اور فلوس کا عددی ہونا باقی ہے تو اتحاد قد رفوت ہو گیا اور قدریا جنس کے فوت ہونے سے کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بیع جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے مسئلہ مذکورہ میں ایک پیسہ کی بیع دو پیسوں کے عوض بلا کسی قباحت کے جائز ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ اس جواب کو یوں فرماتے ہیں کہ فلوس کے عددی ہونے پر عاقدین کا اتفاق باقی ہے کیونکہ عددی ہونے کے حق میں اتفاق کو توڑنے میں عقد فاسد ہو جاتا ہے حالانکہ ان دونوں نے صحت عقد کا ارادہ کیا ہے اور صحت عقد فلوس کے عددی ہونے کو باقی رکھے بغیر ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہی کہا جائے گا کہ فلوس کے عددی ہونے پر عاقدین کا اتفاق ہے اور جب عددی ہونے پر اتفاق ہے تو فلوس ، اخروٹ کے مانند ہو گئے اور ایک اخروٹ کی بیع دو اخروٹ کے عوض جائز ہے پس اسی طرح ایک پیسہ کی بیع دو پیسوں کے عوض جائز ہوگی بر خلاف نقود یعنی در اہم ودنا نیر کے کہ اُن کا شمن ہونا چونکہ پیدائشی اور خلقی ہے۔ اس لئے عاقدین کے اتفاق کر لینے سے ان کی شمنیت باطل نہ ہوگی اور جب باطل نہیں ہوئی تو کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ بیع بھی نا جائز ہوگی امام محمد کا جواب دیتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر دونوں عوض
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, Volume 8. ... Breaking the agreement in the matter of [thaman] causes the contract to be invalid. Like selling one walnut for two walnuts, unlike [naqd] because they are inherently thaman, and unlike when fulus are unspecified because it is a sale of debt for debt, although it is prohibited, and unlike when one of the two is unspecified, because the mere genus makes deferment prohibited. Explanation: Fals, a coin other than gold and silver, plural fulus and aflas. The sale of fulus for fulus with excess has four forms: (1) sale of one unspecified fals for two unspecified fulus; (2) sale of one specified fals for two unspecified fulus; (3) sale of one unspecified fals for two specified fulus; (4) sale of one specified fals for two specified fulus. Among these, the first three forms are invalid, and the fourth is valid according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and this is also one opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i, while Imam Muhammad deems it invalid, and al-Shafi'i also has one opinion like that. [The passage continues with detailed reasoning for each case...]
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, addresses the ruling on selling fulus (copper coins) for fulus with excess (mufadala). It is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text first states a general principle: breaking the agreement regarding thamaniyya (status as price) invalidates the contract, as in selling one walnut for two walnuts. However, this does not apply to [naqd] (gold and silver) because they are inherently thaman, nor to unspecified fulus sold for unspecified fulus (which resembles a sale of debt for debt), nor when one side is unspecified (since the genus alone makes riba al-nasi'ah). Then the sharh explains the four scenarios of selling fulus for fulus with excess. In the first three, where at least one side is unspecified, the sale is invalid due to riba (excess without corresponding consideration). In the fourth scenario (specified for specified), there is disagreement: Imam Muhammad considers it invalid because he holds that fulus are inherently thaman by common consensus, and thus cannot be made specified by the parties. The Shaykhayn (Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) consider it valid because they argue that the parties have agreed to treat the fulus as merchandise, not as thaman, and since fulus are not weighed or measured, no riba applies. The text then addresses an objection: if thamaniyya is invalidated, fulus become like brass pieces, which are weighed, so selling one for two would be riba. The response is that the parties agreed on two aspects: thamaniyya and 'adadi (countability). By selling with excess, they abandoned thamaniyya but retained 'adadi, so fulus remain countable like walnuts, not weighed. Thus, the sale is valid. The author of al-Hidayah supports this by stating that the agreement on 'adadi remains, for breaking it would invalidate the contract which the parties intend to keep valid. Therefore, the fourth scenario is valid, unlike gold and silver whose thamaniyya is inherent and cannot be overridden by the parties.

Key Terms
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins (fals, plural fulus) that are used as currency but are not gold or silver. In this passage, fulus are distinguished from naqd (gold and silver) and are discussed in terms of their status as thaman (price) or merchandise.
ثمنیت (thamaniyya): The quality of being thaman (price/currency). In this text, it refers to the legal attribute by which fulus serve as money in transactions.
عددی ('adadi): Countable by number (ma'dud), as opposed to weighed (wazni) or measured (kayli). In this passage, fulus are considered 'adadi goods, which makes them exempt from riba al-fadl when sold with excess.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is the sale of one specified fals for two specified fulus valid, despite the excess?
A) Because fulus are inherently thaman and can be sold with excess like gold.
B) Because the parties have agreed to treat fulus as merchandise rather than thaman, and fulus are countable, not weighed or measured.
C) Because the sale is of debt for debt, which is permitted in this case.
D) Because both parties are free to set any price they agree upon.

Key Takeaway
The sale of one specified fals for two specified fulus is valid according to the Shaykhayn because parties can waive thamaniyya and fulus remain 'adadi, but invalid according to Imam Muhammad who holds thamaniyya is inviolable; the mufta bihi is the Shaykhayn's view.

Sale of Fulus with Excess: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale of fulus with excess: conditions for permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions under which the sale of fulus with excess is permissible in the Hanafi school and distinguish between the views of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Fulus are thaman by convention; parties can agree to treat them as counted goods, making excess permissible.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of copper coins (fulus) with an excess in quantity. While gold and silver coins are inherently ribawi, fulus derive their status as currency from customary usage, which can be altered by agreement. The passage from al-Hidayah presents a debate between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad, culminating in a conditional permissibility that hinges on the parties' intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
What is being sold? One fuls for two fuls. The act involves an excess in quantity, which typically triggers riba if the items are ribawi. Determine the default ruling.
The passage starts by stating that selling one fuls for two fuls resembles selling one dirham for two dirhams, which is impermissible.
2
Recognize the Shaykhayn's argument
Understand why Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf initially considered the sale impermissible. They argued that fulus become weighed brass once the status of thaman is nullified, making the sale with excess a case of riba.
Their key point: if thaman is nullified, fulus revert to being brass pieces, which are weighed, and selling weighed items by estimation with excess is riba.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's response
Imam Muhammad countered that the parties agreed on two aspects: fulus being thaman and fulus being counted. Nullifying thaman does not nullify the counted nature. Counted items like walnuts are not ribawi, so excess is permissible.
The analogy to walnuts and eggs illustrates that counted items are not subject to riba al-fadl.
4
Extract the conditions for permissibility
From the response, identify the necessary conditions: both fulus must be specified ('ayn) and the parties must intend to treat them as counted goods. If either is unspecified (dayn), the sale is impermissible due to sale of debt for debt or riba al-nasi'ah.
The passage explicitly lists the cases of both unspecified, one specified, and both specified with counted intention.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference in views leads to different rulings: under the Shaykhayn's initial view, the sale is always impermissible; under Imam Muhammad's adopted view, it is permissible under the stated conditions. The mufta bihi is Imam Muhammad's position.
This shows that intra-Hanafi disputes are resolved by later authorities like the author of Hidayah.

Throw in this case the sale will be impermissible, and selling one paisa for two paisas becomes like selling one dirham for two dirhams, which is impermissible, so the mentioned case is also impermissible. The evidence of the two shaykhs is that for the contracting parties, the commodity-ness of fulus is established by their own agreement, not by the agreement of all people, because no one else has guardianship over them. So when the fulus' being thaman is established by their affirmation, it is nullified by their nullification. And when the fulus' being thaman is nullified, the fulus become goods, and goods become specified by specification. But since one or two paisas do not have capacity and measure, i.e., they are neither measured nor weighed, therefore riba does not materialize in selling with excess, and when riba does not materialize, this sale is permissible. 'And it does not return to being weighed... etc.' answers a question: The question is: When the fulus' being thaman for the contracting parties is nullified, does their being weighed also return? Because after nullifying the thaman, the fulus remain pieces of brass, and brass is weighed. So this becomes like selling one piece of brass for two pieces, which is impermissible because selling a weighed thing by estimation is impermissible. Therefore, even after the nullification of thaman, selling one specific pice for two specific pices should have been impermissible, whereas the two shaykhs deem it permissible. The answer is that the contracting parties agreed on two things regarding the fulus: one, that they are thaman, and two, that they are counted. But when they proceeded to sell one for two, they disregarded the consideration of thaman because in the case of being thaman, selling one paisa for two is absolutely impermissible due to riba, and they did not disregard the consideration of being counted. And for them, the removal of fulus from thaman does not necessitate their removal from being counted, i.e., the fact that fulus are not thaman does not imply that they are not counted, like walnuts and eggs, which are counted but not thaman. So similarly, after the contracting parties agree on the nullification of fulus' being thaman, they no longer have thaman, but their being counted remains. And when their being counted remains, then the unity of measure is lost, and with the loss of the genus of measure, sale with excess is permissible. Therefore, in the mentioned case, selling one paisa for two paisas is permissible without any objection. The author of Hidayah presents this answer as: The contracting parties' agreement on the fulus being counted remains, because breaking the agreement on being counted would render the contract invalid, whereas they intend the validity of the contract, and validity is not possible without preserving the fulus' being counted. So it is said that the contracting parties agree on the fulus being counted, and when they agree on being counted, the fulus become like walnuts, and selling one walnut for two walnuts is permissible, so similarly selling one paisa for two paisas is permissible, unlike gold and silver coins, because their being thaman is innate and natural, so their thaman is not nullified by the agreement of the contracting parties, and when it is not nullified, sale with excess is also impermissible. Responding to Imam Muhammad, the author of Hidayah says: If both commodities are unspecified, the sale is impermissible because in that case it necessitates kāli' bil kāli', i.e., sale of debt for debt, which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited. And if one of the two commodities is unspecified and the other specified, it is impermissible because in fulus, although the unity of measure is absent, the unity of genus is present, and the mere presence of genus prohibits deferment (nasa'), so this sale is also prohibited, because the unspecified commodity will be considered deferred, and the specified will be considered spot.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the sale of fulus (copper coins) with an excess in quantity. The text first states a scenario where the sale is initially considered impermissible because one paisa for two paisas resembles selling one dirham for two dirhams, which is riba. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that fulus derive their status as thaman (currency) by the agreement of the contracting parties, and thus they can nullify that agreement. Once thaman is nullified, the fulus become goods (sama'n), and since they are not measured or weighed, riba does not apply. However, the text then raises an objection: if thaman is nullified, the fulus become brass pieces, which are weighed, so the sale should still be ribawi. The response is that the parties agreed on two characteristics of the fulus: being thaman and being counted (ma'dud). When they sold one for two, they abandoned the thaman aspect but kept the counted aspect. Counted items, like walnuts, are not ribawi, so the sale is permissible. The author of Hidayah endorses this answer, adding that fulus remain counted because otherwise the contract would be invalid. He then presents Imam Muhammad's qualification: this ruling only applies when both fulus are specified ('ayn) and the parties treat them as counted. If both are unspecified (dayn), it is forbidden as sale of debt for debt. If one is specified and one unspecified, it is forbidden due to genus unity with deferment.

Key Terms
فلوس (fulūs): Copper coins used as currency; they are considered thaman (price) by convention (urf) but can be treated as goods (sama'n) by agreement.
ثمن (thaman): Price or currency; something that serves as a medium of exchange. According to Hanafis, thaman can be conventional (like fulus) or innate (like gold and silver).
عددی (ma'dūd): Counted items; goods sold by count rather than weight or measure. Not subject to riba al-fadl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the sale of one fuls for two fuls permissible?
A) Always, because fulus are not ribawi.
B) Only when both fulus are specified and the parties agree to treat them as counted items.
C) Only when both fulus are unspecified (dayn).
D) Never, because it involves riba.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of selling fulus with excess depends on whether they are treated as specified counted goods; if unspecified, it is forbidden.

Selling Wheat for Flour or Sawiq: Hanafi Prohibition and Maliki Disagreement
Presents Hanafi prohibition of selling wheat for flour or sawiq, with proofs and rebuttal of Maliki view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for prohibiting the sale of wheat for flour/sawiq and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Partial genus similarity does not permit unequal measure; packing density creates potential riba.

This passage addresses a classic fiqh dispute: can wheat be exchanged for its derivatives, flour or sawiq, in equal measure? While both share the same origin, the Hanafi school prohibits the exchange due to physical differences that create inequality in actual quantity. The Maliki school permits it, analogizing to the permissibility of trading large grains for small grains. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to identify riba in modern commodity exchanges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State clearly the Hanafi position: selling wheat for flour or sawiq is not permissible, whether equal or with excess.
The Arabic phrase 'لا يجوز' indicates prohibition.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
Examine the reasoning: partial similarity (mujanasah) exists because both are from wheat, but the measure (kayl) is not truly equal due to packing density—flour/sawiq pack tightly, wheat grains leave gaps.
This inequality makes the exchange ribawi, as equal volume does not mean equal substance.
3
Present the Maliki view and proof
State the Maliki position: the sale is permissible if equal by measure. Their proof: grinding does not change the essence; analogizing to selling large grains for small grains equally.
Imam Malik and in one view Imam Ahmad hold this.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: the difference in name and form (khalta vs dafiq) is significant; the packing creates real inequality, so the Maliki analogy fails.
The rebuttal highlights that partial similarity is insufficient for permitting the exchange.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: under Hanafi law, such exchanges are invalid; under Maliki, they are valid if equal by measure.
This affects contracts in regions where Hanafi fiqh is followed.

وجہ زائل نہیں ہوئی بلکہ باقی ہے تو گویا مجانست کے زائل ہونے میں شک واقع ہو گیا۔ حالانکہ مجانست کا
Ruling on selling wheat for flour or for sawiq. He said: It is not permissible to sell wheat for flour or for sawiq, because similarity (mujanasah) remains in one respect; since both are parts of wheat, and the standard in both is measure (kayl), but the measure is not equal between them and wheat because they pack tightly in the measure and the grains of wheat are loose, so it is not permissible even if it is measure for measure. Translation: And selling wheat for flour is not permissible, nor for sawiq, because similarity remains in one respect, i.e., flour and sawiq are both parts of wheat, and the standard in both is kayl, but kayl cannot make equality between them and wheat because flour and sawiq pack solidly in the measure, and between the grains of wheat there is space, so it is not permissible even if the sale is measure for measure. Explanation of the issue: According to us, selling wheat for its flour or for its sawiq is not permissible, neither equally nor with excess. This is also a saying of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Thawri. And the madhhab of Imam Malik is that selling wheat for its flour or sawiq equally is permissible. This is also the more apparent saying of Imam Ahmad. Imam Malik's evidence is that wheat's flour and sawiq are identically wheat. The only difference is that the name of the separated parts of wheat is flour and sawiq, and the name of the aggregated parts is grain and wheat. So flour and sawiq resemble small grains of wheat, and the wheat itself resembles large grains. And since selling large grains of wheat for small grains by measure and scale equally is permissible, therefore selling wheat for flour and sawiq equally is also permissible. Our evidence is that between wheat and its flour, and between wheat and its sawiq, there is similarity in one respect and not in another. The similarity exists because when wheat is ground, only its parts are separated, and a thing does not become another by the separation of parts, but remains the same. So what was before grinding remains after grinding. And the similarity is absent because the difference in genus is realized by difference in name, form, and meaning, like between wheat and barley, where the name is different, the form is different, and the benefits are different. Similarly, in this case, before grinding it was called wheat, and after grinding it became flour or sawiq, so the names are different, because wheat is fried and chewed, and between flour and sawiq, similarity in one respect is lost and in one respect not lost but remains, so there is doubt about the loss of similarity. Whereas similarity...
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the sale of wheat for its derivatives, flour (dafiq) and sawiq (parched barley meal). The Hanafi position, drawn from the matn of Hidayah, is that such a sale is impermissible even if done measure for measure. The reason is that while wheat, flour, and sawiq share the same genus (all from the same substance), they differ in their measure characteristics: flour and sawiq pack densely in a measuring container, while wheat grains leave gaps, so equal kayl does not ensure equal quantity. This makes the sale potentially ribawi. The text then notes that this is also the view of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Thawri. However, Imam Malik permits the sale if done equally by measure, and this is also the more apparent view of Imam Ahmad. Imam Malik's evidence is that flour and sawiq are essentially the same as wheat; the only difference is that the constituents are separated. Since selling large wheat grains for small grains equally is permissible, selling wheat for flour equally should also be permissible. The Hanafi rebuttal argues that mujanasah (similarity) is present in one respect (both are from wheat) but absent in another (name, form, and usage differ). This doubt about full similarity makes the sale impermissible as a precaution against riba. The text is cut off mid-sentence, but the argument continues that because the similarity is not complete, the ruling follows the principle of avoiding riba.

Key Terms
مجانست (mujānasah): Similarity or homogeneity in genus; used to determine if riba applies. Here, it is partial between wheat and its derivatives.
کیل (kayl): Measure by volume; the standard for wheat and its derivatives. The issue is that the same volume of flour and wheat does not contain the same quantity of substance.
ستو (sawīq): Parched barley meal, a derivative of barley or wheat; considered similar to flour in this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because flour and wheat are different genera.
B) Because the measure of flour differs from the measure of wheat due to packing density.
C) Because the Prophet prohibited selling food for food.
D) Because flour is not a ribawi item.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits exchanging wheat for its derived forms (flour, sawiq) due to physical differences that create inequality in measure, preventing riba.

Prohibition of Selling Debt for Debt (Kāli bi Kāli)
States the prohibition of selling debt for debt with a hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a sale where both countervalues are unspecified and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Selling debt for debt is strictly prohibited based on explicit Prophetic prohibition.

In this lesson, we examine the first scenario from the passage: a sale where both countervalues are debts rather than tangible items. Such a transaction falls under the forbidden category of kāli bi kāli. You will learn the ruling and the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling two unspecified countervalues (both are debts). The ruling is that it is haram (prohibited).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited kāli bi kāli (debt for debt).
The hadith is not quoted verbatim in the passage, but referenced.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition (نهي) in the hadith indicates that such a transaction is forbidden. The term 'kāli bi kāli' specifically refers to exchanging debts.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While most schools agree on prohibition, some (e.g., Shafi'i) may permit if the debts are known and certain conditions are met.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adheres to the apparent meaning of the prohibition without exceptions, considering it haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع
FIF
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد هشتم
غیر معین ہوں تو بیع اس لئے نا جائز ہے کہ اس صورت میں کافی بالکافی یعنی دین کی بیچ دین کے عوض یعنی ما وجب فی الذمہ کی بیع ما وجب فی الذمہ کے عوض یعنی ادھار کی بیع ادھار کے عوض لازم آئے گی حالانکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کالی بالکالی یعنی دین بدین کی بیع سے منع فرمایا ہے اور اگر دونوں عوضوں میں سے ایک عوض غیر معین اور ایک معین ہو تو اس لئے ناجائز ہے کہ فلوس میں اتحاد قد را گر چہ معدوم مہے لیکن اتحاد جنس موجود ہے اور تنہا جنس کا موجود ہونا نساء یعنی ادھار کو حرام کر دیتا ہے اس لئے یہ بیچ بھی حرام ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ جو عوض غیر معین ہو گا وہ ادھار شمار ہوگا اور جو معین ہوگا وہ نقد شمار ہوگا۔
If both countervalues are unspecified, then the sale is invalid because in that case it would be kāli bi kāli, i.e., selling debt for debt, i.e., selling what is owed for what is owed, i.e., selling credit for credit, while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited kāli bi kāli, i.e., selling debt for debt. And if one of the two countervalues is unspecified and the other is specified, then it is invalid because although unity of measure is absent, unity of genus (jins) exists, and the mere existence of genus prohibits credit (nasi'ah). Therefore, this sale is also forbidden because the unspecified countervalue would be considered credit and the specified would be considered cash.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding sales where the countervalues are unspecified. The text first addresses the case where both are unspecified: such a sale is invalid because it constitutes the prohibited transaction of kāli bi kāli (debt for debt), which the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade. The second case is where one countervalue is unspecified and the other is specified. Here, although the specific amount is known for one side, the unspecified side makes it akin to credit, and because the genus (jins) is the same (e.g., both are gold or both are silver), the existence of jins alone makes the credit element prohibited. Thus the sale is haram. The ruling is based on the hadith prohibiting debt-for-debt sales and on the principle that unity of genus alone suffices to prohibit credit in such exchanges.

Key Terms
کالی بالکالی (kāli bi kāli): Selling debt for debt, i.e., two credits exchanged without immediate delivery of the countervalues.
دین (dayn): A debt or liability owed by one party to another, typically a monetary obligation or something due in the future.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a sale where both countervalues are unspecified prohibited?
A) Because it leads to uncertainty (gharar)
B) Because it constitutes selling debt for debt (kāli bi kāli)
C) Because the Prophet prohibited selling food for food
D) Because the measure is unknown

Key Takeaway
Selling debt for debt is absolutely prohibited based on the Prophetic hadith, regardless of the amounts known or unknown.

Prohibition of Mixing Unspecified and Specified Countervalues with Same Genus
Extends the prohibition to mixed unspecified-specified countervalues with same genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that unity of genus (jins) alone prohibits credit (nasi'ah) and determine when a sale with one unspecified countervalue is haram.

Core Idea
Unity of genus alone suffices to make a mixed credit-cash sale prohibited.

This lesson covers the second scenario from the passage: a sale where one countervalue is specified (cash) and the other is unspecified (credit). Even though one side is cash, if the genus of both items is the same, the credit element triggers prohibition. You will learn how jins works in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling an unspecified countervalue (debt) for a specified countervalue (cash) of the same genus. The ruling is haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle that unity of jins alone prohibits credit (nasi'ah) in exchanges. This is based on riba proofs (e.g., hadith of six commodities).
The passage itself does not quote a specific hadith but states the principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The passage states: 'Although unity of measure is absent, unity of genus exists, and the mere existence of genus prohibits credit.' So the effective cause is jins.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require both unity of jins and measure to prohibit credit.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Hanafi relies on jins alone as sufficient.

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding sales where the countervalues are unspecified. The text first addresses the case where both are unspecified: such a sale is invalid because it constitutes the prohibited transaction of kāli bi kāli (debt for debt), which the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade. The second case is where one countervalue is unspecified and the other is specified. Thus the sale is haram. The ruling is based on the hadith prohibiting debt-for-debt sales and on the principle that unity of genus alone suffices to prohibit credit in such exchanges.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): The category or genus of an item, determined by common origin and essential characteristics (e.g., wheat, gold).
دین (dayn): A debt or liability owed by one party to another.

Selling Wheat for Flour or Sattu: Hanafi Ruling and Maliki Dispute
Provides the Hanafi ruling and rebuts Imam Malik's view allowing equal exchange.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging wheat for its processed forms (flour/sattu), explain the Hanafi proof based on partial jins and volumetric impossibility, and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Wheat cannot be sold for flour or sattu even if measured equally – true equality is impossible due to packing differences.

You already know that exchanging wheat for wheat in unequal amounts is riba al-fadl. But what about exchanging wheat for its own derivatives – flour or roasted flour (sattu)? Are they the same jins or not? The Hanafi school says the sale is invalid regardless of equality, while Imam Malik allows it if measured equally. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and the rebuttal of the Maliki view, focusing on the principle that suspicion of riba is also prohibited when jins and measure are both present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hanafi ruling and its scope
Start by noting that the Hanafi school absolutely prohibits selling wheat for flour or sattu, whether equal or unequal. This is stated clearly in the matn.
The ruling applies to both flour and sattu, as both are processed forms of wheat.
2
Understand the concept of partial jins (mujānasah min wajh)
The text argues that wheat and its derivatives share the same substance (partial jins) but differ in name, form, and benefit. This ambiguity creates a suspicion (shubhah) that the jins unity remains, thus riba rules apply.
Hanafi usul: certainty of jins is not removed by doubt; therefore the jins is considered still present.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof: volumetric inequality
Even if both sides are measured by volume (kayl), true equality is impossible because flour/sattu pack tightly in the measure while wheat grains have gaps. This creates a suspicion of excess, which is prohibited like actual riba.
The principle here is that prohibition of riba covers both actual excess and suspected excess when jins and qadr coincide.
4
Examine the Maliki counter-proof
Imam Malik argues that flour and sattu are essentially crushed wheat; thus they are the same jins. He analogizes exchanging whole wheat for crushed wheat to exchanging large grains for small grains, which is permissible equally by volume.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between simple crushing and change in name/form/benefit.
5
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Conclude that the Hanafi position renders the sale batil (invalid), while the Maliki position considers it valid if equal. The relied-upon fatwa is the Hanafi view.
This affects how a Hanafi mufti would advise on contracts involving grain and its derivatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گندم کی آٹے کے بدلے اور ستو کے بدلے بیع کا حکم
قال ولايجوز بيع الحنطة بالدقيق ولا بالسويق؛ لأن المجانسة باقية من وجه؛ لأنهما من أجزاء الحنطة والمعيار فيهما الكيل لكن الكيل غير مسو بينهما وبين الحنطة لاكتنازهما فيه وتخلخلى حبات الحنطة فلايجوز وإن كان كيلا بكيل
ترجمہ اور گندم کا آٹے کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ ستو کے عوض کیونکہ مجانست من وجہ باقی ہے اسلئے کہ آٹا اور ستو دونوں گندم کے اجزاء میں سے ہیں اور ان دونوں میں معیار کیل ہے لیکن کیل ان دونوں اور گندم کے درمیان برابری نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ آٹا اور ستو پیمانہ میں ٹھوس بھر جاتا ہے اور گندم کے دانوں کے درمیان خلاء ہوتا ہے اسلئے جائز نہیں ہے اگر چہ بیع کیلًا بکیل ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک گندم کی بیع اس کے آٹے کے عوض اور گندم کی بیع اس کے ستو کے عوض جائز نہیں ہے نہ برابر کر کے اور نہ زیادتی کے ساتھ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی، امام احمد اور امام ثوری کا ہے اور امام مالک کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ گندم کی بیع، اس کے آٹے اور ستو کے عوض برابر کر کے جائز ہے یہی امام احمد کا قول اظہر ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گندم کا آٹا اور ستو بعینہ گندم ہے۔ صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ گندم کے اجزاء متفرقہ کا نام آٹا اور ستو ہے اور اجزاء مجتمعہ کا نام حنطہ اور گندم ہے۔ پس آٹا اور ستو گندم کے چھوٹے چھوٹے دانوں کے مشابہ ہو گئے اور نفس گندم بڑے بڑے دانوں کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور گندم کے بڑے بڑے دانوں کو چھوٹے چھوٹے دانوں کے عوض کیل اور پیمانہ کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے فروخت کرنا چونکہ جائز ہے۔ اس لئے گندم کو آٹے اور ستو کے عوض برابر کر کے بیچنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گندم اور اس کے آٹے کے درمیان اور گندم اور ستو کے درمیان من وجہ ہم جنس ہونا موجود ہے اور من وجہ موجود نہیں ہے۔ مجانست موجود تو اس لئے ہے کہ گندم کو پیسے سے صرف گندم کے اجزاء متفرق ہو جاتے ہیں اور شئے جمع تفریق اجزاء کی وجہ سے دوسری نہیں ہو جاتی بلکہ سابقہ شئے ہی باقی رہتی ہے۔ پس پیسے سے پہلے جو چیز تھی پیسے کے بعد بھی وہی چیز باقی ہے۔ اور مجانست غیر موجود اس لئے ہے کہ جنس کا اختلاف نام، صورت اور معنی کے اختلاف سے متحقق ہوتا ہے جیسے گندم اور جو کے درمیان اختلاف جنس ہے کیونکہ دونوں کا نام بھی مختلف ہے، صورت بھی مختلف ہے اور معانی اور منافع بھی مختلف ہیں۔ پس اسی طرح اس صورت میں پیسنے سے پہلے گندم نام تھا اور پیسنے کے بعد آٹا یا ستو ہو گیا تو گویا دونوں کا نام مختلف ہے، صورت بھی مختلف ہے، اور منافع میں بھی فرق ہے کیونکہ گندم کو بھون کر چبایا جاتا ہے اور آٹے اور ستو کو پکا کر کھایا جاتا ہے۔ پس جب نام و صورت میں اختلاف پایا گیا تو گویا من وجہ مجانست زائل ہوگئی اور من وجہ زائل نہیں ہوئی بلکہ باقی ہے تو گویا مجانست کے زائل ہونے میں شک واقع ہو گیا۔ حالانکہ مجانست کا موجود ہونا یقینی تھا اور یقین شک کی وجہ سے زائل نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ مجانست زائل نہیں ہوئی بلکہ باقی ہے۔ پس گندم اور اس کے آٹے کے درمیان اور گندم اور ستو کے درمیان اتحاد جنسی اور اتحاد قدر دونوں پائے گئے۔ اور جب قدر مع الجنس دونوں پائے گئے تو تفاضل اور شبہ تفاضل دونوں حرام ہوں گے اور برابری کے ساتھ بیع جائز ہوگی۔ لیکن گندم اور آٹے اور ستو کا پیمانہ کیل ہوتا ہے اور کیل کے ذریعہ گندم اور اسکے آٹے اور ستو کے درمیان برابری پیدا کرنا ناممکن ہے کیونکہ پیمانے میں آٹے کو ٹھوس ٹھوس کر بھرا جا سکتا ہے مگر گندم کے دانوں کے درمیان چونکہ خلا باقی رہتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو ٹھوس کر نہیں بھرا جا سکتا۔ پس جب گندم کا ایک کیل، آٹے کے ایک کیل کے عوض بیچا جائے گا تو ان دونوں کے درمیان کمی زیادتی کا شبہ باقی رہ جائے گا یعنی آٹا زائد ہوگا اور گندم کم ہوگا۔ اور اموال ربعیہ یعنی قدر مع الجنس پائے جانے کی صورت میں جس طرح حقیقت ربا یعنی زیادتی حرام ہے اسی طرح ربا الشبہ بھی حرام ہے۔ اس لئے گندم کی بیع آٹے اور ستو کے عوض نا جائز قرار دی گئی اگر چہ کیل کے ذریعہ دونوں عوضوں کو برابر کر دیا گیا ہو۔
[Included in commentary]
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on exchanging wheat for its processed forms (flour and sattu). The ruling is that such exchanges are invalid, whether equal or unequal. The Hanafi evidence is based on the concept of jins (genus) and the requirement for equality in volume when both jins and measure (qadr) are present. The passage also brings in the inter-madhhab dispute, specifically with Imam Malik, who allows equal exchange. The Hanafi rebuttal focuses on the impossibility of achieving true volumetric equality due to the different densities of wheat grains versus flour/sattu, rendering the sale invalid even if an attempt is made to measure equally. The argument uses the principle that certainty (of jins) is not overridden by doubt, and that the prohibition of riba applies both to actual excess and to suspicion of excess.

Key Terms
حنطة (hintah): Wheat grain, the unprocessed cereal.
دقيق (daqīq): Flour, the ground form of wheat.
سويق (sawīq): Sattu, roasted barley or wheat flour, often consumed after roasting.
مجانسة (mujānasah): Homogeneity or sharing the same jins (genus).
كيل (kayl): Volume measurement, a standard measure for ribawi items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school prohibits selling wheat for flour even if measured equally by volume?
A) Because flour is a different jins from wheat
B) Because volumetric equality is impossible due to density differences
C) Because the Prophet specifically prohibited this transaction
D) Because both items are foodstuffs subject to riba

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits selling wheat for flour or sattu because true equality in measure is physically impossible, leading to a suspicion of riba that invalidates the sale.

Flour-for-Flour and Flour-for-Sattu: Rulings and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on flour-for-flour and dispute on flour-for-sattu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on flour-for-flour sale and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on flour-for-sattu, identifying the basis of each position.

Core Idea
Flour and sattu are partially homogeneous; their exchange is invalid for Abu Hanifa but valid for the Sahibayn due to different purposes.

This passage addresses two related sales: exchanging flour for flour, and flour for sattu (roasted grain flour). While the Hanafi school unanimously permits flour-for-flour equally by volume, an internal dispute arises when the items differ in processing. Understanding how the Hanafi masters determine 'jins' (genus) and the role of 'maqsud' (purpose) is key to grasping this nuanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sales and their base rulings
First, note that flour-for-flour is permissible in the Hanafi school when equal by volume. Second, flour-for-sattu is disputed: Abu Hanifa prohibits it, while the Sahibayn permit it.
The passage also mentions Shafi'i's objection to flour-for-flour, but the core here is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that flour and sattu share partial homogeneity (both are ground wheat), analogous to flour vs. roasted wheat or sound vs. moth-eaten grain, which are considered same jins. Therefore, equality is required, and since it cannot be guaranteed (or the maqsud differs), the sale is invalid.
He uses analogy (qiyas) with other processed grains where jins is preserved despite processing.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that flour and sattu are different jins because their purposes (maqsud) differ: flour is for cooking, sattu is for instant consumption. Thus, they are not ribawi items of the same kind, so exchange is permissible without equality.
They prioritize the difference in intended use over the common origin.
4
Evaluate the difference in effective cause (illa)
Abu Hanifa considers the common origin (wheat) as the primary factor, while the Sahibayn consider the secondary purpose. The dispute hinges on which factor is more determinative in defining jins for riba rules.
This reflects a broader usul principle: how to weigh multiple potential 'illal.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Abu Hanifa: sale is batil (invalid) regardless of equality. Sahibayn: sale is sahih (valid) without condition of equality. A Hanafi mufti must choose which view to follow based on tarjih or context.
Later Hanafi fatwa sometimes favors the Sahibayn in sales where jins is ambiguous, but Abu Hanifa's view remains strong.

Source Text

آٹے کی آٹے کے بدلے برابر برابر بیع کا حکم
ويجوز بيع الدقيق بالدقيق متساويا كيلا لتحقق الشرط وبيع الدقيق بالسويق لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة متفاضلاً ولا متاوياً لأنه لا يجوز بيع الدقيق بالمقلية ولا بيع السويق بالحنطة فكذا بيع أجزائهما لقيام المجانسة من وجه وعندهما يجوز؛ لأنهما جنسان مختلفان لاختلاف المقصود قلنا معظم المقصود وهو التغذى يشلهما ولايبالى بفوات البعض كالمقلية مع غير المقلية والعلكة بالمسوسة
ترجمہ اور آٹے کو آٹے کے عوض پیمانہ سے برابر کر کے بیچنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ شرط موجود ہے اور آٹے کو ستو کے عوض بیچنا ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نہ متفاضلاً جائز ہے اور نہ متساویا، کیونکہ آٹے کو بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ ستو کو گندم کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے۔ پس اسی طرح ان کے اجزاء کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ من وجہ مجانست موجود ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ آٹا اور ستو اختلاف مقصود کی وجہ سے دو مختلف جنس ہیں۔ ہم کہیں گے کہ سب سے بڑا مقصود یعنی غذا حاصل کرنا دونوں کو شامل ہے اور بعض مقصود کے فوت ہونے کا لحاظ نہیں کیا جائے گا جیسے بھونے ہوئے کی بیع بغیر بھونے ہوئے کے ساتھ اور عمدہ کی بیع گھنے ہوئے کے ساتھ۔ تشریح مسئلہ ہمارے نزدیک پیمانے اور کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے آٹے کی بیع آٹے کے عوض جائز ہے یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ پیمانے سے برابر کرنے کے باوجود آٹے کی بیع آٹے کے عوض ناجائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پیمانے اور کیل کے ذریعہ آٹے کو برابر نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ کیونکہ آٹا پیمانے میں ڈال کر دبانے سے دب جاتا ہے تو کیل کرنے کے باوجود پورے طور پر برابری متحقق نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب برابری متحقق نہیں ہوئی تو برابری کے شبہ ربا کی وجہ سے آٹے کی بیع آٹے کے عوض ناجائز ہوگی اگر چہ کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کی گئی ہو۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گندم کے دونوں آٹوں کے درمیان من کل وجہ مجانست بھی موجود ہے اور دونوں کے درمیان اتحاد قدر بھی
[Included in commentary]
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage deals with two sales: (1) flour for flour, and (2) flour for sattu. For flour-for-flour, the Hanafi school (and Ahmad) allow it equally by volume because both are the same jins and can be measured. Al-Shafi'i disputes this, arguing that flour compresses, so equal volume is impossible, thus it is invalid. The Hanafi response asserts that complete homogeneity and unity of measure exist. For flour-for-sattu, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa rules it invalid due to partial homogeneity and the analogy of prohibiting flour for roasted wheat, etc. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it valid because they consider flour and sattu different jins due to different purposes (one is raw flour for cooking, the other is roasted for instant consumption). The text argues that the primary purpose (nutrition) is shared, so they are not entirely different. The passage ends mid-argument, but it highlights the importance of considering the effective cause ('illa) in determining jins.

Key Terms
دقيق (daqīq): Flour, ground wheat.
سويق (sawīq): Sattu, roasted ground grain (often barley or wheat).
مقصود (maqsūd): Purpose or intended use of the item.
صاحبین (Sāhibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason for Abu Hanifa's ruling that selling flour for sattu is invalid?
A) Because flour and sattu are the same jins
B) Because sattu is a different genus from flour
C) Because the sale involves credit
D) Because the volume measure is uncertain

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two valid positions on selling flour for sattu: Abu Hanifa prohibits it due to partial homogeneity, while the Sahibayn permit it due to different purposes.

The Ruling on Selling Flour for Flour and for Sawiq: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Genus in Riba
Intra-Hanafi dispute on genus classification for riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on exchanging flour for sawiq and apply the criterion of genus (jins) and purpose (maqsud) to distinguish between permissible and impermissible riba-related transactions.

Core Idea
Flour and sawiq share the same origin but differ in purpose; the dispute hinges on whether purpose changes legal genus.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the agreed ruling on selling flour for flour by measure, then dives into a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits exchanging flour for sawiq, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it. The debate turns on a single question—are flour and sawiq of the same genus for riba purposes? Understanding how the Hanafi masters apply the concept of mujanasa (homogeneity) and the role of primary purpose will sharpen your ability to analyze similar commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
Start with the clear ruling: flour-for-flour is permissible if both are equal by measure. This sets the baseline for the subsequent dispute.
This ruling is undisputed in the Hanafi school; the Shafi'i objection is noted but overruled.
2
Locate the disputed case
The passage shifts to flour-for-sawiq. Note that both commodities derive from wheat, but their processing and usage differ. This is where the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf arises.
Sawiq is parched and ground; flour is raw ground wheat.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa uses two arguments: (1) analogy to fried vs. non-fried wheat (impermissible due to genus unity and density difference), and (2) since flour and sawiq are parts of those wheat types, homogeneity remains. The key is that partial homogeneity (mujanasa min wajh) is enough to trigger riba rules.
He considers the primary purpose (nutrition) as shared, making the minor purpose difference irrelevant.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that purpose (maqsud) determines genus. Flour is for baking, sawiq for drinking; thus they are different genera, so riba al-fadl does not apply and exchange with excess is permissible.
They focus on the secondary purposes (baking vs. drinking) rather than the overarching nutrition.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author of al-Hidayah rebuts the Sahibayn by asserting that the major purpose (nutrition) includes both, and partial loss of minor purposes is negligible, as in the case of fried vs. non-fried wheat.
This shows how the criterion of 'major purpose' is used in the Hanafi school to determine genus.

آٹے کی آٹے کے بدلے برابر برابر بیع کا حکم
ويجوز بيع الدقيق بالدقيق متساويا كيلا لتحقق الشرط وبيع الدقيق بالسويق لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة متفاضلاً ولا متساوياً لأنه لا يجوز بيع الدقيق بالمقلية ولا بيع السويق بالحنطة فكذا بيع أجزائهما لقيام المجانسة من وجه وعندهما يجوز؛ لأنهما جنسان مختلفان لاختلاف المقصود قلنا معظم المقصود وهو التغذى يشلهما ولايبالى بفوات البعض كالمقلية مع غير المقلية والعلكة بالمسوسة
ترجمہ اور آئے کو آنے کے عوض پیمانہ سے برابر کر کے بیچنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ شرط موجود ہے اور آنے کوستو کے عوض بیچنا ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نہ متفاضلاً جائز ہے اور نہ متساویا ، کیونکہ آٹے کو بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور نہ تو کو گندم کے عوض ( بیچنا جائز ہے ) پس اسی طرح ان کے اجزاء کی بیع ( جائز نہیں ہے) کیونکہ من وجہ مجانست موجود ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ آٹا اور ستو اختلاف مقصود کی وجہ سے دو مختلف جنس ہیں ۔ ہم جو ابدیں گے کہ سب سے بڑا مقصود یعنی غذا حاصل کرنا دونوں کو شامل ہے اور بعض مقصود کے فوت ہونے کا لحاظ نہیں کیا جائے گا جیسے بھونے ہوئے کی بیع بغیر بھونے ہوئے کے ساتھ اور عمدہ کی بیع گھنے ہوئے کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح مسئلہ ہمارے نزدیک پیمانے اور کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے آنے کی بیع آنے کے عوض جائز ہے یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ پیمانے سے برابر کرنے کے باوجود آنے کی بیع آنے کے عوض نا جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پیمانے اور کیل کے ذریعہ آنے کو برابر نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ آٹا پیمانے اور کیل میں ڈال کر بھینچنے سے پہنچ جاتا ہے یعنی دبانے سے دب جاتا ہے تو کیل کرنے کو باوجود پورے طور پر برابری متحقق نہ ہوگی اور جب برابری متحقق نہیں ہوئی تو برابری شنبه ر بوا کی وجہ سے آٹے کی بیچ آئے کے عوض نا جائز ہوگی اگر چہ کیل کیے ذریعہ برابری کی گئی ہو۔ ہماری دلیل .... یہ ہے کہ گندم کے دونوں آٹوں کے درمیان من کل وجہ مجانست بھی موجود ہے اور دونوں کے درمیان اتحاد قد ربھی
ہے۔ دونوں آئوں کی جنس کا ایک ہونا تو ظاہر ہے اور اتحاد قد ر اس لئے ہے کہ آٹا کیلی ہے کیونکہ لوگ آنے کی خرید و فروخت کیل ہی گئے ذریعہ کرتے ہیں اسی وجہ سے آنے کی بیع سلم کیل کے ذریعہ جائز ہے اور کیل کے ذریعہ آنا قرض لینا بھی جائز ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آنا کیلی ہے پس جب اتحاد جنس بھی ہے اور اتحاد قد ربھی ہے تو دونوں عوضوں میں یعنی کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کرنے کی صورت میں بیج جائز ہوگی اور یہاں یہی مسئلہ فرض کیا گیا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ علت رہوا پائے جانے کی صورت میں شرط جواز بیع مساوات اور برابری ہے اور یہاں یہ شرط موجود ہے۔ اسلئے کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے آنے کی بیچ آئے کے عوض جائز ہے۔ شیخ امام ابی بکر محمد بن فضل سے منقول ہے کہ اگر آٹا ، آنے کے عوض بیچا گیا اور کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کی گئی تو یہ بیچ اس وقت جائز ہوگی۔ جبکہ دونوں کیل خوب دبا دبا کر بھرے گئے ہوں کیونکہ اس صورت میں کمی زیادتی کا شبہ واقع نہ ہوگا۔ اور گندم کے آنے کی بیچ گندم کے ستو کے عوض حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نہ برابر کر کے جائز ہے اور نہ کی زیادتی کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔ البتہ صاحبین کے نزدیک مساویا اور متفاضلا دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔ چونکہ آنا بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے اجزاء ہیں اس لئے آئے اور ستو
The ruling of selling flour for flour equally: And it is permissible to sell flour for flour equally by measure because the condition is established; and selling flour for sawiq (parched barley/grain) is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, whether with excess or equally, because it is not permissible to sell flour for mashed (or fried) wheat, nor to sell sawiq for wheat, so likewise the sale of their parts (the flour derived from them) is impermissible due to the existence of partial homogeneity (mujanasa min wajh). According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible because they are two different genera due to difference in purpose. We say: the major purpose, which is nutrition, includes both, and the loss of some purpose is not considered, like the sale of fried (wheat) with non-fried, and premium with damaged. Explanation: According to us, selling flour for flour by measure equally is permissible. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i says that despite making them equal by measure, selling flour for flour is impermissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that flour cannot be made equal by measure because when poured and pressed, it compresses, so full equality is not achieved; and when equality is not achieved, due to the suspicion of riba, selling flour for flour is impermissible even if equalized by measure. Our proof is that between the two flours there is complete homogeneity (mujanasa min kulli wajh) and also equality in quantity (ittihad qadr) because flour is sold by measure (kayl) – people buy and sell flour by measure, so salam (advance sale) of flour by measure is permissible, and borrowing flour by measure is permissible. Thus it is known that flour is measured by volume. So when there is unity of genus and unity of measure, then selling one for the other with equal measure is permissible. And that is exactly the case here. In summary, when the cause of riba exists, the condition for permissible sale is equality, and here that condition is present. Therefore, selling flour for flour by equal measure is permissible. It is narrated from Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Fadl that if flour is sold for flour and equalized by measure, the sale is only permissible if both measures are filled with firm pressure (daba daba), because then no suspicion of excess remains. As for selling wheat flour for wheat sawiq, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible whether equal or with excess. However, according to the two companions, it is permissible both equally and with excess. The proof of the two companions is that wheat flour and its sawiq are two separate genera, even though their origin (wheat) is one. They are different in genus because their purposes differ: flour is used to make bread and halwa, which cannot be obtained from sawiq; sawiq is drunk or eaten mixed with ghee and sugar, which cannot be obtained from flour. Therefore, flour and sawiq are two separate genera, and when they are separate genera, selling one for the other both equally and with excess is permissible, because with difference in genus, selling with excess is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa argues for the impermissibility of selling flour for sawiq in two ways. The first: The sale of fried (parched) wheat for non-fried wheat is impermissible by consensus, whether equally or with excess. This impermissibility is because their genus is one and equality by measure is impossible, since non-fried wheat is denser, so in one measure fried wheat will be less and non-fried more. When equality is impossible and there is suspicion of excess, the sale is impermissible. Now, flour is parts of non-fried wheat, and sawiq is parts of fried wheat. It is also accepted that flour has nothing added to the wheat except that the parts have become separated; similarly, sawiq has no addition to fried wheat except that the parts have become separated. So when flour is parts of non-fried wheat and sawiq is parts of fried wheat, their genus is one, and after equalizing by measure, suspicion of excess remains because flour has more air, so if the same vessel is filled with sawiq, it will weigh less. Due to this suspicion of excess, selling flour for sawiq is impermissible according to Abu Hanifa. The second proof, which the author of al-Hidayah mentioned, is that selling flour for fried wheat and selling sawiq for non-fried wheat are impermissible. This impermissibility is solely because it entails riba al-fadl, and riba al-fadl is established by homogeneity (mujanasa). So homogeneity is established between sawiq and non-fried wheat. Since flour is parts of non-fried wheat, therefore (the same ruling applies to) flour and sawiq.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the rulings and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the exchange of flour (dough) for flour and for sawiq (parched grain). The passage begins by stating the agreed rule: selling flour for flour is permissible provided both are equal in measure, because the condition for avoiding riba (equality in genus and measure) is met. It then introduces the dispute over selling flour for sawiq. Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits it whether equal or with excess, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it. The reason for the dispute is whether flour and sawiq are considered the same genus (jins) for riba purposes. Abu Hanifa holds that partial homogeneity exists because both are derived from wheat, and the major purpose (nutrition) is the same; thus they share genus, and since equality by measure is uncertain due to density differences, the sale is invalid due to suspicion of riba. The Sahibayn argue that the different purposes (baking vs. drinking) make them separate genera, so equality is not required, and the sale is permissible even with excess. The passage also discusses the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who prohibits flour-for-flour sale even by measure because compaction makes precise equality impossible. The Hanafi response is that flour is legally a measured commodity (kayli), so equality by measure is valid as long as the measure is filled properly. A narration from Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Fadl states that if both measures are firmly packed, the sale is permissible. The passage concludes with Abu Hanifa's two proofs: one analogizing to the impermissible sale of fried for non-fried wheat, and the other arguing that since flour and sawiq are parts of these wheat types, and those wheat types are homogenous, homogeneity also exists between flour and sawiq. This is a detailed example of how Hanafi scholars apply the principles of riba al-fadl and the role of genus (jins) and measure (kayl) in determining valid transactions.

Key Terms
دقيق (daqiq): Flour or dough; in this context, flour made from wheat (or barley) that is sold by measure (kayl).
سويق (sawiq): Parched grain (usually barley or wheat) that is ground and can be eaten as a drink or mixed with ghee and sugar.
مجانسة (mujanasa): Homogeneity or genus similarity; used here to determine whether two items are of the same genus for riba purposes.
ربوا الفضل (riba al-fadl): Excess riba; the prohibition of exchanging same-genus commodities in unequal quantities when sold by measure or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is selling flour for sawiq impermissible even when both are measured equally?
A) Because flour and sawiq are from different genera so riba does not apply
B) Because they share partial genus and equality by measure is uncertain due to density differences
C) Because sawiq is not a measured commodity
D) Because it is prohibited by consensus of all schools

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, genus for riba is determined by essence and primary purpose; when primary purpose is shared, partial homogeneity triggers riba rules, making exchange impermissible unless equality is certain.
