Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Sale of Wheat Flour for Satto: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discusses the ruling on selling flour for satto with proof and rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on selling flour for satto, explain the Sahibayn's counterargument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf of this intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Flour and satto are same genus under Hanafi law; riba al-fadl makes exchange impermissible even if measured equally.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a classic dispute within the Hanafi school about whether wheat flour and wheat satto (coarse roasted wheat) belong to the same genus for riba purposes. Imam Abu Hanifa forbids the exchange due to density differences preventing true equality by measure, while the Sahibayn allow it based on different purposes. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the rules of riba al-fadl in commodity exchanges.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the exact legal question: whether flour and satto are the same genus for riba al-fadl.
2
Identify the Hanafi position
What does Imam Abu Hanifa rule and why? He forbids the sale even if equal by measure.
His proof uses qiyas to roasted/unroasted wheat.
3
Identify the opposing view
What do the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue and on what basis? They permit the sale equally or with disparity.
Their proof relies on difference in purpose (bread vs. drink).
4
Examine the proofs
Trace Abu Hanifa's two proofs: (1) analogy to roasted/unroasted wheat where measure equality is impossible due to density; (2) linking satto to roasted wheat and flour to unroasted, establishing common genus.
Also note the Sahibayn's proof based on different purposes.
5
Analyze the response
How does the text respond to the Sahibayn? It argues that both share the essential purpose of being food, and minor differences do not negate common genus, just as with roasted/unroasted wheat.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Abu Hanifa invalidates the sale, Sahibayn validate it.

نہ ہوگا۔ اور گندم کے آنے کی بیچ گندم کے ستو کے عوض حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نہ برابر کر کے جائز ہے اور نہ کی زیادتی کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔ البتہ صاحبین کے نزدیک مساویا اور متفاضلا دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گندم کا آٹا اور اس کا ستو دو جنس الگ الگ ہیں اگر چہ دونوں کی اصل یعنی گندم ایک ہے۔ اور ان دونوں کی جنس مختلف اس لئے ہے کہ دونوں کے مقصود میں اختلاف ہے کیونکہ آٹے سے روٹی پکاتے ہیں، پر اٹھا پکاتے ہیں اور یہ دونوں باتیں ساتو سے حاصل نہیں ہو سکتیں۔ اور ستو گھول کر کھاتے ہیں اور گھی اور شکر میں لت پت کر کے کھاتے ہیں اور یہ مقصد آئے سے حاصل نہیں ہو سکتا۔ حاصل یہ ہوا کہ آٹا اور ستو دو الگ الگ جنس ہیں اور جب دو الگ الگ جنس ہوئیں تو ان میں سے ایک کو دوسرے کے عوض برابر، برابر بھی جائز ہوگا اور کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ بیچنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہوتا ہے۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ [بيع] الدقيق بالسواق کے عدم جواز پر دو طریقہ سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ بھونے ہوئے گندم کی بیع بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض بالا تفاق متساویا بھی ناجائز ہے اور متفاضل بھی نا جائز ہے۔ اور یہ عدم جواز اس لئے ہے کہ ان دونوں کی جنس ایک ہے اور کیل کے ذریعہ بڑا بری پیدا کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے، کیونکہ بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم میں جو ٹھوس پن ہوتا ہے وہ بھونے ہوئے گندم میں نہیں ہوتا پس ایک کیل میں بھونا ہوا گندم کم آئے گا اور بغیر ہونا ہوا زائد آئے گا۔ اور جب ان دونوں میں مساوات ممکن نہیں ہے بلکہ کمی زیادتی کا شبہ ہے تو یہ بیع بھی نا جائز ہوگی ۔ اور آٹا بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے اجزاء ہیں اور سٹو بھونے ہوئے گندم کے اجزاء ہیں۔ اور یہ بات بھی مسلم ہے کہ آٹے میں گندم پر کسی چیز کا اضافہ نہیں ہوتا علاوہ اس کے کہ اجزاء مجتمع متفرق ہو گئے اس طرح ستو بھونے ہوئے گندم پر کوئی اضافہ نہیں ہوتا علاوہ اس کے کہ جو اجزاء یکجا تھے وہ متفرق ہو گئے۔ پس جب آٹا بغیر بھو نے گندم کے اجزاء ہیں اور ستو بھونے ہوئے گندم کے اجزاء ہیں تو ان دونوں کی جنس بھی ایک ہوگی اور کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کر دینے کے بعد کمی زیادتی کا شبہ باقی رہتا ہے کیونکہ [آٹے] میں یہ نسبت ستو کے ٹھوس پن زیادہ ہوتا ہے، تو جس برتن میں آنا بھرا گیا ہوا اگر اسی برتن میں ستو بھرا جائے تو [ستو] وزن کے اعتبار سے کم ہو جائے گا۔ اسی تفاضل کے شبہ کی وجہ سے آٹے کی بیع [سنتہ] کے عوض امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے۔ دوسری دلیل جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے بیان فرمایا ہے یہ ہے کہ [آٹے] کی بیچ بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض اور ستو کی بیج بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض نا جائز ہے اور یہ عدم جواز محض اس لئے ہے کہ یہ ربوا افضل کو مستلزم ہے اور ربوا الفضل مجانست سے ثابت ہوتا ہے تو ستو اور بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے درمیان مجانست ثابت ہوگئی اور چونکہ آنا بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے اجزاء ہیں اس لئے آئے اور ستو کے درمیان بھی مجانست ثابت ہو جائے گی اور آئے اور ستو کے درمیان کیل کے ذریعہ مساوات اور برابری کرنا چونکہ ناممکن ہے اس لئے آنے کی بیع ستو کے عوض متفاضلا بھی نا جائز ہے اور مقتسادیا بھی نا جائز ہے۔
صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آٹا اور سقو اعظم مقصود ہونے یعنی غذا ہونے میں دونوں شریک ہیں۔ یعنی آنے سے بھی غذا حاصل کی جاتی ہے اور ستو بھی غذا حاصل کی جاتی ہے، اور رہا بعضی چیزوں میں تفاوت تو وہ اتحاد جنس کیلئے مضر نہیں ہے۔ جیسے بھونے ہوئے گندم اور بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم میں کچھ نہ کچھ تفاوت کے بعد اتحاد جنس ہے۔ اور کھن لگے ہوئے گندم اور کھن نہ لگے ہوئے گندم میں کچھ نہ کچھ تفاوت کے باوجود اتحاد جنس ہے اسی طرح ستو اور آٹے کے درمیان بھی قدرے تفاوت کے باوجود اتحاد جنس ہے۔ اور جب اتحاد جنس ہے جس طرح بھونے ہوئے گندم کی بیع بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض اور عمدہ گندم کی بیچ کھن لگے ہوئے عوض متفاضلا اور متساویا دونوں طرح نا جائز ہے اسی طرح آٹے کی بیع ستو کے عوض متفاضل اور متساویا دونوں طرح نا جائز ہے۔
Book of Transactions. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary of Bidaya, volume six. It is apparent that the genus of both flours is one, and equality in measure is because flour is measured by volume, as people buy and sell flour by volume; due to this, salam sale of flour by volume is valid, and taking a loan of flour by volume is also valid. From this it is known that flour is measure-based. So when there is unity of genus and unity of measure, then between the two countervalues, i.e., when making equality by volume, the sale will be valid. And here this very issue is assumed. The conclusion is that when the cause of riba exists, the condition for validity of sale is equality, and here this condition is present. Therefore, selling flour for flour after making them equal by volume is valid. It is narrated from Shaykh Imam Abi Bakr Muhammad ibn Fadl that if flour is sold for flour and equality is made by volume, this sale will be valid when both volumes are filled by pressing down firmly, because in that case suspicion of increase or decrease will not occur. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling wheat flour for wheat satto is not valid whether equally or with excess. However, according to the Sahibayn, it is valid in both ways, equally and with disparity. The Sahibayn's proof is that wheat flour and its satto are two separate genera, even though their origin, wheat, is one. And their genus is different because their purposes differ: from flour bread is baked and roti is made, and these two things cannot be obtained from satto. And satto is consumed by mixing with water or by mixing with ghee and sugar, and this purpose cannot be obtained from flour. The conclusion is that flour and satto are two different genera, and when they are two different genera, then one may be sold for the other equally or with excess, because in case of difference of genus, selling with excess is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa proves the impermissibility of selling flour for satto in two ways. First: The sale of roasted wheat for unroasted wheat is impermissible by consensus, whether equally or with excess. And this impermissibility is because both are of the same genus and it is not possible to achieve equality by measure, because unroasted wheat has a solidity that roasted wheat does not have. Thus in one measure, roasted wheat will be less and unroasted will be more. And when equality is not possible between them, rather there is suspicion of increase or decrease, this sale is also impermissible. And flour is parts of unroasted wheat, and satto is parts of roasted wheat. And it is also accepted that flour has no addition to wheat except that its parts have become separated; similarly, satto has no addition to roasted wheat except that its parts which were together have become separated. So when flour is parts of unroasted wheat and satto is parts of roasted wheat, then both are of the same genus, and after making equality by measure, the suspicion of increase or decrease remains because in [flour] this proportion, the solidity of satto is more; so if the vessel in which flour was filled is filled with satto, it will weigh less. Due to this suspicion of disparity, selling flour for satto according to Imam Abu Hanifa is impermissible. The second proof that the author of Hidayah has mentioned is that selling [flour] for roasted wheat and selling satto for unroasted wheat is impermissible, and this impermissibility is purely because it entails riba al-fadl, and riba al-fadl is established by commonality of genus. So commonality of genus is established between satto and unroasted wheat, and since flour is parts of unroasted wheat, commonality of genus is also established between flour and satto. And since making equality by measure between flour and satto is impossible, selling flour for satto is impermissible whether with excess or equally.
The response to the Sahibayn's proof is that flour and satto share the great purpose, i.e., being food. That is, food is obtained from both flour and satto. As for differences in some things, they do not harm unity of genus. For example, between roasted and unroasted wheat there is some difference but unity of genus exists. And between wheat with husk and without husk, despite some difference, unity of genus exists. Similarly, between satto and flour, despite some difference, unity of genus exists. And when unity of genus exists, just as sale of roasted wheat for unroasted wheat and sale of good quality wheat for husked wheat is impermissible both with excess and equally, so too sale of flour for satto is impermissible both with excess and equally.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of wheat flour for wheat satto (coarsely ground roasted wheat). The author first establishes that plain flour is sold by volume (measure), so when selling flour for flour, equality by measure is required to avoid riba. The specific issue is whether flour and satto are considered the same genus. Imam Abu Hanifa holds they are the same genus (wheat), so riba al-fadl applies, and due to density differences, equal measure cannot guarantee actual equality, making such sale impermissible even if measured equally. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider flour and satto different genera because their purposes differ (flour for bread, satto for mixing), so sale is permissible both with equality and disparity. The author then provides Imam Abu Hanifa's two proofs: first, analogy to roasted/unroasted wheat where equality by measure is impossible; second, by showing that satto is analogous to roasted wheat, and flour to unroasted, thus establishing common genus and impermissibility. Finally, the response to the Sahibayn emphasizes that both are food, and minor differences do not negate common genus, just as with roasted/unroasted wheat or husked/unhusked wheat. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Imam Abu Hanifa's view, as it is preferred in the Hidayah and later fatwa collections.

Key Terms
آٹا (atta): Wheat flour, a staple food item sold by volume (measure).
ستو (satto): Coarsely ground roasted wheat, used as a food item mixed with water or ghee and sugar.
ربوا الفضل (riba al-fadl): Usury of excess, prohibited when exchanging same genus items with disparity in measure or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is selling wheat flour for wheat satto impermissible even if measured equally?
A) Because satto is a different genus due to its purpose
B) Because flour and satto have different densities, so equal measure does not guarantee actual equality, leading to riba
C) Because satto is not a food item
D) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade it

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, flour and satto are considered the same genus for riba purposes, making their exchange impermissible unless equal by weight—but since weight is not customary, such exchanges are prohibited.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Selling Meat for a Live Animal: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs (talil)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on selling meat for a live animal, explain the reasoning behind each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A live animal is not weighed; selling meat for it is generally permissible, but Imam Muhammad feared riba when the genus is the same.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about a specific exchange: selling butchered meat for a live animal of the same species. At first glance, this looks like bartering two food items, which could trigger riba al-fadl rules. However, the Hanafi masters diverge on whether the uncertainty in the animal's meat quantity matters. Understanding their reasoning sharpens our grasp of riba's scope and the role of custom (urf) in determining weight classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the parties
The issue is the validity of selling meat (a weighed item) for a live animal of the same genus (e.g., goat meat for a goat). The parties are Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (permissive) versus Imam Muhammad (restrictive).
The animal's meat is inside the carcass and cannot be precisely known.
2
State each position precisely
Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf: The sale is permissible without conditions, because a live animal is not customarily weighed (it is an unweighed item). Muhammad: The sale is permissible only if the meat being sold is clearly more than the meat inside the animal, so that the excess corresponds to non-meat parts and riba is avoided.
3
Analyze the proofs (talil)
Muhammad analogizes to selling oil for sesame seeds: both are derived from the same source, and an exact match is impossible, leading to riba. The two shaykhs argue that the animal's unweighed nature breaks the analogy; it is like selling a weighed item for an unweighed one, which is not riba.
The proof of the two shaykhs relies on custom (urf) – animals are sold by head, not weight.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: Under Muhammad, the sale is invalid unless the meat is more; under the majority, it is always valid. The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (general permissibility).
The commentary further explains that selling meat of a different genus (e.g., beef for goat) is unanimously permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گوشت کی حیوان کے بدلے بیع کا حکم، اقوال فقہاء
قال ويجوز بيع اللحم بالحيوان عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد إذا باعه بلحم من جنسه لا يجوز إلا إذا كان اللحم المفرز أكثر ليكون اللحم بمقابلة ما فيه من اللحم والباقى بمقابلة السقط إذ لو لم يكن كذالك يتحقق الريامن حيث زيادة السقط ومن حيث زيادة اللحم فصار كالحل بالسمسم ولهما أنه باع الموزون بما ليس بموزون؛ لأن الحيوان لايوزن عادة ولا يمكن معرفة ثقله بالوزن؛ لأنه يخفف نفسه مرة ويثقل أخرى بخلاف تلك المسالة ؛ لأن الوزن فى الحال يعرف قدر الدهن إذا ميز بينه وبين الثجير ويوزن الثجير
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک گوشت کو زندہ جاندار کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب حیوان کو اسی کی جنس کے گوشت کے عوض فروخت کیا تو جائز نہیں ہے جبکہ جانور سے الگ کیا ہوا گوشت (اس سے) زیادہ ہو جتنا حیوان میں ہے تا کہ گوشت ( کا ایک حصہ ) اس گوشت کے مقابل ہو جو حیوان میں ہے اور باقی حیوان کے اجزاء کے مقابلہ میں ہو۔ اسلئے کہ اگر ایسا نہ ہوا تو ر بو امتحقق ہوگا۔ حیوان کے اجزاء کی زیادتی کے اعتبار سے اور گوشت کی زیادتی کے اعتبار سے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے تل کے عوض میں تیل ہوتا ہے اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے موزونی چیز کو ایسی چیز کے عوض بیچا ہے جو موزونی نہیں اسلئے کہ جانور کو عادہ وزن نہیں کیا جاتا ہے اور وزن کے ذریعہ اس کے بوجھ کو پہچانا بھی ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ بھی اپنے آپ کو ہانکا کر لیتا ہے اور بھی بھاری کر لیتا ہے برخلاف اس مسئلہ کے کیونکہ وزن کرنے سے فی الحال تیل کی مقدار پہچان لی جائے گی، جبکہ نیل اور کھلی کو الگ الگ کر لیا جائے اور کھلی وزن کی جاتی ہے۔
تشریح گوشت کو جانور کے عوض بیچنے کی چند صورتیں ہیں۔
ایہ کہ گوشت اس کی جنس کے علاوہ جانور کے عوض فروخت کیا مثلاً گائے کا گوشت بکری کے عوض فروخت کیا تو یہ بالا تفاق جائز ہے خواہ بکری کے اندر کا گوشت گائے کے گوشت سے زیادہ ہو خواہ برابر ہو خواہ کم ہو جیسا کہ مختلف الاجناس گوشت کی بیع قلت و کثرت کا
Ruling on selling meat for a live animal, statements of jurists. He said: Selling meat for a live animal is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: If he sells it for meat of its own genus, it is not permissible unless the meat separated is more, so that the meat (portion) corresponds to the meat within the animal, and the remaining corresponds to the waste. If it were not so, riba would occur due to increase in waste or increase in meat. Thus it becomes like (selling) oil for sesame seeds. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), he sold a weighed item for something not weighed, because a live animal is not customarily weighed, and its weight cannot be known by weighing because it lightens itself sometimes and becomes heavy at other times, unlike that issue (oil and sesame) because by weighing, the amount of fat can be known at once when it is distinguished from the pulp, and the pulp is weighed. Translation: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, selling meat for a live animal is valid. And Imam Muhammad said: When an animal is sold for meat of its own genus, it is not valid unless the meat separated from the animal is more than (the meat within) so that one portion of meat corresponds to the meat in the animal and the rest corresponds to the parts of the animal. Because if it were not so, riba would occur due to excess of animal parts or excess of meat. So it becomes like oil in exchange for sesame seeds. The proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that he sold a weighed item for something not weighed, because a live animal is not customarily weighed and its weight cannot be known by weighing, as it sometimes lightens itself and sometimes becomes heavy, unlike that issue because by weighing, the amount of oil is known at once when the oil is separated from the pulp, and the pulp is weighed. Explanation: There are several forms of selling meat for an animal. First: Meat is sold for an animal of a different genus, e.g., beef sold for a goat. This is permissible by consensus, whether the meat inside the goat is more than the beef, equal, or less, just as the sale of meat of different genera, regardless of quantity.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on selling meat for a live animal. The core ruling: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider such sale permissible in general, because a live animal is not considered a weighed item (mawzun) customarily, so it falls under items sold by count or estimation. Imam Muhammad restricts this: if the animal is sold for meat of its own genus (e.g., goat meat for a goat), then it is only valid if the meat being sold is clearly more than the meat within the animal, so that the excess meat corresponds to the animal's non-meat parts (bones, skin, etc.). This avoids riba al-fadl, which would occur if there was uncertainty about equality. Muhammad's analogy is to selling oil for sesame seeds: oil is derived from sesame, and you cannot exchange them without knowing the exact proportions. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that since the animal is not customarily weighed, the sale is of a weighed item for an unweighed one, which is permissible in such cases. The commentary then lists scenarios: selling meat for a different species animal (e.g., beef for goat) is unanimously permissible regardless of quantity. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, allowing the sale of meat for a live animal generally, with Muhammad's restriction being a cautionary view.

Key Terms
لحم (lahm): Meat, specifically butchered meat separated from the animal.
حيوان (hayawan): A live animal, considered an unweighed item customarily because its weight fluctuates.
موزون (mawzun): An item that is sold and traded by weight, such as meat, oil, etc.
سقط (saqt): Waste, here referring to the non-meat parts of the animal (bones, skin, offal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, selling meat for a live animal of the same genus is:
A) Always invalid due to riba
B) Valid only if the meat is more than the animal's meat
C) Valid without any condition
D) Valid only if the animal is weighed first

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, selling meat for a live animal is generally permissible because the animal is not treated as a weighed item, though Imam Muhammad required the meat to be more to avoid riba - the majority view is followed in fatwa.

The Sale of Flour for Sattu: Hanafi Position and Response to Sahibayn
Hanafi ruling and response to Sahibayn's proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of flour for barley grits and explain why the Sahibayn's objection based on impossibility of equalization does not break the unity of genus.

Core Idea
Genus unity of food items overrides impossibility of precise measure in riba-prohibited sales.

In this passage, we examine a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the sale of flour (aata) for barley grits (sattu). The relied-upon position holds that such a sale is invalid because both are foodstuffs of the same genus. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argued that since equalization by measure is impossible, the sale should be valid. The commentator refutes this by establishing that minor differences do not break genus unity, using clear analogies from wheat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the passage addresses the sale of flour for barley grits and that there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on its validity.
The ruling is about riba al-fadl in food items.
2
Understand the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the sale is invalid whether equal or unequal, because both items share unity of genus as food.
Genus unity is determined by the primary purpose (food) rather than minor differences.
3
Recognize the Sahibayn's argument
The Sahibayn argued that because equalization by measure (kayl) is impossible, the sale should be valid, implying they considered the items as different genera.
This argument relies on the practical difficulty of precise measurement.
4
Follow the Hanafi response using analogies
The commentator rebuts by showing that minor differences (roasted/unroasted, clean/unclean) do not break genus unity, using analogies from wheat.
These analogies are qiyas jaliy, demonstrating that genus remains intact despite variation.
5
Derive the practical outcome
Conclude that the sale of flour for barley grits is invalid in all cases, and the mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that the Sahibayn's view would allow the sale, but it is not relied upon.

Source Text

کتاب البیوع
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم کے درمیان بھی مجانست ثابت ہو جائے گی اور آٹے اور ستو کے درمیان کیل کے ذریعہ مساوات اور برابری کرنا چونکہ ناممکن ہے اس لئے آٹے کی بیع ستو کے عوض متفاضلا بھی نا جائز ہے اور متساویا بھی نا جائز ہے۔
صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آٹا اور ستو اعظم مقصود ہونے یعنی غذا ہونے میں دونوں شریک ہیں۔ یعنی آٹے سے بھی غذا حاصل کی جاتی ہے اور ستو سے بھی غذا حاصل کی جاتی ہے، اور رہا بعضی چیزوں میں تفاوت تو وہ اتحاد جنس کے لئے مضر نہیں ہے۔ جیسے بھونے ہوئے گندم اور بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم میں کچھ نہ کچھ تفاوت کے باوجود اتحاد جنس ہے۔ اور کھن لگے ہوئے گندم اور کھن نہ لگے ہوئے گندم میں کچھ نہ کچھ تفاوت کے باوجود اتحاد جنس ہے اسی طرح ستو اور آٹے کے درمیان بھی قدرے تفاوت کے باوجود اتحاد جنس ہے۔ اور جب اتحاد جنس ہے جس طرح بھونے ہوئے گندم کی بیع بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض اور عمدہ گندم کی بیچ کھن لگے ہوئے عوض متفاضلا اور متساویا دونوں طرح نا جائز ہے اسی طرح آٹے کی بیع ستو کے عوض متفاضل اور متساویا دونوں طرح نا جائز ہے۔
Book of Sales. In the middle of Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu sharh of Hidayah, volume eight, homogeneity (mujanasat) is also established. And since equalization by measure between flour and barley grits is impossible, therefore the sale of flour in exchange for barley grits is invalid whether unequal or equal. The answer to the proof of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that flour and barley grits share the greatest purpose, i.e., being food. That is, from flour food is obtained and from barley grits food is also obtained. As for the difference in some aspects, it does not harm the unity of genus. Just as there is unity of genus between roasted wheat and unroasted wheat despite some difference, and between unclean wheat and clean wheat despite some difference, similarly between barley grits and flour there is unity of genus despite some difference. And when there is unity of genus, just as the sale of roasted wheat in exchange for unroasted wheat and the sale of fine wheat in exchange for unclean wheat is invalid both unequally and equally, similarly the sale of flour in exchange for barley grits is invalid both unequally and equally.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of flour (aata) for barley grits (sattu). The relied-upon position (likely Abu Hanifa) is that such a sale is invalid because both are staple foods of the same genus. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argued that the sale could be valid because equalization by measure is impossible, implying that the two items are of different genera. The author refutes this by demonstrating that despite minor differences (roasted/unroasted, clean/unclean), unity of genus remains. Thus, the prohibition of riba applies, and the sale is invalid whether equal or unequal.

Key Terms
اتحاد جنس (ittihad al-jins): Unity of genus; two items belonging to the same species in the context of riba.
ربوا (riba): Usury or prohibited increase in exchange.
کیل (kayl): Measure by volume or similar standard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Valid equally, invalid unequally
B) Invalid both equally and unequally
C) Valid both equally and unequally
D) Valid only if measured by volume

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits the sale of flour for barley grits in any amount because they belong to the same genus of food, and the impossibility of exact measurement does not negate genus unity.

Selling Meat for a Live Animal: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling meat for a live animal of the same species, with scenario elaboration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four scenarios of selling meat for an animal, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the sale of meat for a live animal of the same species, and state the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit selling meat for a live animal unconditionally; Muhammad requires the meat to exceed the animal's meat content.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents an internal disagreement among the three senior Hanafi imams regarding the permissibility of bartering meat for a live animal of the same species. The commentator first presents the positions and proofs of the two sides, then elaborates four distinct scenarios of meat-for-animal transactions, highlighting where the dispute applies. Understanding this dispute deepens your appreciation of how Hanafi usul principles (especially riba conditions) operate in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and the four scenarios
List the four scenarios of meat-for-animal sale: different species, same species slaughtered and separated, same species slaughtered not separated, same species live. Note which are disputed.
The fourth scenario (live animal of same species) is the disputed case between the two.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that selling meat for a live animal is permissible in all cases, whether the meat is more, equal, or less. Their proof: meat is weighable (mawzun), live animal is not weighable due to constant weight change, so no riba concern. They also argue genus difference: meat is insentient, animal is sentient.
Key principle: when items differ in genus or measure, equality of quantity is not required.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
Muhammad restricts permissibility to when the separated meat is greater than the animal's meat content. His proof: analogy to oil for sesame seeds, where excess oil corresponds to the residue; otherwise riba arises. He argues that the animal's non-meat parts constitute an extra without countervalue if meat is equal or less.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on the common feature of genus unity.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Muhammad's analogy
The two distinguish the oil case because both oil and sesame are weighable, while here the live animal is not weighable. Hence the requirement of equality of quantity (ittihad al-qadr) does not apply. Additionally, the genus difference breaks the analogy.
This response highlights the importance of illa (effective cause) in qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: according to the two, the sale is always valid; according to Muhammad, valid only if meat exceeds the animal's meat. The author (Ashraf al-Hidayah) relies on the position of the two, making it the operative ruling for fatwa.
Thus in practice, selling meat for a live animal of the same species is unconditionally permissible.

بالارادہ ہے اور اتحاد جنس فوت ہونے کی صورت میں بھی بیع متفاضلا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے گوشت کی بیع اس کے ہم جنس زندہ جانور کے عوض جائز ہے گوشت خواہ زندہ جانور کے گوشت سے زیادہ ہو خواہ برابر ہو خواہ کم ہو۔ برخلاف تل اور اس کے تیل کے کیونکہ فی الحال تل کا وزن کرنے سے تیل کی مقدار پہچان لی جائے گی جبکہ تیل اور کھلی کو الگ کر لیا جائے۔
Ruling on selling meat for an animal, statements of the jurists. He said: The sale of meat for an animal is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: If he sells it for meat of its own genus, it is not permissible unless the separated meat is more (than what is in the animal), so that the meat (portion) corresponds to the meat in the animal, and the remainder corresponds to the non-meat parts. Because if it is not like that, riba would occur due to the increase in non-meat parts and due to the increase in meat. So it becomes like (the case of) sesame oil for sesame seeds. And for them (the two: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that he sold a weighed item for something not weighed, because an animal is not usually weighed, and its weight cannot be known by weighing because it lightens itself sometimes and becomes heavier at other times, unlike that other case (of oil and sesame), because there the amount of oil can be known by weighing when the oil and the residue are separated and the residue is weighed. Translation: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, selling meat for a live animal is permissible. Imam Muhammad said: When an animal is sold in exchange for meat of its own genus, it is not permissible unless the separated meat is more than the meat in the animal, so that one portion of the meat corresponds to the meat in the animal, and the remainder corresponds to the other parts of the animal. Because if it is not so, riba would be realized due to the increase in the animal's parts and due to the increase in meat. Thus it becomes like oil in exchange for sesame. And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that he sold a weighed item for an item that is not weighed, because an animal is not customarily weighed, and its weight cannot be known through weighing because it lightens itself sometimes and becomes heavy at other times, unlike that case because by weighing the amount of oil can be known at the moment when the oil and the residue are separated and the residue is weighed. Elaboration on the scenarios of selling meat for an animal: First scenario: Meat sold for an animal of a different species, e.g., cow meat for a goat: this is unanimously permissible, whether the meat in the goat is more, equal, or less than the cow meat, just as the sale of meat of different species is permissible without regard to quantity. Second scenario: Meat sold for an animal of the same species and the animal is slaughtered and separated from its skin and other parts: this is also unanimously permissible provided the two countervalues are equal in weight; if not equal, it is impermissible. Third scenario: Meat sold for a slaughtered animal of the same species but the animal has not been separated from its skin and parts: e.g., goat meat for a slaughtered goat not skinned: this is impermissible unless the meat is more than the meat in the slaughtered goat. Fourth scenario: Meat sold for a live animal of the same species: e.g., goat meat for a live goat: according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), this is permissible whether the meat is equal to the meat in the live animal or not. Imam Muhammad said: If the separated goat meat is more than the meat in the live goat, then it is permissible; otherwise it is impermissible. Imam Muhammad's proof: If the separated meat is more than the live goat's meat, e.g., fifty kg of separated meat and the goat yields forty kg of meat after slaughter, the thirty kg corresponds to the meat in the goat, and the remaining ten kg corresponds to the skin and other parts (head, legs, etc.). Thus no riba or suspicion of riba arises. But if the separated meat is not more, i.e., equal or less, then riba is realized. Because if equal, the meat and the animal's meat are equal, and the remaining parts (skin etc.) are extra, and in both cases there is riba. So if the meat is in excess, it is permissible; otherwise not. This is like the case of oil for sesame seeds: if the oil is more than the oil content in the sesame, it is permissible, so that oil corresponds to oil and the excess oil corresponds to the residue; otherwise it is impermissible. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that meat is Weighable (mawzun), and its sale and purchase is by weight, while an animal is not Weighable. It is not customarily weighed, and the weight of a live animal cannot be known because it sometimes lightens itself and sometimes becomes heavier, so it cannot be determined whether the goat has made itself light or heavy. In any case, selling meat for a goat is selling a Weighable item for a non-Weighable item, so there is no equality of quantity (ittihad qadr) between meat and the goat. And it has passed earlier that when there is no equality of quantity, the sale is permissible whether equal or unequal. Moreover, if you reflect, you will find that there is no unity of genus between meat and a live goat, because meat is insentient and the live goat is sentient, moving by free will. And when unity of genus is absent, the sale is permissible even if unequal. Therefore, the sale of meat for a live animal of the same genus is permissible, whether the meat is more, equal, or less than the animal's meat. Unlike the case of sesame and its oil, because by weighing the sesame at the moment, the amount of oil can be known when the oil and the residue are separated.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of meat in exchange for a live animal of the same species. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the 'two' or 'shaykhayn') hold that the sale is permissible in all cases, whether the meat is more, equal, or less than the animal's meat content. Their reasoning is that meat is a weighable (mawzun) commodity, while a live animal is not weighable due to its constant change in weight, so there is no equality of quantity (ittihad al-qadr) required to trigger riba. Moreover, they argue that the genus of meat and a live animal differs because one is insentient and the other is sentient with free will. Imam Muhammad, however, restricts permissibility to cases where the separated meat is greater than the meat content of the animal. He draws an analogy to the case of oil in exchange for sesame seeds: the sale is permissible only if the oil exceeds the oil content of the seeds, so that the excess oil corresponds to the residue. For Muhammad, if the meat is equal or less, riba occurs because the animal's non-meat parts (skin, bones, etc.) constitute an extra without countervalue. The text elaborates on four scenarios, with third and fourth being disputed. The dominant position relied upon for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as the author concludes by emphasizing their proof.

Key Terms
موزونی (mawzun): Weighable commodity; an item customarily sold by weight.
غیر موزونی (ghayr mawzun): Non-weighable; an item not customarily traded by weight, such as a live animal.
اتحاد قدر (ittihad al-qadr): Equality of quantity/measure in a transaction to avoid riba.
ربوا (riba): Usury or prohibited excess in exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two), selling goat meat for a live goat is:
A) Impermissible unless the meat is more than the animal's meat
B) Permissible in all cases regardless of quantity
C) Permissible only if the meat equals the animal's meat in weight
D) Impermissible in all cases

Key Takeaway
The default Hanafi position (mufta bihi) permits selling meat for a live animal of the same species unconditionally, as the live animal is not weighable and differs in genus from meat.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Selling Meat for a Live Animal: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on meat-for-live-animal sale with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on selling meat for a live animal of the same species and explain the reasoning behind each view using the concepts of mawzūnī, ghayr mawzūnī, ittihād qadr, and ittihād jins.

Core Idea
Meat is weighable; a live animal is not — so no riba, sale is permissible unconditionally.

The sale of meat for a live animal of the same species raises questions of riba: are they of the same genus and measure? Two positions exist within the Hanafi school. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permit it unconditionally, while Imam Muhammad restricts it to cases where the meat exceeds the estimated meat in the live animal. Each side uses rigorous legal reasoning. This lesson dissects the arguments and identifies the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule the sale permissible regardless of weight equality. Imam Muhammad rules it permissible only if the meat exceeds the meat in the live animal.
Imam Muhammad's condition is based on qiyas.
2
Identify the opponent's proof
Imam Muhammad draws an analogy with sesame seeds and oil: if oil is not more than the oil in seeds, riba occurs. Similarly, if meat is not more than the meat in the live animal, the non-meat parts become extra, leading to riba.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The two Shaykhs argue that a live animal is non-weighable (ghayr mawzūnī), so no unity of measure exists. Also, the live animal is sensible (self-moving), so no unity of genus. Hence, riba does not apply.
They rely on the custom of not weighing live animals.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: according to the two Shaykhs, the sale is valid even if the meat is less; according to Imam Muhammad, it is invalid unless the meat is more.
Mufta bihi follows the two Shaykhs.

That meat was sold in exchange for an animal of its own kind. For example: goat meat sold in exchange for a goat, but that goat is slaughtered and its skin and other parts have been separated from it – this is also permissible by consensus, provided that both countervalues are equal in weight, and if they are not equal then it is not permissible. That meat was sold in exchange for a slaughtered animal of its same species, but the animal has not been separated from its skin and parts. For example: goat meat sold in exchange for a slaughtered goat, and the slaughtered goat has not been separated from its skin and its limbs, hands, feet etc. – then this case is impermissible unless the meat is more than the meat that is in the slaughtered goat. 4. Meat sold in exchange for a live animal of its same species, e.g., goat meat sold in exchange for a live goat: according to the two Shaykhs this case is permissible, whether the meat is equal to the meat in the live animal or not. And Imam Muhammad said: If the separated goat meat is more than the meat in the live goat, then it is permissible; otherwise it is not permissible. Imam Muhammad's proof: If the separated meat is more than the meat in the live goat, e.g., the separated goat meat is 50 kg, and after slaughtering the live goat 40 kg of meat came out – then this case is permissible because the 40 kg of meat of the live goat will be in exchange for the 40 kg of separated meat, and the remaining 10 kg of meat will be in exchange for the goat's skin and other parts like head, trotters, etc. And in this case no riba or suspicion of riba occurs. But if the separated meat is not more than the live goat's meat, but equal or less, then riba is realized. Because if the separated meat is equal to the meat in the live goat, then this meat and the live goat's meat are equal, and the remaining parts of the goat like skin etc. are extra, and in both these cases there is riba. Therefore, if the meat is more than the meat in the live goat, then it is permissible; otherwise not. And this is like the case of sesame seeds and their oil: if the oil is more than the oil in the sesame seeds, then it is permissible so that oil is in exchange for oil, and the extra oil is in exchange for the oil cake; otherwise if the oil is equal to or less than the oil in the sesame seeds, then the sale is not permissible. The proof of the two Shaykhs: Meat is weighable (mawzuni), its purchase and sale are done by weight, and an animal is non-weighable (ghayr mawzuni); customarily it is not weighed, and it is not possible to recognize the weight of a live animal because sometimes it makes itself light and sometimes heavy, so it cannot be known whether the goat has made its weight light or heavy. In any case, selling meat in exchange for a goat is selling a weighable thing in exchange for a non-weighable thing, so there is no unity of measure (ittihad qadr) between meat and goat, and it has previously passed that when there is no unity of measure, sale is permissible both equally and with disparity. And if you reflect, you will know that between meat and a live goat there is also no unity of genus (ittihad jins) because meat is insensible and a live goat is sensible, self-moving. And when unity of genus is absent, sale with disparity is permissible. Therefore, the sale of meat in exchange for a live animal of its same genus is permissible whether the meat is more than the meat of the live animal, equal, or less. Contrary to sesame seeds and their oil, because at present by weighing the sesame seeds the quantity of oil can be recognized, when the oil and the oil cake are separated, because the oil cake is a thing that is weighed. For example, a quintal (100 kg) of sesame seeds, but when oil is extracted from them and the oil cake is removed, the oil cake became 600 grams, so it is known that the oil is 400 grams. Therefore, in this case the oil must be more than the oil in the sesame seeds so that oil is in exchange for oil and the excess oil is in exchange for the oil cake.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on selling meat in exchange for a live animal of the same species. The text presents three scenarios: 1) Meat sold for a slaughtered animal separated from skin and parts – permissible only if equal in weight. 2) Meat sold for a slaughtered animal not separated – impermissible unless meat exceeds the animal's meat. 3) Meat sold for a live animal – the central dispute. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) deem it permissible unconditionally because they consider the live animal non-weighable (ghayr mawzuni) and lacking unity of genus with meat. Imam Muhammad restricts permissibility to cases where the separated meat exceeds the estimated meat in the live animal, drawing an analogy with sesame seeds and oil. Each position is supported by detailed proofs. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position according to later Hanafi authorities is the view of the two Shaykhs, as reflected in many fatawa.

Key Terms
موزونی (mawzūni): A commodity that is customarily sold by weight, such as meat.
غیر موزونی (ghayr mawzūni): A commodity not customarily sold by weight, such as live animals.
اتحاد قدر (ittihād qadr): Unity of measure – when both countervalues are of the same type (e.g., both weighable) and thus must be equal to avoid riba.
اتحاد جنس (ittihād jins): Unity of genus – both items belong to the same category (e.g., edible items of same type).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because both are of the same genus, so equality is required.
B) Because the live animal is non-weighable and meat is weighable, so no unity of measure.
C) Because the buyer and seller agree to it.
D) Because Imam Muhammad allowed it.

Key Takeaway
The sale of meat for a live animal of the same species is unconditionally permissible according to the relied-upon Hanafi position because a live animal is non-weighable, eliminating riba concerns.

Selling Fresh Dates for Dried Dates: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on equal exchange of fresh and dried dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on selling rutab for tamr equal for equal, analyze the proofs, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits equal exchange of fresh and dried dates; Sahibayn forbid it based on a weak hadith.

This passage presents an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the sale of fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) in equal measure. Understanding the proof structure and the tarjih is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi fiqh in date transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa permits selling fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) equal for equal; the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) forbid it.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute, not between madhhabs.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's dalil
The Sahibayn rely on a hadith where the Prophet asked if fresh dates shrink when dried. When told yes, he forbade the equal exchange. Understand the implication: if shrinkage occurs, equal exchange hides a potential riba al-fadl.
This hadith is narrated via a weak chain.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa uses two hadiths: (1) The Prophet called fresh dates from Khaybar 'tamr,' indicating they are the same genus; (2) The Prophet said 'When the two types differ, sell however you wish.' He argues that if rutab and tamr are different types, the exchange is permitted without equality.
These hadiths are considered stronger in chain.
4
Evaluate the weakness of the Sahibayn's hadith
The chain of the Sahibayn's hadith goes through Zayd ibn 'Ayyash, who is classified as a weak narrator by hadith critics. This weakness allows Abu Hanifa to set aside that hadith.
This is a methodological point: weak hadith cannot override stronger evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, equal exchange is valid; according to Sahibayn, it is invalid (riba). The later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Al-Marghinani) prefer Abu Hanifa's view, and the fatwa today is on permissibility.
This tarjih is also supported by agreement of the other three imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad).

Source Text

تر کھجور کی خشک کھجور کیساتھ برابر برابر بیع جائز ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
قال ويجوز بيع الرطب بالتمر مثلاً بمثل عند أبي حنيفة وقالا لايجوز لقوله عليه السلام حين سئل عنه أو ينقص إذا جف فقيل نعم فقال لا إذا له أن الرطب تمر لقوله عليه السلام حين أهدى إليه رطبا أو كل تمر خيبر هكذا سماه تمرا وبيع التمر بمثله جائز لما روينا ولأنه لو كان تمرا جاز البيع بأول الحديث وإن كان غير تمر فباخره وهو قوله عليه السلام إذا اختلف النوعان قبيعوا كيف شئتم ومدار ما روياه على زيد ابن عياش وهو ضعيف عند النقلة
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک پختہ تازے چھوارے کو پختہ خشک چھوارے کے عوض برابر برابر بیچنا جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ جس وقت تازہ چھوارے کے بارے میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے دریافت کیا گیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ کیا تازہ چھوارہ خشک ہو کر کھٹ جاتا ہے تو عرض کیا گیا کہ ہاں۔ پس رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا تو جائز نہیں ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رطب ( تازہ چھوارے) بھی تمر ہے کیونکہ جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس خیبر کے رطب ( تازہ چھوارے ) ہدیہ بھیجے گئے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ کیا خیبر کے کل تمر ایسے ہی ہیں۔ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے را کوتر فر مایا اور تم کو مر کے عوض برابر برابر بیچنا حدیث مذکور کی وجہ سے جائز ہے ، اور اس لئے کہ رطب اگر تمر ہے تب تو اول حدیث کی وجہ سے بیع جائز ہے اور اگر غیر تمر ہے تو آخر حدیث کی وجہ سے جائز ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جب دو نوع مختلف ہوں تو جس طرح چاہو فروخت کرو۔ اور جو حدیث صاحبین نے روایت کی ہے اس کا مدار زید بن عیاش پر ہے اور وہ ناقلین حدیث کے نزدیک ضعیف راوی ہیں۔ تشریح طلب، پختہ تازہ چھوارے کو کہتے ہیں جس کو اردو زبان میں کھجور کہتے ہیں اور تمر پختہ خشک چھوارے کو کہتے ہیں جب چھوارہ بولا جاتا ہے تو یہی مفہوم مراد ہوتا ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ رطب کی بیع تمر کے عوض متفاضلا یعنی کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ بالا جماع نا جائز ہے اور متساویا یعنی برابر ، برابر حضرت ابو حنیفہ کے بزدیک تو جائز ہے البتہ صاحبین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے۔ حضرت امام مالک، امام شافعی، امام احمد بھی جواز کے قائل ہیں ۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک بار رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم سے بیع الرطب بالتمر مثلاً بمثل کے بارے میں دریافت کیا گیا کہ یہ جائز ہے یا نہیں تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پوچھا کہ کیا ر طب یعنی تازہ چھوارہ خشک ہو کر گھٹ جاتا ہے لوگوں نے جواب میں عرض کیا کہ ہاں گھٹ جاتا ہے اس پر آپ نے فرمایا کہ اگر یہ بات ہے تو پھر رطب کی بیع تمر کے عوض برابر، برابر نا جائز ہے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیج الرطب بالتمر برابر برابر بھی نا جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل نقلی یہ ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ مدنی آقاصلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں خیبر کے رطب یعنی تازہ چھوارے ہدیہ پیش
Fresh dates with dried dates equal for equal sale, is it permissible? Statements of jurists.
He said: Selling fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) equal for equal is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible, because of his statement (peace be upon him) when asked about it: 'Does it decrease when it dries?' They said: 'Yes.' He said: 'No, then.' And because fresh dates are dates (tamr) according to his statement (peace be upon him) when fresh dates from Khaybar were gifted to him: 'Are all the dates of Khaybar like this?' Thus he called it dates (tamr). And selling dates for their equivalent is permissible according to what we narrated. And if it were dates, the sale is permissible by the first hadith; and if it were not dates, then by the latter part, which is his statement: 'When the two types differ, then sell however you wish.' And the chain of what they narrated depends on Zayd ibn 'Ayyash, and he is weak according to the transmitters.
Translation: According to Abu Hanifa, selling ripe fresh dates in exchange for ripe dried dates equal for equal is permissible. The two Sahibayn said it is not permissible, because when the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked about fresh dates, he said: 'Does the fresh date diminish when it dries?' They replied: 'Yes.' Then the Messenger of Allah said: 'Then it is not permissible.' And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that rutab (fresh dates) is also tamr (dried dates), because when fresh dates from Khaybar were sent as a gift to the Messenger of Allah, he said: 'Are all the dates (tamr) of Khaybar like this?' The Messenger called rutab as tamr. And selling tamr for its equivalent is permissible due to the mentioned hadith. And also, if rutab is tamr, then by the first hadith the sale is permissible; and if it is not tamr, then by the latter hadith it is permissible, and that is his statement: 'When the two types differ, then sell however you wish.' And the hadith that the two Sahibayn narrated is based on Zayd ibn 'Ayyash, who is a weak narrator according to the hadith scholars.
Explanation: Rutab refers to ripe fresh dates, which in Urdu are called khajur; and tamr refers to ripe dried dates. When the word 'chhuara' (date) is used, this same meaning is intended. The issue is: Selling rutab in exchange for tamr with disparity (i.e., with increase or decrease) is impermissible by consensus. As for equal for equal, according to Abu Hanifa it is permissible, but according to the two Sahibayn it is impermissible. Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad also hold it permissible. The proof of the two Sahibayn is that once the Messenger of Allah was asked about selling fresh dates for dried dates equal for equal: is it permissible? He asked: 'Does the fresh date, when it dries, decrease?' People answered: 'Yes, it decreases.' Then he said: 'If that is the case, then selling fresh dates for dried dates equal for equal is impermissible.' From this hadith it is known that selling rutab for tamr equal for equal is also impermissible. The transmitted proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that once the people of Madinah presented fresh dates from Khaybar as a gift to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) in equal measure. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, such a sale is permissible because rutab is a type of tamr, as evidenced by the Prophet calling Khaybar dates 'tamr'. Thus, selling tamr for tamr equally is allowed. Additionally, if one considers rutab different from tamr, the hadith regarding different types permits sale without equality. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it impermissible based on another hadith where the Prophet forbade it after being informed that fresh dates shrink when dried. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that the hadith of the Sahibayn is weak due to its chain through Zayd ibn 'Ayyash. The commentary also notes that other imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) side with Abu Hanifa on permissibility. The practical implication: according to Abu Hanifa, one can exchange equal weights of fresh and dried dates, while according to the Sahibayn, such an exchange is forbidden because of the hidden usury (riba al-fadl) due to unequal amounts of the same genus after drying.

Key Terms
رطب (rutab): Fresh, ripe dates that are soft and moist, before drying. In Urdu known as 'khajur'.
تمر (tamr): Dried dates, the common dried fruit. In Urdu, 'chhuara'.
مثلاً بمثل (mithlan bi mithl): Equal for equal, without excess or deficiency. Used in sales of ribawi items to avoid riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Abu Hanifa permits selling fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) in equal measure?
A) Because fresh dates are not considered dates.
B) Because the hadith of the Sahibayn is weak and he considers rutab as a type of tamr.
C) Because he only permits it when fresh dates are less in weight.
D) Because of consensus among the Sahaba.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position permits equal exchange of fresh and dried dates, based on Abu Hanifa's stronger evidence.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Sale of Fresh Dates for Dry Dates: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Genus and Riba
intra-Hanafi dispute on sale of fresh dates for dry dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on selling fresh dates for dry dates in equal measure, explain the proof of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the tarjih method by critiquing weak hadith.

Core Idea
Fresh dates are the same genus as dry dates according to Abu Hanifa, so equal exchange is valid; the Sahibayn's opposing hadith is weak.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: whether selling fresh dates (rutab) for dry dates (tamr) in equal measure is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa permits it, while his two disciples, the Sahibayn, prohibit it. The disagreement hinges on whether rutab and tamr are considered the same genus for riba purposes, and on a hadith that the Sahibayn rely upon. By studying the proofs and the critical evaluation of the hadith narrator, you will understand how Hanafi jurists resolve such disagreements.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position according to Abu Hanifa
Identify that Imam Abu Hanifa permits selling rutab for tamr in equal measure. This is the starting point of the dispute.
Note the term 'mithlan bi-mithl' (equal for equal).
2
Identify the dissenting view of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that such a sale is impermissible. Understand their reasoning.
They rely on a hadith about shrinkage.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale after being told that rutab shrinks when dried.
This hadith is transmitted by Zayd ibn 'Ayyash.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa uses two proofs: (1) a hadith where the Prophet called rutab 'tamr', indicating they are the same genus; (2) a rational argument that whether rutab is tamr or not, the sale is valid by the riba hadith's rules.
The Prophet said 'a-kullu tamri Khaybar haakadha?' (Is all the tamr of Khaybar like this?) referring to fresh dates.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The commentator weakens the Sahibayn's hadith by pointing out the narrator Zayd ibn 'Ayyash is da'if (weak). Therefore, Abu Hanifa's view is preferred and is the mufta bihi.
Other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) also agree with Abu Hanifa.

عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رطب کی دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یا تو رطب تمر ہے اور یا غیر تمر ہے اگر رطب، تمر ہے تو رطب کی بیع تمر کے عوض برابر، برابر جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیث ربوا کے اول میں گذر چکا التمر بالتمر مثلاً بمثل اور اگر رطب غیر تمر ہے تو رطب کی بیع تمر کے عوض متساویا اور متفاضلاً دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس حدیث کے آخر میں ہے اذا اختلف النوعان فبيعوا كيف شنتم یعنی اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں جس طرح چاہو فروخت کرو خواہ متساو یا خواہ متفاضلا۔ صاحبین کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث کا مدار زید بن عیاش پر ہے اور زید بن عیاش ائمہ حدیث کے نزدیک ضعیف اور مجہول راوی ہیں اس لئے یہ روایت حدیث مشہور کے مقابلے میں قابل استدلال نہ ہوگی۔
The discussion on whether selling fresh dates in exchange for dry dates in equal measure is permissible. The rulings of the jurists: Abu Hanifa said it is permissible equal for equal. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is not permissible because of the hadith when the Prophet was asked about it and said 'Does it shrink when dried?' They said yes, and he said 'Then do not do it.' Abu Hanifa argues that rutab is tamr because when the Prophet was presented with fresh dates from Khaybar, he called them tamr. He also used the principle: if rutab is tamr, the first part of the hadith (al-tamr bi'l-tamr mithlan bi-mithl) applies; if it is not tamr, then the second part (when types differ, sell as you wish) applies. The hadith of the two (Sahibayn) is based on Zayd ibn 'Ayyash, who is a weak narrator. Explanation: Rutab is fresh dates, tamr is dry dates. The issue: selling rutab for tamr with excess is unanimously prohibited; equal for equal is permissible according to Abu Hanifa but not according to the two. Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad also hold permissibility. The proof of the two: the hadith about shrinking. Abu Hanifa's proof: the Prophet called rutab tamr. Rational proof: either rutab is tamr, then equal sale is allowed by the first part of the riba hadith, or it is not tamr, then unequal sale is allowed by the second part. The response to the hadith of the two: its chain includes Zayd ibn 'Ayyash, who is weak and unknown among hadith scholars, so it is not acceptable against the famous hadith.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of fresh dates (rutab) for dry dates (tamr) in equal measure. The Hanafi position according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that such a sale is permissible (ja'iz), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), hold it impermissible. The Sahibayn rely on a hadith where the Prophet, upon being asked about this exchange, inquired whether the fresh dates shrink when dried. When told yes, he forbade the sale. Abu Hanifa, however, argues that the Prophet himself referred to fresh dates as 'tamr' when he received a gift from Khaybar, demonstrating that rutab is indeed a type of tamr. Consequently, the sale of tamr for tamr in equal measure is governed by the general prohibition of riba only when unequal; equality renders it permissible. Moreover, Abu Hanifa presents a rational argument: if rutab is tamr, the sale is valid under the first part of the riba hadith; if it is not tamr, then it is a sale of two different types, which is permissible with or without equality under the second part. The hadith cited by the Sahibayn is criticized for having a weak narrator, Zayd ibn 'Ayyash, making it unreliable against the established ruling. The commentator notes that the majority of scholars, including Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, also permit the sale, reinforcing Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
رطب (rutab): Fresh dates, still moist and soft.
تمر (tamr): Dry dates, the fully ripened and dried fruit.
زید بن عیاش (Zayd ibn 'Ayyash): A narrator of hadith considered weak (da'if) by hadith scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa permit the sale of fresh dates (rutab) for dry dates (tamr) in equal measure, while the Sahibayn forbid it?
A) Abu Hanifa considers rutab and tamr as different genera, so riba rules do not apply.
B) Abu Hanifa considers rutab to be tamr based on the Prophet's usage, so the sale is of the same genus and equality is required; he holds the equality exists at contract time.
C) The Sahibayn follow a stronger hadith that Abu Hanifa ignores.
D) Abu Hanifa allows all types of sales without restriction.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view that rutab is tamr permits equal exchange, and the Sahibayn's hadith is weak due to Zayd ibn 'Ayyash.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Sale of Fresh Grapes for Raisins: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Equality at Contract vs. Final State
Expands the intra-Hanafi dispute to multiple commodities and clarifies the criterion of 'most balanced state'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on the timing of equality in barter of shrinkable commodities and apply the distinction to new cases.

Core Idea
For riba in barter, Abu Hanifa requires equality at contract; Muhammad requires it at the final stable state.

This passage extends a key intra-Hanafi dispute about bartering fresh dates for dry dates to other commodities like grapes and wheat. The dispute hinges on whether equality must hold at the time of the contract or when the commodity reaches its final state (e.g., dried). Understanding this difference is crucial for correctly classifying such sales under Hanafi fiqh and for distinguishing between valid and invalid exchanges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Commodity Pairs
List the pairs mentioned in the text: fresh grapes for raisins, fresh wheat for dry wheat, soaked wheat for dry wheat, soaked raisins for dry raisins, and fresh dates for fresh dates. Note that all involve a commodity that can change (dry out) over time.
Also note the analogous case of fried wheat mentioned in the text.
2
State the Positions of the Three Imams
For each pair (except fresh dates for fresh dates), state that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit the sale if equal in measure at contract time, while Muhammad prohibits it. For fresh dates for fresh dates, all agree it is valid.
Recall that Abu Yusuf makes an exception for fresh dates for dry dates due to a specific hadith.
3
Identify the Key Principle for Muhammad
Muhammad bases his ruling on the principle of 'a'dal al-ahwal' (the most balanced state), meaning the final stable state of the commodity (e.g., when grains are dry). He argues that equality must hold at that state because that is when true equivalence is measurable.
Contrast with Abu Hanifa who considers only the state at contract time.
4
Explain Muhammad's Distinction
Muhammad distinguishes between cases where the variation (shrinkage) occurs while both items still retain the name they had at contract (e.g., fresh grapes for raisins: grapes are fresh, raisins are dry – one name changes) and cases where the variation occurs after the name has changed (e.g., fresh dates for fresh dates: both are 'rutab' at contract and later become 'tamr', but the contraction was on fresh dates, so the variation is not in the subject matter of the contract).
This distinction explains why fresh dates for fresh dates is permitted even by Muhammad.
5
Apply to a New Case
Consider the sale of 100 kg of fresh wheat for 100 kg of dry wheat. According to Abu Hanifa, it is valid if equal at contract. According to Muhammad, it is invalid because the fresh wheat will lose weight when dried, and equality does not hold in the final state. Determine whether the variation occurs before or after the name changes.
Fresh wheat and dry wheat have different names (ratbah vs. hanṭah yābisah), so the variation is in the subject matter, making it invalid for Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی تازہ انگور کو خشک انگور کے عوض یعنی اسی اختلاف پر ہے اور اس کی وجہ وہی ہے جس کو بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ اور کہا گیا کہ بالا تفاق جائز نہیں ہے بھونے ہوئے گندم کی بیع کو بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور رطب کو رطب کے عوض پیمانہ سے برابر کر کے بیچنا ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ بیع التمر بالتمر ہے اور ایسے ہی پختہ تازے گندم کو یا پانی سے بھیگے ہوئے گندم کو اس کے مثل کے عوض یا خشک کے عوض بیچنا (ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک) جائز ہے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ ہر تمام صورتیں نا جائز ہیں۔ کیونکہ امام محمد اعدل حوال میں سوات کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں اور وہ انجام کی حالت ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ بالفعل کی حالت کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں اور یوں ہی ابو یوسف اطلاق حدیث پر عمل کرتے ہوئے مگر ابو یوسف نے اپنی اس اصل کو بیع الرطب بالتمر میں ترک کر دیا ہے۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم نے صاحبین کے واسطے روایت کیا ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ان مسئلوں اور بیع الرطب بالرطہ
He said: And likewise fresh grapes for raisins — meaning on this same dispute, and the reasoning is what we explained. And some said it is unanimously not permissible, by analogy to fried wheat (i.e., the difference between fried and non-fried wheat). And fresh dates for fresh dates is permissible in equal measure by volume according to us because it is a sale of tamr for tamr. And likewise, the sale of fresh wheat or soaked wheat for its like or for dry wheat, or fresh dates or soaked raisins for their like in equal measure is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said all that is not permissible because he considers equality in the most balanced state, which is the final state (when dry). Abu Hanifa considers at the time of contract, and likewise Abu Yusuf acting on the general application of the hadith, except that Abu Yusuf abandoned this principle in the sale of fresh dates for dry dates due to the hadith we narrated for the two of them. And the distinction for Muhammad between these cases and fresh dates for fresh dates is that the variation appears while both items retain the name on which the contract was made; in the sale of fresh dates for dry dates, one remains with that name, so there is variation in the very subject matter. In fresh dates for fresh dates, the variation appears after that name has changed, so it is not a variation in the subject matter, and thus is not considered. Translation: And similarly, the sale of fresh grapes for dry grapes is on this same dispute, and its reason is what has been explained. And it was said that it is unanimously not permissible, by analogy to the sale of fried wheat for non-fried wheat. And selling fresh dates for fresh dates in equal measure by volume is permissible according to us, because it is a sale of tamr for tamr. And similarly, the sale of fresh wheat or soaked wheat for its like or for dry wheat, or fresh dates or soaked raisins for their like in equal measure is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Imam Muhammad said all these cases are impermissible. Because Imam Muhammad considers equality in the most balanced state, which is the final state. And Imam Abu Hanifa considers the actual state at the time, and similarly Abu Yusuf acts on the general application of the hadith, except that Abu Yusuf abandoned this principle in the sale of fresh dates for dry dates due to the hadith we narrated for the two. And according to Muhammad, the distinction between these cases and the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates is that in these cases, the variation appears while both items retain the name on which the contract was made, whereas in the sale of fresh dates for dry dates, one retains that name, so there is variation in the very subject matter. In the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, the variation appears after that name has changed, so it is not a variation in the subject matter, and thus is not considered.

Commentary
This passage extends the intra-Hanafi dispute to other commodities like fresh grapes for raisins, fresh wheat for dry wheat, etc. The key principle is whether equality is required at the time of contract or at the final state when the commodity becomes dry and stable. Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that equality is considered at the time of contract (متماثلا كيلا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف). They rely on the literal application of the prohibitory hadith on riba, which requires equality in measure at the time of exchange. Imam Muhammad, however, insists on equality in the 'most balanced state' (أعدل الأحوال), which is when the commodity has reached its final stable state (e.g., dried). He argues that because these items change (e.g., fresh grapes become lighter when dried), equality at the time of contract does not guarantee true equality. In the case of selling fresh dates for fresh dates (الرطب بالرطب), all agree it is permissible because both are in the same state and no change is expected; the variation only occurs after the contract. For fresh grapes for raisins, the variation occurs while the grapes are still fresh and will dry later, thus Muhammad considers it impermissible. The text also notes that Abu Yusuf made an exception in the sale of fresh dates for dry dates, accepting the Sahibayn's hadith there, but applies his principle elsewhere.

Key Terms
عنب ('inab): Fresh grapes, the fruit before drying.
زبيب (zabib): Raisins, dried grapes.
أعدل الأحوال (a'dal al-ahwal): The most balanced state, i.e., the final stable condition of the commodity (e.g., dryness).
حنطة مقلية (hanṭah muqliyyah): Fried wheat, used as an analogy to show that processing changes the commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the sale of fresh grapes for raisins in equal measure?
A) Muhammad requires equality at the time of contract; Abu Hanifa requires it at the final dry state.
B) Muhammad requires equality at the final dry state; Abu Hanifa requires it at the time of contract.
C) Both require equality at the time of contract, but Abu Hanifa makes an exception for grapes.
D) Muhammad considers grapes and raisins different genera, so equality is not required.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, there is a legitimate dispute on whether riba equality in barter is required at contract time or at the final stable state; the position of Abu Hanifa is commonly followed, but Muhammad's view offers a more rigorous preventive approach.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Selling Fresh Dates for Dried Dates: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Establishes permissibility of fruit-for-fruit exchange with equality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) and identify the primary dalil from the Sunnah that supports it.

Core Idea
Fresh dates are a type of tamr; exchange them equally or differ type—both valid, but excess within same type is riba.

This lesson explores a classic Hanafi ruling on a common commercial transaction: exchanging fresh dates for dried dates. The passage from Al-Hidayah establishes that such an exchange is permissible if done like-for-like by measure, based on the prophetic hadith that dates for dates must be equal. We will examine the proof, the rational argument, and an intra-Hanafi dispute settled by tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr). The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) if the quantities are equal by measure; if excess occurs, it becomes riba and is haram.
The ruling is conditional on equality in the same type (both being tamr).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is the authentic hadith: 'al-tamr bi'l-tamr mithlan bi-mithl wa'l-fadlu riba' (dates for dates, like for like, excess is riba). This is cited in the text.
The translation is provided: 'Selling dates for dates, like for like, and any excess is riba.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'mithlan bi-mithl' (like for like) indicates that equality of quantity is required when exchanging the same type. The term 'tamr' includes fresh dates (rutab) as shown by the Prophet calling them tamr. Thus, the hadith directly covers this exchange.
The rational argument: if rutab is tamr, equality required; if not tamr, differing types allow inequality.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) initially objected based on a hadith from Zayd ibn 'Ayyash suggesting fresh dates shrink, making equal exchange unfair. The author rejects this narration as weak and unknown.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the Sahibayn eventually agreed with Abu Hanifa.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers Abu Hanifa's view by declaring the opposing narration weak. The mufta bihi position is that selling fresh dates for dried dates is permissible if equal by measure.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah, and the ruling facilitates trade.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم
کئے گئے ان کو دیکھ کر آپ نے فرمایا او كل تمر خيبر هكذا ، کیا خیبر کے تمام چھوارے ایسے ہی ہیں، ملاحظہ فرمائیے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بر طلب کو تمر فرمایا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ رطب تمر ہیں۔ اور تمر کی بیع تمر کے عوض برابر ، برابر جائز ہے جیسا کہ حدیث النمر بالتمر مثلاً بمثل والفضل ربا یعنی تمر کی بیع تمر کی عوض برابر بر جائز ہے۔ اس پر شاہد عدل ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ رطب کی بیع تمر کے عوض برابر، برابر جائز ہے۔
عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رطب کی دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یا تو رطب تمر ہے اور یا غیر تمر ہے اگر رطب ، تمر ہے تو رطب کی بیع تمر کے عوض برابر، برا بر جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیث ربوا کے اول میں گذر چکا التمر بالتمر مثلاً بمثل اور اگر رطب غیر تمر ہے تو رطب کی بیع تمر کے عوض متساویا اور متفاضلاً دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس حدیث کے آخر میں ہے اذا اختلف النوعان فبيعوا كيف شنتم یعنی اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں جس طرح چاہو فروخت کرو خواہ متساو یا خواہ متفاضلا۔ صاحبین کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث کا مدار زید بن عیاش پر ہے اور زید بن عیاش ائمہ حدیث کے نزدیک ضعیف اور مجہول راوی ہیں اس لئے یہ روایت حدیث مشہور کے مقابلے میں قابل استدلال نہ ہوگی۔
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume eight. When he saw them, he said: 'Are all the dates of Khaybar like this?' Observe: The Prophet (peace be upon him) called fresh dates 'tamr'. From this it is known that fresh dates are tamr. And selling tamr for tamr is permissible if equal, as in the hadith: 'Selling dates for dates, like for like, and any excess is riba.' So selling fresh dates for tamr is permissible if equal. Rational proof: Fresh dates are either tamr or not. If fresh dates are tamr, then selling them for tamr is permissible if equal, due to the hadith 'al-tamr bi'l-tamr mithlan bi-mithl'. If fresh dates are not tamr, then selling them for tamr is permissible whether equal or unequal, because the same hadith ends with 'idha ikhtalafa al-naw'ani fa-bi'u kayfa shi'tum' meaning: when the types differ, sell as you wish. The answer to the hadith presented by the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that it depends on Zayd ibn 'Ayyash, and Zayd ibn 'Ayyash is a weak and unknown narrator according to hadith scholars, so this narration cannot be used as evidence against the well-known hadith.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of selling fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) like-for-like by measure. The author begins by referencing an incident where the Prophet (peace be upon him) saw dates from Khaybar and referred to them as 'tamr', establishing that fresh dates are linguistically and legally a type of tamr. The primary evidence is the well-known hadith: 'Selling dates for dates, like for like, and any excess is riba,' which strictly requires equality in quantity (by measure) when exchanging the same type. The author also provides a rational proof: if fresh dates are tamr, the rule applies; if not, they differ in type and the hadith allows unequal exchange. The author then addresses the objection raised by the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) based on a different hadith narrated by Zayd ibn 'Ayyash. The author rejects this narration because Zayd is considered weak (da'if) and unknown (majhul) by hadith scholars, so it cannot override the clear, authentic hadith. Therefore, the Hanafi position is upheld: selling fresh dates for dry dates is permissible when equal by measure.

Key Terms
رطب (rutab): Fresh dates, still moist and not fully dried.
تمر (tamr): Dried dates, the common term for dates in a preserved state.
ربا (riba): Usury or unlawful increase in exchange of ribawi goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is selling fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) permissible if equal by measure?
A) Because fresh dates are not ribawi items.
B) Because the Prophet called fresh dates 'tamr', so they are considered the same type.
C) Because the hadith allows any exchange between different types.
D) Because dried dates are not commonly consumed.

Key Takeaway
Selling fresh dates for dried dates is permissible in the Hanafi school only when equal by measure, based on the authentic hadith that dates for dates must be like for like.
