Selling Fresh Grapes for Raisins: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ribawi exchange of fresh and dried fruit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on selling fresh grapes for raisins and identify the mufta bihi position with its justification.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree fresh grapes and raisins are one type; they differ on when equality must be assessed.

This lesson unpacks a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is it permissible to sell fresh grapes for an equal measure of raisins? While all Hanafi imams agree that grapes and raisins are the same ribawi type, they diverge on the timing of equality. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider the current state sufficient; Muhammad demands equality in the final dried state. The ruling has practical implications for fruit exchanges and teaches us about the role of 'a'dal al-ahwal' in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ikhtilaf
Recognize that the sale of fresh grapes (inab) for raisins (zabib) is a ribawi exchange of the same type, requiring equality. The dispute is whether equality is satisfied at contract or must persist after drying.
The term 'a'dal al-ahwal' (most balanced state) is key to Muhammad's position.
2
State Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's position
They permit the sale if measured equally at the time of contract, based on the general hadith and the principle that the current state is sufficient.
Abu Yusuf makes an exception for fresh dates vs. dried dates, following a specific narration.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad prohibits it because equality must be assessed in the final state after drying, as disparity will inevitably arise.
He uses qiyas with roasted wheat and emphasizes the potential for hidden riba.
4
Understand the distinction with dates
The text contrasts grapes/raisins with fresh dates (rutab) and dried dates (tamr). For dates, the prophetic hadith establishes that fresh dates are called tamr, so the sale is permissible as tamr for tamr. No such hadith applies to grapes.
This distinction explains why Abu Yusuf's exception for dates does not extend to grapes.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's: selling fresh grapes for raisins by equal measure is permissible.
Al-Hidayah adopts this view, and it is the basis for fatwa today.

Source Text

قال وكذا العنب بالزبيب يعنى على هذا الخلاف والوجه ما بيناه وقيل لايجوز بالاتفاق اعتبارا بالحنطة المقلية والرطب بالرطب يجوز متماثلا كيلا عندنا؛ لأنه بيع التمر بالتمر وكذا بيع الحنطة الرطبة أو المبلولة بمثلها أو باليابسة أو التمر أو الزبيب المنقع بالمنقع منها متماثلا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد لا يجوز جميع ذالك؛ لأنه يعتبر المساواة في أعدل الأحوال وهو المال وأبو حنيفة يعتبر في الحال وكذا أبويوسف عملا بإطلاق الحديث إلا أنه ترك هذا الأصل في بيع الرطب بالتمر لما رويناه لهما ووجه الفرق لمحمد بين هذه الفصول وبين الرطب بالرطب أن التفاوت فيها يظهر مع بقاء البدلين على الاسم الذى عقد عليه العقد وفى الرطب بالتمر مع بقاء أحدهما على ذالك فيكون تفاوتا في عين المعقود عليه والرطب بالرطب التفاوت بعد زوال ذالك الاسم فلم يكن تفاوتا في المعقود عليه فلا يعتبر
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی تازہ انگور کو خشک انگور کے عوض یعنی اسی اختلاف پر ہے اور اس کی وجہ وہی ہے جس کو بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ اور کہا گیا کہ بالا تفاق جائز نہیں ہے بھونے ہوئے گندم کی بیع کو بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور رطب کو رطب کے عوض پیمانہ سے برابر کر کے بیچنا ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ بیج التمر بالتمر ہے اور ایسے ہی پختہ تازے گندم کو یا پانی سے بھیگے ہوئے گندم کو اس کے مثل کے عوض یا خشک کے عوض بیچنا ) ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ( جائز ہے ) اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ ہر تمام صورتیں نا جائز ہیں۔ کیونکہ امام محمد اعدل حوال میں سوات کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں اور وہ انجام کی حالت ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ بالفعل کی حالت کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں اور یوں ہی ابو یوسف اطلاق حدیث پر عمل کرتے ہوئے مگر ابو یوسف نے اپنی اس اصل کو بیع الرطب بالتمر میں ترک کر دیا ہے۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم نے صاحبین کے واسطے روایت کیا ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ان مسئلوں اور بیع الرطب بالرطہ

٣١٩
كتاب البيوع
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہشتم کے درمیان وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں تفاوت ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے باوجود یکہ دونوں عوش اس نام پر باقی رہتے ہیں جس پر عقد منعقد کیا گیا ہے اور بیع الرطب بالتمر میں ( تفاوت ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے ) باوجود یکہ دونوں میں سے ایک اسی نام پر باقی رہتا ہے( جس پر عقد واقع ہوا ) تو یہ معقود علیہ کی ذات میں تفاوت ہو گا اور رطب بالرطب کی بیع میں یہ نام زائل ہونے کے بعد تفاوت ہوا ہے تو یہ معقود علیہ میں تفاوت نہ ہوا ۔ پس اس کا اعتبار بھی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک پختہ تازہ انگور کو خشک انگور (کشمش ) کے عوض پیمانہ کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے بیچنا
جائز ہے، اور صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک نہ متساو یا جائز ہے اور نہ متفاضلا جائز ہے۔ فریقین کی دلیلیں سابق میں گذر چکی ہیں۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عنب اور زبیب دونوں کی اگر ایک جنس ہے تو ان میں سے ایک کی بیچ دوسرے کے عوض کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے جائز ہے اور اگر دونوں کی جنس الگ الگ ہے تو حدیث اذا اختلف النوعان فبيعوا كيف شئتم کی وجہ سے ان کی بیع متساویاً اور متفاضل دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔ صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تازہ انگور ، خشک ہو کر چونکہ گھٹ جاتا ہے اس لئے زید بن عیاش کی حدیث ... او ينقص اذا جف فقيل نعم فقال لا کی وجہ سے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔
بعض حضرات کا خیال یہ ہے کہ عنب کی بیچ زبیب کے عوض متساویا بالاتفاق ناجائز ہے صاحبین کے نزدیک بھی اور حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی اور اس عدم جواز پر قیاس سے استدلال کیا ہے، یعنی جس طرح بھونے ہوئے گندم کی پیے بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض پیمانے سے برابر کر کے ناجائز ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے، اسی طرح عنب یعنی تازے انگور کی بیع خشک انگور یعنی کشمش کے عوض پیمانے سے برابر کرنے کے باوجود نا جائز ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی اس روایت کے مطابق بیج استمر بالرطب اور بیع العنب بالزبیب کے درمیان فرق بیان کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بیع التمر بالرطب متساو یا جائز ہے اور اس روایت کے مطابق بیج العنب بالزبیب متساویا نا جائز ہے۔ بہر حال وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ رطب پر تمر کا اطلاق حدیث او کل تمر خیبر هكذا سے ثابت ہے۔ پس رطب کا تمر کے عوض بیچنا تمر کا تمر کے عوض بیچنا ہے۔ اور تمر کا تمر کے عوض برابر برابر بیچنا جائز ہے۔ لہذا رطب کا تمر کے عوض برابر برابر بیچنا بھی جائز ہوگا ۔ اور زبیب کا اطلاق عنب پر چونکہ حدیث سے ثابت نہیں ہے اس لئے زیب اور عنب میں کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کرنے کے باوجود تفاوت کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور جب تفاوت معتبر ہے تو بیع فاسد اور نا جائز ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ رطب کی بیع رطب کے عوض اور عنب کی بیچ عنب کے عوض پیمانے سے برابر کر کے ہمارے نزدیک جائزہ
ہے یہی امام مالک او امام احمد کا قول ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رطب اور عنب خشک ہو جانے پر متفاوت ہو جاتے ہیں یعنی رطب اور عنب کی خشک ہو جانے کے بعد ضروری نہیں کہ دونوں عوض برابر رہیں بلکہ دونوں میں کمی زیادتی واقع ہو سکتی ہے اور کی زیادتی واقع ہونے کا نام رہوا ہے اور ر بوانا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے رطب کی بیچ رطب کے عوض اور عنب کی بیچ عنب کے عوض بذریعہ کیل برابر برابر نا جائز ہے، جیسا کہ گندم کی بیچ آٹے کے
عوض برابر ، برابر نا جائز ہے۔
He said: And likewise grapes for raisins, meaning on the same difference of opinion, and the correct view is what we explained. It was said: It is impermissible by consensus, by analogy with roasted wheat. And selling fresh dates for fresh dates is permissible like-for-like by measure according to us, because it is selling dates for dates. Similarly, selling wet wheat or moistened wheat for its like or for dry wheat, or dates or soaked raisins for their like, like-for-like, is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: All of that is impermissible, because he considers equality in the most balanced state, which is the end state. Abu Hanifa considers equality in the current state, and likewise Abu Yusuf, acting upon the general application of the hadith. However, Abu Yusuf abandoned this principle in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates due to the hadith we narrated for the two companions. The point of distinction for Muhammad between these cases and fresh dates for fresh dates is that disparity appears while both items retain the name upon which the contract was made. In the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, disparity appears while one of them retains that name, so it is disparity in the very object of the contract. In fresh dates for fresh dates, the disparity occurs after that name disappears, so it is not disparity in the object of the contract and thus not considered. Translation: And similarly, fresh grapes for dried grapes (raisins) is on the same difference of opinion. And it was said that it is impermissible by consensus, by analogy with roasted wheat. And selling fresh dates (rutab) for fresh dates like-for-like by measure is permissible according to us, because it is selling dates for dates. Similarly, selling fresh wheat or wet wheat for its like or for dry wheat, or dates or soaked raisins for their like like-for-like, is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad said all these cases are impermissible. Because Imam Muhammad considers equality in the most balanced state, which is the final state. Imam Abu Hanifa considers the current state, and Abu Yusuf acts upon the general application of the hadith, but Abu Yusuf abandoned this principle in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates due to the hadith we narrated for the two companions. And according to Imam Muhammad, the distinction between these issues and the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates is that disparity becomes apparent in these cases while both items still retain the name upon which the contract was made. In the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, disparity appears while one still retains that name, so it is disparity in the essence of the object of contract. In the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, the disparity occurs after that name disappears, so it is not disparity in the object of contract; hence it is not considered. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling fresh grapes for dried grapes (raisins) by measure is permissible. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three imams (al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad), it is not permissible either equally or unequally. The proofs were given earlier. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: If grapes and raisins are the same type, selling one for the other by measure is permissible; if they are different types, the hadith 'When types differ, sell as you wish' allows equal or unequal sale. The proof of the two companions and the three imams: Since fresh grapes shrink when dried, the hadith of Zayd ibn 'Ayyash 'Does it decrease when dried? He said yes. He said: No' makes the sale impermissible. Some scholars hold that selling grapes for raisins is impermissible by consensus, even according to Imam Abu Hanifa, proved by analogy with roasted wheat: just as roasted wheat cannot be sold for unroasted wheat by measure, similarly grapes for raisins is impermissible. However, it becomes necessary to distinguish between the sale of fresh dates for dried dates and the sale of grapes for raisins. Because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling fresh dates for dried dates like-for-like is permissible, but in this accepted narration, selling grapes for raisins like-for-like is impermissible. The distinction: The application of 'tamr' to fresh dates is proven by the hadith 'Are all the dates of Khaybar like this?' So selling fresh dates for dried dates is selling dates for dates, which is permissible. The application of 'zabib' to grapes is not proven by hadith, so even if measured equally, disparity is considered, making the sale invalid. The author of al-Hidayah says: Selling fresh dates for fresh dates and grapes for grapes by measure is permissible according to us. This is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is impermissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: Fresh dates and grapes become unequal when dried: it is not necessary that they remain equal after drying, and inequality may occur, which is riba, and riba is prohibited. Therefore, selling fresh dates for fresh dates and grapes for grapes by measure is impermissible, just as selling wheat for flour like-for-like is impermissible.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage delves into the ruling on selling fresh grapes (inab) for raisins (zabib), a related ribawi exchange. The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit the exchange if equal by measure, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it. The core difference lies in when equality is assessed: Abu Hanifa considers the current state at the time of contract, while Muhammad considers the most balanced state (after drying, to avoid potential riba). Abu Yusuf generally follows Abu Hanifa's principle of applying the hadith broadly, but he makes an exception for fresh dates for dried dates based on a specific narration. Muhammad distinguishes between cases where disparity appears while both items still bear the original name (like fresh grapes and raisins) and where one loses the name (like fresh dates for fresh dates, where after drying both lose the 'fresh' designation). Later, the text addresses an inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi school (along with Maliki and Hanbali) permits selling fresh dates for fresh dates or fresh grapes for fresh grapes by measure, while Shafi'i prohibits it, arguing that drying causes disparity that leads to riba. The Shafi'i analogy is that like wheat and flour (which are different states), fresh and dried produce are different. The Hanafi response relies on the hadith that fresh dates are called tamr, and fresh grapes are not called zabib in revelation, so the analogy to dates does not apply. Overall, this lesson clarifies the nuanced Hanafi position on ribawi exchanges involving produce that changes state.

Key Terms
عنب (inab): Fresh grapes.
زبيب (zabib): Raisins, dried grapes.
أعدل الأحوال (a'dal al-ahwal): The most balanced state, i.e., the final state after drying, used by Muhammad to assess equality.
رطب (rutab): Fresh dates, moist dates.
تمر (tamr): Dried dates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, is it permissible to sell fresh grapes for an equal measure of raisins?
A) No, because the hadith prohibits it.
B) Yes, because the Prophet said fresh grapes are raisins.
C) Yes, because equality at the time of contract is sufficient.
D) No, because Muhammad's view is preferred.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling fresh grapes for raisins by equal measure at the time of contract, following Abu Hanifa, despite Imam Muhammad's objection based on final state equality.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Dispute on Fresh Grapes for Dried Grapes (cunab bi'l-zabib)
Explains the cunab bi'l-zabib dispute and its resolution via name application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on selling fresh grapes for dried grapes by measure equally and evaluate the proofs based on hadith and name categorization.

Core Idea
If the name changes upon drying, it is a different species; if not, equality post-drying is required.

This lesson unpacks the celebrated dispute over selling fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib). The Hanafi school has multiple narrations, and the key to reconciling them lies in whether the dried form shares the same name by hadith. We will walk through the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and the three other Imams, and understand how the later Hanafi tradition settled on prohibition by distinguishing species based on linguistic usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is selling fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib) by measure equally (mithlan bi-mithl). Determine the initial ruling from each camp.
Imam Abu Hanifa permits it (in one narration); Sahibayn and the three Imams prohibit it absolutely.
2
Locate the dalil for each side
Imam Abu Hanifa relies on the general hadith 'idha ikhtalafa al-naw'an fabi'u kayfa shi'tum' (when types differ, sell as you wish), treating cunab and zabib as either same or different genera. The opposing side relies on the hadith of Zayd ibn 'Ayyash: the Prophet prohibited when told that fresh grapes shrink upon drying.
Also note the claim of consensus with analogy to roasted/unroasted wheat.
3
Apply the name-based distinction
The text resolves the contradiction by noting that the term 'zabib' is not applied to 'cunab' in any hadith, unlike 'tamr' which is applied to 'rutab'. Therefore, cunab and zabib are considered different species, making equality insufficient even if measured equally.
This reconciles Abu Hanifa's permissive narration with the prohibition, showing that the mufta bihi position is prohibition.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a Hanafi following the permissive narration would allow equal sale; the relied-upon view prohibits it. Thus, a mufti today would rule that selling fresh grapes for raisins by measure equally is impermissible.

كتاب البيوع
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہشتم کے درمیان وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں تفاوت ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے باوجود یکہ دونوں عوش اس نام پر باقی رہتے ہیں جس پر عقد منعقد کیا گیا ہے اور بیع الرطب بالتمر میں ( تفاوت ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے ) باوجود یکہ دونوں میں سے ایک اسی نام پر باقی رہتا ہے( جس پر عقد واقع ہوا ) تو یہ معقود علیہ کی ذات میں تفاوت ہو گا اور رطب بالرطب کی بیع میں یہ نام زائل ہونے کے بعد تفاوت ہوا ہے تو یہ معقود علیہ میں تفاوت نہ ہوا ۔ پس اس کا اعتبار بھی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک پختہ تازہ انگور کو خشک انگور (کشمش ) کے عوض پیمانہ کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے بیچنا جائز ہے، اور صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک نہ متساو یا جائز ہے اور نہ متفاضلا جائز ہے۔ فریقین کی دلیلیں سابق میں گذر چکی ہیں۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عنب اور زبیب دونوں کی اگر ایک جنس ہے تو ان میں سے ایک کی بیچ دوسرے کے عوض کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے جائز ہے اور اگر دونوں کی جنس الگ الگ ہے تو حدیث اذا اختلف النوعان فبيعوا كيف شئتم کی وجہ سے ان کی بیع متساویاً اور متفاضل دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔ صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تازہ انگور ، خشک ہو کر چونکہ گھٹ جاتا ہے اس لئے زید بن عیاش کی حدیث ... او ينقص اذا جف فقيل نعم فقال لا کی وجہ سے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔
بعض حضرات کا خیال یہ ہے کہ عنب کی بیچ زبیب کے عوض متساویا بالاتفاق ناجائز ہے صاحبین کے نزدیک بھی اور حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی اور اس عدم جواز پر قیاس سے استدلال کیا ہے، یعنی جس طرح بھونے ہوئے گندم کی پیے بغیر بھونے ہوئے گندم کے عوض پیمانے سے برابر کر کے ناجائز ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے، اسی طرح عنب یعنی تازے انگور کی بیع خشک انگور یعنی کشمش کے عوض پیمانے سے برابر کرنے کے باوجود نا جائز ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی اس روایت کے مطابق بیج استمر بالرطب اور بیع العنب بالزبیب کے درمیان فرق بیان کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بیع التمر بالرطب متساو یا جائز ہے اور اس روایت کے مطابق بیج العنب بالزبیب متساویا نا جائز ہے۔ بہر حال وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ رطب پر تمر کا اطلاق حدیث او کل تمر خیبر هكذا سے ثابت ہے۔ پس رطب کا تمر کے عوض بیچنا تمر کا تمر کے عوض بیچنا ہے۔ اور تمر کا تمر کے عوض برابر برابر بیچنا جائز ہے۔ لہذا رطب کا تمر کے عوض برابر برابر بیچنا بھی جائز ہوگا ۔ اور زبیب کا اطلاق عنب پر چونکہ حدیث سے ثابت نہیں ہے اس لئے زیب اور عنب میں کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کرنے کے باوجود تفاوت کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور جب تفاوت معتبر ہے تو بیع فاسد اور نا جائز ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ رطب کی بیع رطب کے عوض اور عنب کی بیچ عنب کے عوض پیمانے سے برابر کر کے ہمارے نزدیک جائزہے یہی امام مالک او امام احمد کا قول ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رطب اور عنب خشک ہو جانے پر متفاوت ہو جاتے ہیں یعنی رطب اور عنب کی خشک ہو جانے کے بعد ضروری نہیں کہ دونوں عوض برابر رہیں بلکہ دونوں میں کمی زیادتی واقع ہو سکتی ہے اور کی زیادتی واقع ہونے کا نام رہوا ہے اور ر بوانا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے رطب کی بیچ رطب کے عوض اور عنب کی بیچ عنب کے عوض بذریعہ کیل برابر برابر نا جائز ہے، جیسا کہ گندم کی بیچ آٹے کے عوض برابر ، برابر نا جائز ہے۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رطب کو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تمر فرمایا ہے تو رطب کی بیع رطب کے عوض در حقیت تمر کی بیع تمر کے عوض ہے اور حدیث التمر بالتمر مثلاً بمثل کی وجہ سے تمر کی بیع تمر کی عوض برابر جائز ہے۔ اسلئے رطب کی بیچ رطب کے عوض بھی برابر جائز ہو گی ۔ سی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے عنب کی بیع عنب کے عوض برابر برابر بھی جائز ہو گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ شیخین کے نزدیک کیل کے ذریعہ برابر کر کے پختہ تازہ گندم کی بیچ، پختہ تازہ گندم کے عوض یا بھیگے ہوئے گندم کے عوض یا خشک گندم کے عوض جائز ہے اور اسی طرح بھیگے ہوئے گندم کی بھیج بھیگے ہوئے گندم کے عوض اور خشک کے برابر، برابر جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح بھیگے ہوئے چھواروں کی بھیج بھیگے ہوئے چھواروں کے عوض اور بھیگے ہوئے کشمش کی بیج بھیگے ہوئے کشمش کے برابر، برابر جائز ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ مذکورہ صورتوں میں بیچ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ دونوں عوضوں میں مساوات اور برابری کا اعتبار ایسی حالت میں کرتے ہیں جو سب سے بڑھ کر برابری دلیل . کرنے والی ہو۔ اور وہ انجام یعنی خشک ہو جانے کی حالت ہے۔ یعنی امام محمد کے نزدیک عوضین کے خشک ہو جانے کے بعد ان کے درمیان مساوات اور برابری ضروری ہے۔ جیسا کہ حدیث او ینقص اذا جف فقيل نعم فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم لا سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے اور مذکورہ صورتوں میں عوضین کے درمیان فی الحال اگرچہ مساوات و برابری موجود ہے لیکن خشک ہونے کے بعد تفاوت واقع ہو جائے گا۔ اسلئے مذکر وہ صورتوں میں بیع نا جائز ہے۔
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرات شیخین حدیث مشهور الحنطة بالحنطة النمر بالمتر مثلاً بمثل الحدیث پر عمل کرتے ہوئے عقد بیع کے وقت عوضین کے درمیان مساوات اور برابری کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں یعنی اموال ربویہ کی بیچ میں عقد بیع کے وقت دونوں عوضوں کا برابر برابر ہونا ضروری ہے بعد میں برابری باقی رہے یا برابری باقی نہ رہے۔ البتہ امام ابو یوسف نے عقد بیع کے وقت مساوات کا اعتبار کرنے کے اصول بیع الرطب بالتمر میں حدیث او ینقص اذا جف فقيل نعم فقال لا کی وجہ سے ترک کر دیا ہے۔ یعنی بیع الرطب بالتمر میں اگر دونوں عوض بالفعل برابر ہوں تو بھی اس حدیث کی وجہ بو یوسف کے نزدیک بیع نا جائز ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ امام محمد صبیح الرطب بالرطب میں بالفعل مساوات کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں یعنی اگر رطب کو رطب کے عوض کیل سے برابر کر کے بیچا گیا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ خشک ہو جانے کے بعد برابری باقی رہے یا نہ رہے اور مذکورہ صورتوں میں یعنی پختہ تازہ گندم وغیرہ کی بیع میں انجام کی حالت یعنی خشک ہونے کے بعد مساوات کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں۔ سو ان میں وجہ فرق کیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں یعنی تازہ گندم وغیرہ کی بیع میں خشک ہو جانے کے بعد عوضین کے درمیان تفاوت ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے باوجود یکہ دونوں عوض اسی نام پر باقی رہتے ہیں۔ جس پر عقد منعقد کیا گیا تھا مثلاً گندم خشک ہونے سے پہلے بھی گندم کہلاتا ہے اور خشک ہونے کے بعد بھی گندم ہی کہلاتا ہے اسی طرح تمر اور زبیب خشک ہونے سے پہلے بھی تمر اور زبیب ہیں اور خشک ہونے کے بعد بھی تمر اور زبیب ہی کہلاتے ہیں۔ نام میں کوئی تبدیلی واقع نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور بیع الرطب بالتمر میں خشک ہو جانے کے بعد تفاوت ظاہر ہوتا ہے باوجود یکہ دونوں میں سے ایک یعنی تم اسی نام پر باقی رہتا ہے جس پر عقد واقع ہوا تھا پس یہ تفاوت معقود علیہ کی ذات میں ظاہر ہوا اور معقود علیہ کی ذات میں جو تفاوت ہوتا ہے وہ ربوا ہونے کی وجہ سے مفسد ہوتا ہے اسلئے ان صورتوں میں بیع فاسد اور نا جائز ہے اور رطب بالرطب کی بیچ میں نیہ نام زائل ہونے کے بعد تفاوت ہوا ہے کیونکہ خشک ہونے سے پہلے عوضین کا نام رطب تھا اور خشک ہو جانے کے بعد تمر ہو گیا۔ پس جب وہ نام زائل ہونے کے بعد تفاوت ظاہر ہوا جس
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Eight. The reason for distinction is that in these cases (fresh wheat, etc.) the difference becomes apparent even though both counterparts remain on the same name on which the contract was concluded. And in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, the difference becomes apparent even though one of them (the dried dates) remains on the same name on which the contract was concluded. So this difference is in the essence of the subject matter. And in the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, the difference occurs after the name is removed, so it is not a difference in the subject matter. Therefore it is not considered. Explanation of the issue: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib/kishmish) by measure equally is permissible. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad), it is not permissible either equally or with inequality. The proofs of the two sides have passed earlier. Imam Sahib's proof is that if cunab and zabib are of the same genus, then selling one for the other by measure equally is permissible, and if they are of different genera, then due to the hadith 'When the types differ, sell as you wish', their sale is permissible both equally and with inequality. The proof of the Sahibayn and three Imams is that since fresh grapes shrink when dried, due to the hadith of Zayd ibn 'Ayyash ... 'Does it decrease when dry?' He said yes, so he (peace be upon him) said no, the sale will not be permissible. Some people think that the sale of cunab for zabib equally is unanimously impermissible, according to the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa as well, and they have argued for this impermissibility by analogy: just as the sale of roasted wheat for unroasted wheat by measure equally is impermissible as previously mentioned, similarly the sale of fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib) by measure is impermissible despite equality. And according to this narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, it is necessary to explain the distinction between the sale of dates for fresh dates and the sale of grapes for dried grapes. Because according to Imam Sahib, the sale of dates for fresh dates equally is permissible, and according to this narration, the sale of grapes for dried grapes equally is impermissible. In any case, the reason for distinction is that the application of the name 'tamr' (dates) to 'rutab' (fresh dates) is established by the hadith 'And he ate the dates of Khaybar like this'. So selling fresh dates for dates is selling dates for dates. And selling dates for dates equally is permissible. Therefore selling fresh dates for dates equally is also permissible. And since the application of the name 'zabib' to 'cunab' is not established by hadith, therefore despite equality by measure between zabib and cunab, the difference is considered, and when difference is considered, the sale is invalid and impermissible. The author of Hidayah says: According to us, selling fresh dates for fresh dates and fresh grapes for fresh grapes by measure equally is permissible. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. According to Imam Shafi'i, it is impermissible. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that fresh dates and fresh grapes become unequal when dried, i.e., after drying it is not necessary that the two counterparts remain equal; rather increase or decrease may occur, and that is riba, and riba is impermissible. Therefore selling fresh dates for fresh dates and fresh grapes for fresh grapes by measure equally is impermissible, just as selling wheat for flour equally is impermissible. Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) called fresh dates 'tamr', so selling fresh dates for fresh dates is in reality selling dates for dates, and due to the hadith 'Dates for dates, like for like', selling dates for dates equally is permissible. Therefore selling fresh dates for fresh dates equally is also permissible. By analogy to this, selling fresh grapes for fresh grapes equally is also permissible. The author of Hidayah says: According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), selling fresh (unroasted) wheat for fresh wheat, or for soaked wheat, or for dry wheat by measure equally is permissible. Similarly, selling soaked wheat for soaked wheat and for dry wheat equally is permissible. Similarly, selling soaked dates for soaked dates and soaked raisins for soaked raisins equally is permissible. Imam Muhammad said that in the mentioned cases the sale is not permissible. Imam Shafi'i holds this view. Imam Muhammad's proof is that he considers equality and sameness in the two counterparts in the state that is most indicative of equality, which is the final state (dryness). That is, according to Imam Muhammad, after the two counterparts have dried, equality and sameness between them is necessary, as is apparent from the hadith 'Does it decrease when dry?' He said yes, so he (peace be upon him) said no. And in the mentioned cases, although equality and sameness exist at present, after drying difference will occur. Therefore in those cases the sale is impermissible. The proof of the Shaykhayn is that they act upon the famous hadith 'Wheat for wheat, dates for dates, like for like', considering equality between the two counterparts at the time of the contract. That is, in ribawi properties, it is necessary that the two counterparts be equal at the time of the contract, whether equality remains afterwards or not. However, Imam Abu Yusuf abandoned this principle of considering equality at contract time in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates due to the hadith 'Does it decrease when dry? ...' So in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, even if the two counterparts are actually equal, according to Abu Yusuf the sale is impermissible due to this hadith. As for the matter that Imam Muhammad considers actual equality in the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, i.e., if fresh dates are sold for fresh dates by measure equally, according to Imam Muhammad it is permissible, whether equality remains after drying or not. And in the aforementioned cases (fresh wheat, etc.) he considers equality in the final state, i.e., after drying. So what is the reason for distinction? The answer is that in these cases (fresh wheat, etc.) after drying the difference between the two counterparts becomes apparent even though both counterparts remain on the same name on which the contract was concluded. For example, wheat is called wheat before drying and also after drying. Similarly, dates and raisins are called dates and raisins before and after drying; no change in name occurs. And in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, the difference becomes apparent after drying even though one of them (the dried dates) remains on the same name on which the contract was concluded. So this difference appears in the essence of the subject matter, and a difference in the essence of the subject matter invalidates due to riba. Therefore in those cases the sale is invalid and impermissible. And in the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, the difference occurs after the name is removed because before drying the name of the counterparts was 'rutab' (fresh dates), and after drying they become 'tamr' (dried dates). So when the difference appears after the name is removed, it

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, a Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, deals with the complex rulings on ribawi sales involving fresh and dried produce. It opens by establishing a key distinction: when the name of a commodity changes upon drying (e.g., rutab becomes tamr), the difference in weight that appears after drying is not considered because the name change indicates a change in legal species. Conversely, when the name remains the same (e.g., wheat remains wheat, tamr remains tamr, zabib remains zabib), any difference emerging after drying is attributed to the essence of the subject matter and invalidates the sale due to riba. The author then explains the positions of the Hanafi imams on specific cases. First, regarding fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib/kishmish): Imam Abu Hanifa permits it by measure equally, reasoning that if they are the same genus, equality is required; if different, the general hadith allows any trade. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three other Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) prohibit it, citing the hadith of Zayd ibn 'Ayyash that fresh produce shrinks upon drying, implying inevitable inequality. Some scholars report a consensus that this sale is impermissible even in Abu Hanifa's view, relying on an analogy with roasted and unroasted wheat. The author then reconciles the two narrations from Abu Hanifa by focusing on the application of names: the hadith applies the name 'tamr' to 'rutab', so selling rutab for tamr is like selling tamr for tamr, which is permissible equally. No such hadith applies 'zabib' to 'cunab', so cunab and zabib remain distinct, making equality insufficient. Next, the passage discusses selling fresh dates for fresh dates and fresh grapes for fresh grapes. The Hanafi school (represented by the author of Hidayah, following the Shaykhayn—Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permits these sales by measure equally, relying on the hadith that the Prophet called fresh dates 'tamr', thus assimilating the ruling to tamr bi'l-tamr. Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i prohibit them, insisting that equality must be maintained after drying, as the hadith about shrinkage indicates. The Shaykhayn respond that the famous hadith 'wheat for wheat, dates for dates' requires equality only at the time of contract, not after drying. However, Abu Yusuf makes an exception for the sale of fresh dates for dried dates due to the explicit hadith. The author then explains why Imam Muhammad distinguishes between fresh dates for fresh dates (which he permits) and fresh wheat for fresh wheat (which he prohibits): in the former, the name changes upon drying (rutab to tamr), so any later difference is not attributed to the essence; in the latter, the name remains (wheat is still wheat), so any later difference is attributed to the essence and invalidates the sale. This same principle explains the difference between the cases where the name remains (wheat, tamr, zabib) and cases where it changes (rutab). The passage ends with a summary that in sales where the name remains, the difference appears in the essence, causing invalid sales; where the name changes, the difference is not in the essence, and the sale remains valid.

Key Terms
رطب (rutab): Fresh, moist dates as opposed to dry dates (tamr)
تمر (tamr): Dried dates
عنب (cunab): Fresh grapes
زبيب (zabib): Raisins (dried grapes)
ربا (riba): Usury or interest; here specifically riba al-fadl (surplus in barter of same genus)
مثلاً بمثل (mithlan bi-mithl): Like for like; equal in measure/weight

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the mufta bihi ruling for selling fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib) by measure equally?
A) Permissible, because both are fruits of the vine.
B) Impermissible, because fresh grapes shrink upon drying.
C) Impermissible, because the name 'zabib' is not applied to 'cunab' by hadith, making them different species.
D) Permissible, because equality at contract time is the only requirement.

Key Takeaway
The sale of fresh grapes for dried grapes by measure equally is impermissible in the Hanafi school because they are considered different legal species due to the lack of a hadith linking the names.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
12 min
Dispute on Fresh Dates for Fresh Dates and the Wheat Analogy
Explores the intra-Hanafi dispute on rutab bi'l-rutab and the wheat analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permit selling fresh dates for fresh dates equally while Imam Muhammad prohibits it, using the principle of name permanence after drying.

Core Idea
If the name remains after drying, difference is fatal; if name changes, only contract-time equality matters.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute over selling fresh dates for fresh dates (rutab bi'l-rutab) and the analogous case of fresh wheat for fresh wheat. The key is whether the commodity's name changes upon drying. The Shaykhayn hold that equality at the time of contract suffices, except where an explicit hadith overrides (rutab bi'l-tamr). Imam Muhammad insists that equality must hold after drying when the name remains the same. We will trace the proofs and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the positions of Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad
The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permit selling fresh dates for fresh dates by measure equally, as well as similar cases with wheat and soaked produce. Imam Muhammad prohibits these same sales.
Imam Muhammad makes an exception for rutab bi'l-rutab, which he permits.
2
Analyze the reasoning of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad requires equality in the final state (after drying) because the hadith of shrinkage indicates that post-drying equality is the true measure. For cases where the name remains (wheat), any difference after drying is fatal. For rutab bi'l-rutab, the name changes, so post-drying difference is not considered.
This is consistent with his view on rutab bi'l-tamr (prohibited) and rutab bi'l-rutab (permitted).
3
Analyze the reasoning of the Shaykhayn
The Shaykhayn follow the hadith 'like for like' requiring equality only at the time of contract, not after drying. They do not consider post-drying changes unless an explicit hadith (like for rutab bi'l-tamr) overrides. Thus, they permit all cases where equality exists at contract, including fresh wheat and fresh dates.
Abu Yusuf makes an exception for rutab bi'l-tamr because of the specific hadith.
4
Identify the underlying principle
The principle is whether the name of the commodity changes upon drying. If the name remains (wheat, tamr, zabib), any later difference is in the essence and invalidates. If the name changes (rutab to tamr), the difference is not in the essence and is ignored.
This principle explains why Imam Muhammad permits rutab bi'l-rutab but prohibits fresh wheat bi'l-wheat.

شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرات شیخین حدیث مشهور الحنطة بالحنطة النمر بالمتر مثلاً بمثل الحدیث پر عمل کرتے ہوئے عقد بیع کے وقت عوضین کے درمیان مساوات اور برابری کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں یعنی اموال ربویہ کی بیچ میں عقد بیع کے وقت دونوں عوضوں کا برابر برابر ہونا ضروری ہے بعد میں برابری باقی رہے یا برابری باقی نہ رہے۔ البتہ امام ابو یوسف نے عقد بیع کے وقت مساوات کا اعتبار کرنے کے اصول بیع الرطب بالتمر میں حدیث او ینقص اذا جف فقيل نعم فقال لا کی وجہ سے ترک کر دیا ہے۔ یعنی بیع الرطب بالتمر میں اگر دونوں عوض بالفعل برابر ہوں تو بھی اس حدیث کی وجہ بو یوسف کے نزدیک بیع نا جائز ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ امام محمد صبیح الرطب بالرطب میں بالفعل مساوات کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں یعنی اگر رطب کو رطب کے عوض کیل سے برابر کر کے بیچا گیا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ خشک ہو جانے کے بعد برابری باقی رہے یا نہ رہے اور مذکورہ صورتوں میں یعنی پختہ تازہ گندم وغیرہ کی بیع میں انجام کی حالت یعنی خشک ہونے کے بعد مساوات کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں۔ سو ان میں وجہ فرق کیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں یعنی تازہ گندم وغیرہ کی بیع میں خشک ہو جانے کے بعد عوضین کے درمیان تفاوت ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے باوجود یکہ دونوں عوض اسی نام پر باقی رہتے ہیں۔ جس پر عقد منعقد کیا گیا تھا مثلاً گندم خشک ہونے سے پہلے بھی گندم کہلاتا ہے اور خشک ہونے کے بعد بھی گندم ہی کہلاتا ہے اسی طرح تمر اور زبیب خشک ہونے سے پہلے بھی تمر اور زبیب ہیں اور خشک ہونے کے بعد بھی تمر اور زبیب ہی کہلاتے ہیں۔ نام میں کوئی تبدیلی واقع نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور بیع الرطب بالتمر میں خشک ہو جانے کے بعد تفاوت ظاہر ہوتا ہے باوجود یکہ دونوں میں سے ایک یعنی تم اسی نام پر باقی رہتا ہے جس پر عقد واقع ہوا تھا پس یہ تفاوت معقود علیہ کی ذات میں ظاہر ہوا اور معقود علیہ کی ذات میں جو تفاوت ہوتا ہے وہ ربوا ہونے کی وجہ سے مفسد ہوتا ہے اسلئے ان صورتوں میں بیع فاسد اور نا جائز ہے اور رطب بالرطب کی بیچ میں نیہ نام زائل ہونے کے بعد تفاوت ہوا ہے کیونکہ خشک ہونے سے پہلے عوضین کا نام رطب تھا اور خشک ہو جانے کے بعد تمر ہو گیا۔ پس جب وہ نام زائل ہونے کے بعد تفاوت ظاہر ہوا جس
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Eight. The reason for distinction is that in these cases (fresh wheat, etc.) the difference becomes apparent even though both counterparts remain on the same name on which the contract was concluded. And in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, the difference becomes apparent even though one of them (the dried dates) remains on the same name on which the contract was concluded. So this difference is in the essence of the subject matter. And in the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, the difference occurs after the name is removed, so it is not a difference in the subject matter. Therefore it is not considered. Explanation of the issue: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, selling fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib/kishmish) by measure equally is permissible. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad), it is not permissible either equally or with inequality. The proofs of the two sides have passed earlier. Imam Sahib's proof is that if cunab and zabib are of the same genus, then selling one for the other by measure equally is permissible, and if they are of different genera, then due to the hadith 'When the types differ, sell as you wish', their sale is permissible both equally and with inequality. The proof of the Sahibayn and three Imams is that since fresh grapes shrink when dried, due to the hadith of Zayd ibn 'Ayyash ... 'Does it decrease when dry?' He said yes, so he (peace be upon him) said no, the sale will not be permissible. Some people think that the sale of cunab for zabib equally is unanimously impermissible, according to the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa as well, and they have argued for this impermissibility by analogy: just as the sale of roasted wheat for unroasted wheat by measure equally is impermissible as previously mentioned, similarly the sale of fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib) by measure is impermissible despite equality. And according to this narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, it is necessary to explain the distinction between the sale of dates for fresh dates and the sale of grapes for dried grapes. Because according to Imam Sahib, the sale of dates for fresh dates equally is permissible, and according to this narration, the sale of grapes for dried grapes equally is impermissible. In any case, the reason for distinction is that the application of the name 'tamr' (dates) to 'rutab' (fresh dates) is established by the hadith 'And he ate the dates of Khaybar like this'. So selling fresh dates for dates is selling dates for dates. And selling dates for dates equally is permissible. Therefore selling fresh dates for dates equally is also permissible. And since the application of the name 'zabib' to 'cunab' is not established by hadith, therefore despite equality by measure between zabib and cunab, the difference is considered, and when difference is considered, the sale is invalid and impermissible. The author of Hidayah says: According to us, selling fresh dates for fresh dates and fresh grapes for fresh grapes by measure equally is permissible. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. According to Imam Shafi'i, it is impermissible. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that fresh dates and fresh grapes become unequal when dried, i.e., after drying it is not necessary that the two counterparts remain equal; rather increase or decrease may occur, and that is riba, and riba is impermissible. Therefore selling fresh dates for fresh dates and fresh grapes for fresh grapes by measure equally is impermissible, just as selling wheat for flour equally is impermissible. Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) called fresh dates 'tamr', so selling fresh dates for fresh dates is in reality selling dates for dates, and due to the hadith 'Dates for dates, like for like', selling dates for dates equally is permissible. Therefore selling fresh dates for fresh dates equally is also permissible. By analogy to this, selling fresh grapes for fresh grapes equally is also permissible. The author of Hidayah says: According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), selling fresh (unroasted) wheat for fresh wheat, or for soaked wheat, or for dry wheat by measure equally is permissible. Similarly, selling soaked wheat for soaked wheat and for dry wheat equally is permissible. Similarly, selling soaked dates for soaked dates and soaked raisins for soaked raisins equally is permissible. Imam Muhammad said that in the mentioned cases the sale is not permissible. Imam Shafi'i holds this view. Imam Muhammad's proof is that he considers equality and sameness in the two counterparts in the state that is most indicative of equality, which is the final state (dryness). That is, according to Imam Muhammad, after the two counterparts have dried, equality and sameness between them is necessary, as is apparent from the hadith 'Does it decrease when dry?' He said yes, so he (peace be upon him) said no. And in the mentioned cases, although equality and sameness exist at present, after drying difference will occur. Therefore in those cases the sale is impermissible. The proof of the Shaykhayn is that they act upon the famous hadith 'Wheat for wheat, dates for dates, like for like', considering equality between the two counterparts at the time of the contract. That is, in ribawi properties, it is necessary that the two counterparts be equal at the time of the contract, whether equality remains afterwards or not. However, Imam Abu Yusuf abandoned this principle of considering equality at contract time in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates due to the hadith 'Does it decrease when dry? ...' So in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, even if the two counterparts are actually equal, according to Abu Yusuf the sale is impermissible due to this hadith. As for the matter that Imam Muhammad considers actual equality in the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, i.e., if fresh dates are sold for fresh dates by measure equally, according to Imam Muhammad it is permissible, whether equality remains after drying or not. And in the aforementioned cases (fresh wheat, etc.) he considers equality in the final state, i.e., after drying. So what is the reason for distinction? The answer is that in these cases (fresh wheat, etc.) after drying the difference between the two counterparts becomes apparent even though both counterparts remain on the same name on which the contract was concluded. For example, wheat is called wheat before drying and also after drying. Similarly, dates and raisins are called dates and raisins before and after drying; no change in name occurs. And in the sale of fresh dates for dried dates, the difference becomes apparent after drying even though one of them (the dried dates) remains on the same name on which the contract was concluded. So this difference appears in the essence of the subject matter, and a difference in the essence of the subject matter invalidates due to riba. Therefore in those cases the sale is invalid and impermissible. And in the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, the difference occurs after the name is removed because before drying the name of the counterparts was 'rutab' (fresh dates), and after drying they become 'tamr' (dried dates). So when the difference appears after the name is removed, it
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, a Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, deals with the complex rulings on ribawi sales involving fresh and dried produce. It opens by establishing a key distinction: when the name of a commodity changes upon drying (e.g., rutab becomes tamr), the difference in weight that appears after drying is not considered because the name change indicates a change in legal species. Conversely, when the name remains the same (e.g., wheat remains wheat, tamr remains tamr, zabib remains zabib), any difference emerging after drying is attributed to the essence of the subject matter and invalidates the sale due to riba. The author then explains the positions of the Hanafi imams on specific cases. First, regarding fresh grapes (cunab) for dried grapes (zabib/kishmish): Imam Abu Hanifa permits it by measure equally, reasoning that if they are the same genus, equality is required; if different, the general hadith allows any trade. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three other Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) prohibit it, citing the hadith of Zayd ibn 'Ayyash that fresh produce shrinks upon drying, implying inevitable inequality. Some scholars report a consensus that this sale is impermissible even in Abu Hanifa's view, relying on an analogy with roasted and unroasted wheat. The author then reconciles the two narrations from Abu Hanifa by focusing on the application of names: the hadith applies the name 'tamr' to 'rutab', so selling rutab for tamr is like selling tamr for tamr, which is permissible equally. No such hadith applies 'zabib' to 'cunab', so cunab and zabib remain distinct, making equality insufficient. Next, the passage discusses selling fresh dates for fresh dates and fresh grapes for fresh grapes. The Hanafi school (represented by the author of Hidayah, following the Shaykhayn—Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permits these sales by measure equally, relying on the hadith that the Prophet called fresh dates 'tamr', thus assimilating the ruling to tamr bi'l-tamr. Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i prohibit them, insisting that equality must be maintained after drying, as the hadith about shrinkage indicates. The Shaykhayn respond that the famous hadith 'wheat for wheat, dates for dates' requires equality only at the time of contract, not after drying. However, Abu Yusuf makes an exception for the sale of fresh dates for dried dates due to the explicit hadith. The author then explains why Imam Muhammad distinguishes between fresh dates for fresh dates (which he permits) and fresh wheat for fresh wheat (which he prohibits): in the former, the name changes upon drying (rutab to tamr), so any later difference is not attributed to the essence; in the latter, the name remains (wheat is still wheat), so any later difference is attributed to the essence and invalidates the sale. This same principle explains the difference between the cases where the name remains (wheat, tamr, zabib) and cases where it changes (rutab). The passage ends with a summary that in sales where the name remains, the difference appears in the essence, causing invalid sales; where the name changes, the difference is not in the essence, and the sale remains valid.

Key Terms
شیخین (Shaykhayn): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (here distinguished from Muhammad)
صاحبين (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (students of Abu Hanifa)
رطب (rutab): Fresh dates
تمر (tamr): Dried dates
عنب (cunab): Fresh grapes
زبيب (zabib): Raisins (dried grapes)
حنطة (hintah): Wheat (used in the hadith 'wheat for wheat')

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the Shaykhayn's ruling on selling fresh wheat for fresh wheat by measure equally?
A) Permissible, because equality at contract time suffices.
B) Impermissible, because wheat is a ribawi item and must be equal after drying.
C) Permissible, only if both parties agree to weigh after drying.
D) Impermissible, because fresh wheat is not a ribawi item.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (Shaykhayn) permits selling fresh produce of the same kind (e.g., fresh dates for fresh dates) by measure equally, relying on contract-time equality and the principle that name change upon drying removes the essence-based concern.

Selling Fresh Dates for Dried Dates: The Timing of Equality
Intra-Hanafi dispute on riba in date exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on selling fresh dates for dried dates and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the timing of equality.

Core Idea
Equality in ribawi sales may be required at contract or after drying — the name change determines the 'illa.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab dispute about the moment when equality must hold in ribawi exchanges. The hadith 'dates for dates like for like' requires equality, but another hadith about fresh dates drying raises the question: does future inequality matter? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) generally consider only the time of contract, while Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i look to the final state after drying unless the commodity's name changes. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying riba rules to agricultural products.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two hadith
The first hadith 'al-tamr bi al-tamr mithlan bi mithlin' commands equality in date-for-date sales. The second hadith (about fresh dates drying) asks whether the sale is allowed if the fresh dates decrease when dried; the Prophet answered 'no'.
The second hadith is specific to rutab bi tamr.
2
Understand Shaykhayn's principle
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (except in this case) hold that equality at the time of contract suffices for same-genus ribawi items. The second hadith is taken as an exception for rutab bi tamr.
Abu Yusuf abandons the general principle for this specific case.
3
Understand Imam Muhammad's principle
Imam Muhammad requires equality after drying if the name of the commodity does not change (e.g., wheat remains wheat, dates remain dates). If the name changes (rutab becomes tamr), only contract-time equality matters.
This is why rutab bi rutab is permissible even if future inequality arises.
4
Apply the distinction
In fresh wheat vs. dry wheat, name unchanged → future equality required (Imam Muhammad). In fresh dates vs. dry dates, name changes → only contract equality needed. Contrast this with fresh dates for fresh dates: name changes after drying, so permissible.
The 'illa is the presence or absence of name change in the subject matter.

بعد تفاوت ظاہر ہوا جس پر عقد واقع ہوا تھا تو یہ معقود علیہ کی ذات میں تفاوت نہ ہوا اور جب معقود علیہ کی ذات میں تفاوت نہ ہوا تو اس کا اعتبار بھی نہ ہوگا۔اور جب اس تفاوت کا اعتبار نہیں تو رطب کی بیع رطب کے عوض جائز ہے۔
Our argument is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) called fresh dates (rutab) as dates (tamr), so selling fresh dates for fresh dates is in reality selling dates for dates, and due to the hadith 'dates for dates like for like', selling dates for dates equally is permissible. Therefore, selling fresh dates for fresh dates equally is also permissible. By analogy on this, selling grapes for grapes equally is also permissible. The author of Hidayah says that according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), selling fresh wheat for fresh wheat, or for soaked wheat, or for dry wheat is permissible after equalizing by measure, and similarly selling soaked wheat for soaked wheat and dry wheat equally is permissible. Similarly, selling soaked dates for soaked dates and soaked raisins for soaked raisins equally is permissible. Imam Muhammad said that in the mentioned cases, the sale is not permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i also holds this view. Imam Muhammad's argument is that they (the two shaykhs) consider equality between the two counter-values in the state that is most indicative of equality, which is the end state after drying. That is, in his view, equality after drying is necessary between the counter-values, as is apparent from the hadith: 'Does it decrease when it dries? He said yes, then the Prophet said: No.' In the mentioned cases, although equality exists at present, disparity will occur after drying, so the sale is impermissible. The two shaykhs' argument is that they act on the famous hadith 'wheat for wheat, dates for dates, like for like' and consider equality at the time of the contract. In sales of ribawi items, both counter-values must be equal at the time of contract, whether equality remains afterwards or not. However, Imam Abu Yusuf abandoned the principle of considering equality at the time of contract in the case of selling fresh dates for dates due to the hadith 'Does it decrease when it dries? He said yes, then the Prophet said: No.' So according to Imam Abu Yusuf, even if both counter-values are actually equal, the sale of fresh dates for dates is impermissible due to this hadith. As for Imam Muhammad, he considers actual equality in the case of selling fresh dates for fresh dates, i.e., if fresh dates are sold for fresh dates by measure equally, then it is permissible according to him, whether equality remains after drying or not. But in the mentioned cases (fresh wheat etc.), he considers the end state after drying. So what is the difference? The answer is that in these cases (fresh wheat etc.), disparity becomes apparent after drying even though both counter-values remain under the same name as that on which the contract was concluded. For example, wheat is called wheat before and after drying; similarly dates and raisins are called by the same names before and after drying; no change in name occurs. In the case of selling fresh dates for dates, disparity becomes apparent after drying even though one of them, i.e., dates, remains on the same name as that on which the contract was concluded. So this disparity appears in the essence of the subject matter, and disparity in the essence of the subject matter is corrupting due to riba, so the sale is invalid and impermissible in these cases. In the sale of fresh dates for fresh dates, disparity occurs after the name ceases, because before drying the counter-values were called fresh dates and after drying they become dates. So when disparity appears after the name on which the contract was concluded has ceased, then it is not disparity in the essence of the subject matter, and when it is not in the essence, it is not considered. So selling fresh dates for fresh dates is permissible.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute about the sale of ribawi items of the same genus but different states of freshness. The core issue is whether equality must be present at the time of contract or after drying. The Hanafi school (Shaykhayn: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) generally holds that equality at the time of contract suffices, based on the hadith 'dates for dates like for like'. However, Abu Yusuf makes an exception for fresh dates (rutab) sold for dried dates (tamr) due to a specific hadith indicating that fresh dates decrease when dried, thus future inequality is considered. Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i require equality after drying in cases where the name remains the same (e.g., fresh and dry wheat both called 'wheat'), but allow fresh dates for fresh dates because the name changes from rutab to tamr upon drying. The text explains the reasoning: if the name does not change, drying causes disparity in the essence (ayn) of the commodity, which triggers riba. If the name changes, the disparity is only in the name, not in the essence, so the sale is permissible. This is a nuanced application of the principles of riba al-fadl and the role of 'illa (effective cause) in analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
رطب (rutab): Fresh dates that are moist and not yet dried
تمر (tamr): Dried dates, the fully ripened and dried fruit of the date palm
مثلاً بمثل (mithlan bi mithlin): Like for like, meaning equal in measure or weight
ربوی (ribawi): An item subject to riba rules: gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt, and their analogies.
علت (illa): The effective cause that gives a ruling, here the 'illa for riba in same-genus items is jins (genus) and miqdar (quantity) by weight/measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because fresh wheat loses weight when dried, but fresh dates gain weight.
B) Because the name 'wheat' remains the same after drying, while 'rutab' changes to 'tamr'.
C) Because the hadith about drying only applies to dates, not wheat.
D) Because Imam Muhammad only uses the hadith about drying for fruits, not grains.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the apparent conflict between two hadith by distinguishing cases where the commodity's name remains unchanged (future equality required) versus where it changes (only contract equality needed).

Definition and Ruling: Busr vs Kafari in Date Exchanges
Rules of selling early-stage dates for dried dates and distinguishing kafari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish busr from kafari in terms of legal genus and state the rulings for their exchange with tamr under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Busr is tamr, so unequal exchange is riba; kafari is not tamr, but its unknown quantity blocks salam.

In this passage, the Hanafi school clarifies two types of date products: busr (fresh dates immediately after the cluster opens) and kafari (the covering or sheath before the fruit forms). Although both originate from the date palm, they have distinct legal identities. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying riba rules and salam conditions in date transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The passage addresses the permissibility of selling busr (fresh dates) and kafari (date buds) for tamr (dried dates) with inequality, and the validity of salam when the subject is kafari.
2
Define Busr and Its Legal Status
Busr is defined as tamr—the same genus. Therefore, selling busr for tamr with inequality is prohibited (riba). It must be exchanged equally by measure and hand-to-hand.
The Urdu explanation describes busr as 'gora'.
3
Define Kafari and Its Legal Status
Kafari is the covering of the date cluster before the fruit forms; it is not tamr. Hence, it can be exchanged with tamr unequally (even two for one) without riba.
The name 'tamr' applies only after the fruit's form appears.
4
Examine the Exception for Salam
Although kafari is not tamr, salam (forward sale) is invalid because kafari is 'adadi mutafawit'—sold by count and variable in size/value, causing jahalah (ignorance).
This answers the potential objection of why kafari cannot be the subject of salam.
5
Summarize Practical Rules
Spot exchange: busr–tamr must be equal by weight/measure and hand-to-hand; kafari–tamr can be unequal. Credit sale: kafari cannot be sold on credit due to uncertainty; busr-tamr on credit is also invalid (riba).

Source Text

بسر کی تمر کے ساتھ تفاضلا بیع کا حکم

ولو باع البسر بالتمر متفاضلا لايجوز؛ لأن البسر تمر بخلاف الكفرى حيث يجوز بيعه بما شاء من التمر اثنان بواحد لانه ليس بتمر فإن هذا الاسم له من أول ما تنعقد صورته لا قبله والكفرى عددى متفاوت حتى لو باع التمر به نسيئة لايجوز للجهالة

ترجمہ: اور اگر گدرے چھوارے کو خشک چھوارے کے عوض کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کیا تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ بسر بھی تمر ہے برخلاف غنچہ کے اسلئے کہ اس کو جس قدر چھواروں کے عوض چاہے بیچنا جائز ہے دو کو ایک کے عوض کیونکہ غنچہ، چھوارہ نہیں ہوتا اسلئے کہ یہ نام اور اس کی ابتدائی شکل بننے پر ہوتا ہے اس سے پہلے نہیں ہوتا اور کفری ( غنچہ ) عددی متفاوت ہے حتی کہ اگر فنچہ کے عوض چھوارے کو ادھار فروخت کیا تو مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے۔

تشریح: بسر وہ چھوارہ جو کھل کھلنے کے بعد ابتدائی شکل پر ہوتا ہے اردو زبان میں اس کو گورا کہا جاتا ہے۔ کفری را کی تشدید کے ساتھ کھجور کے شگوفہ کا غلاف یعنی کھجور کے پھل کی ابتدائی شکل بننے سے پہلے کی حالت کو کفری کہتے ہیں۔

صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ گدری کھجوروں کو خشک چھواروں کے عوض کمی، زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا نا جائز ہے کیونکہ بسر بھی تمر ہے اور تمر کی بیع تمر کے عوض کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے بسر کی بیع تمر کے عوض کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ نا جائز ہوگی۔ البتہ کیل کے ذریعہ برابر، برابر بیچنا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ مجلس عقد میں باہم قبضہ ہو جائے، ہاں کھجور کے شگوفوں کی بیع چھواروں کے عوض برابر برابر بھی جائز ہے اور کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ بھی جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ دو شگوفوں کو ایک چھوارے کے عوض اور دو چھواروں کو ایک شگوفہ کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفری ( شگوفہ ) چونکہ کھجور کی ابتدائی شکل بنے سے پہلے کی حالت کا نام ہے اس لئے کفری تمر نہیں ہوگا اور جب کفری، تمر نہیں ہے تو ان دونوں میں اختلاف جنس پایا گیا اور اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں عقد بیع متساویا اور متفاضلاً دونوں طرح جائز ہوتا ہے اسلئے کفری کی بیع تمر کے عوض متساویا اور متفاضلا دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔

والكفرى عدد ...... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جب کفری ( شگوفہ ) تمر کا ہم جنس نہیں ہے تو کفری کے اندر بیع سلم جائز ہونی چاہئے بایں طور کہ تمر کو راس المال اور کفری کو مسلم فیہ قرار دینا درست ہو حالانکہ بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کفری چونکہ عددی متفاوت ہے یعنی کفری کی خرید و فروخت گن کر ہوتی ہے اور اسکے احادو افراد چھوٹے، بڑے ہونے کی وجہ سے مالیت میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں اسلئے مسلم فیہ یعنی کفری کے مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع سلم نا جائز ہوگی۔ حتی کہ اگر چھوارے کو کفری کے عوض ادھار فروخت کیا تو کفری کے مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ کفری چونکہ چھوٹے بڑے ہوتے
Ruling on selling busr for tamr with inequality: And if one sells busr for tamr with inequality, it is not permissible, because busr is tamr, unlike kafari, for which it is permissible to sell it for as many tamr as one wishes, two for one, because it is not tamr. This name (tamr) is for it from the time its form first appears, not before. And kafari is counted and disparate, such that if one sells tamr for it on credit, it is not permissible due to ignorance. Translation: And if one sells fresh dates (busr) for dried dates (tamr) with excess or deficiency, it is not permissible because busr is also tamr. Unlike the bud (kafari), because it is permissible to sell it for as many tamr as one wishes, two for one, because the bud is not tamr. This name is for it from the time its form appears, not before. And kafari (bud) is counted and disparate, such that if one sells tamr for it on credit, it is not permissible due to ignorance. Explanation: Busr is the date that is at the initial stage after the cluster opens; in Urdu it is called 'gora'. Kafari (with tashdid on 'ra') is the covering of the date cluster, i.e., the state before the date fruit's initial form appears. The scenario is that selling fresh dates (busr) for dried dates with excess or deficiency is not permissible because busr is tamr, and selling tamr for tamr with excess or deficiency is not permissible. Therefore, selling busr for tamr with excess or deficiency is not permissible. However, selling by measure equally is permissible provided there is hand-to-hand exchange in the session. Yes, selling date buds (kafari) for tamr is permissible both equally and with excess/deficiency. For example, selling two buds for one tamr or two tamr for one bud is permissible. The proof is that kafari (bud) is the name for the state before the initial form of the date appears, so kafari is not tamr. When kafari is not tamr, there is a difference of genus, and in case of difference of genus, the sale is permissible both equally and with inequality. Therefore, selling kafari for tamr is permissible in both ways. 'Wal kafari 'adadi...' etc. is an answer to a question. The question is: When kafari (bud) is not of the same genus as tamr, then salam sale (advance payment) should be permissible in kafari, i.e., making tamr as capital and kafari as the commodity to be delivered should be correct, whereas salam is not permissible. The answer is that kafari is counted and disparate, i.e., its sale is by counting, and its individuals vary in value due to being small or large, so the commodity (muslam fihi) is unknown, making salam impermissible. Even if one sells tamr for kafari on credit, the sale is not permissible due to the unknown nature of kafari, because kafari are small and large.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling that clarifies the status of busr (fresh dates at the initial stage after the cluster opens) and kafari (the covering of the date cluster, i.e., the undeveloped state before the fruit forms) in the context of riba. The matn states that selling busr for tamr with inequality is invalid because busr is considered tamr—it is the same genus. Therefore, the rules of riba apply: equal exchange in weight/measure and hand-to-hand delivery. However, kafari is not tamr; it is a different genus, so exchange can be unequal. The commentary explains that busr is called 'gora' in Urdu, and kafari is the covering (sheath) of the date cluster before the fruit forms. The key distinction is that busr is a stage of tamr, so it shares the same legal identity; kafari is a separate entity. This leads to the ruling that selling busr for tamr with inequality is prohibited, but selling kafari for tamr is allowed even with inequality. The text also addresses a potential objection: if kafari is not tamr, why is salam (forward sale) not allowed for kafari? The answer is that kafari is a counted commodity (ma'dud) whose individual units vary in size and value, making the subject matter unknown (jahalah), which invalidates salam. Thus, the impermissibility of salam here is not due to riba but due to uncertainty.

Key Terms
بسر (busr): Fresh dates at the initial stage right after the cluster opens, before ripening; considered tamr in legal rulings
كفرى (kafari): The covering of the date cluster (sheath) before the date fruit forms; not considered tamr
عددى متفاوت (adadi mutafawit): A commodity that is sold by counting and whose individual units vary in size and value, leading to uncertainty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling busr (fresh dates) for tamr (dried dates) with inequality prohibited?
A) Because busr is not tamr
B) Because busr is tamr and ribawi rules require equality
C) Because the sale is without measure
D) Because it is a credit sale

Key Takeaway
Busr is tamr, so riba governs its exchange with tamr; kafari is not tamr but is adadi mutafawit, making its credit sale invalid but its spot sale permissible even unequally.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on Selling Unripe Dates (Busr) for Dry Dates (Tamr) with Disparity
Explains prohibition of busr for tamr with disparity and exception for kafri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling busr for tamr with disparity, explain the genus-based reasoning, and distinguish the exception for kafri and its implications for salam.

Core Idea
Busr is tamr, so disparity is riba; kafri is not tamr, so disparity is permissible.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains a key fiqh distinction in date transactions: selling unripe dates (busr) for dry dates (tamr) with disparity is prohibited because busr shares the same genus as tamr. However, the spathe (kafri) before fruit formation is a different genus, so disparity is allowed. The author also addresses why salam (advance sale) is invalid for kafri due to ignorance of quantity. Understanding this requires grasping how the Hanafi school defines ribawi genera and the condition of knowledge in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two products and their legal status
Recognize that busr (unripe dates just after cluster opens) and tamr (dry dates) are both ribawi items measured by weight/volume. The passage also introduces kafri (spathe before fruit formation).
Busr is considered tamr by the Hanafis for riba purposes; kafri is not.
2
Determine the ruling for busr-tamr sale with disparity
State that selling busr for tamr with excess or deficiency (e.g., 2 kg busr for 1 kg tamr) is not permissible. If equal in measure and hand-to-hand, it is permissible.
The prohibition is due to riba fadl (unequal exchange of same genus ribawi items).
3
Analyze the reasoning: why busr is considered tamr
The author states 'busr is tamr' because the name 'tamr' applies from the moment the fruit forms its initial shape. Thus busr falls under the same genus, triggering riba rules.
This is a textual (linguistic) basis, not merely customary.
4
Identify the exception: kafri
Kafri (spathe) is before the fruit forms, so it is not tamr. Hence selling kafri for tamr with disparity (e.g., two spathes for one tamr) is permissible.
Kafri is a different genus, so riba rules do not apply to disparity.
5
Understand why salam for kafri is invalid
Although kafri is a different genus, salam (advance payment sale) is invalid because kafri is 'adadi mutafawit' (counted but individually variable). This leads to jahalah (ignorance) about the exact subject matter, which invalidates the contract.
Credit sales of kafri for tamr also invalid due to jahalah; only spot sale is allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ گدری کھجوروں کو خشک چھواروں کے عوض کمی، زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کرنا نا جائز ہے کیونکہ بسر بھی تمر ہے اور تمر کی بیع تمر کے عوض کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے بسر کی بیع تمر کے عوض کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ نا جائز ہوگی۔ البتہ کیل کے ذریعہ برابر، برابر بیچنا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ مجلس عقد میں باہم قبضہ ہو جائے ، ہاں کھجور کے شگوفوں کی بیچ چھواروں کے عوض برابر برابر بھی جائز ہے اور کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ بھی جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ دو شگوفوں کو ایک چھوارے کے عوض اور دو چھواروں کو ایک شگوفہ کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفری ( شگوفہ ) چونکہ کھجور کی ابتدائی شکل بنے سے پہلے کی حالت کا نام ہے اس لئے کفری تمر نہیں ہوگا اور جب کفری، تمر نہیں سے تو ان دونوں میں اختلاف جنس پایا گیا اور اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں عقد بیع متسا دیا اور متفاضلاً دونوں طرح جائز ہوتا ہے اسلئے کفری کی بیع تمر کے عوض متساویا اور متفاضلا دونوں طرح جائز ہے۔
والكفرى عدد ...... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جب کفری ( شگوفہ ) تمر کا ہم جنس نہیں ہے تو کفری کے اندر بیع سلم جائز ہونی چاہئے بایں طور کہ تمر کو راس المال اور کفری کو مسلم فیہ قرار دینا درست ہو حالانکہ بیع سلم جائز نہیں ہے۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کفری چونکہ عددی متفاوت ہے یعنی کفری کی خرید و فروخت گن کر ہوتی ہے اور اسکے احادو افراد چھوٹے، بڑے ہونے کی وجہ سے مالیت میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں اسلئے مسلم فیہ یعنی کفری کے مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع سلم نا جائز ہوگی۔ حتی کہ اگر چھوارے کو کفری کے عوض ادھار فروخت کیا تو کفری کے مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ کفری چونکہ چھوٹے بڑے ہوتے ہیں اسلئے ادھار ہونے کیوجہ سے انکی شناخت نہیں ہو سکتی۔ بلکہ قبضہ کے وقت نزاع پیدا ہو گا۔ اس طور پر کہ مشتری چھوٹے چھوٹے کفری سپرد کر دیگا اور بائع بڑے بڑے کفری کا مطالبہ کر یگا اور مفضی الی النزاع کی چیز چونکہ مفسد بیج ہوتی ہے اسلئے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہوگی۔
And if one sells unripe dates (busr) for dry dates (tamr) with disparity, it is not permissible, because busr is tamr, unlike kafri (spathe) for which it is permissible to sell for whatever amount of tamr one wishes, even two for one, because it is not tamr. For this name (tamr) applies from the first time its (the fruit's) form appears, not before. And kafri is numerically disparate, so much so that if one sells tamr for it on credit, it is not permissible due to ignorance (jahalah). Translation: And if unripe dates are sold for dry dates with excess or deficiency, it is not permissible, because busr is also tamr. Unlike the spathe, because selling it for whatever amount of dates one wishes is permissible, two for one, because the spathe is not dates. For this name (dates) applies at the formation of its initial shape, not before. And kafri (spathe) is numerically disparate, so much so that if dates are sold for it on credit, it is not permissible due to ignorance. Explanation: Busr is the date that is in its initial form after the cluster opens; in Urdu it is called 'gura'. Kafri, with tashdid on the ra, is the covering of the date-palm spathe, i.e., the state before the initial formation of the date fruit. The ruling: Selling unripe dates for dry dates with excess or deficiency is not permissible, because busr is also tamr, and selling tamr for tamr with disparity is not permissible. Therefore, selling busr for tamr with disparity is not permissible. However, selling them by measure, equal for equal, is permissible provided hand-to-hand exchange takes place in the session. Yes, selling spathes (kafri) for dates, whether equal or with disparity, is permissible. For example, selling two spathes for one date, or two dates for one spathe, is permissible. The proof is that kafri (spathe) is the name of the state before the initial formation of the date, so kafri is not tamr. When kafri is not tamr, there is difference of genus between them, and in case of difference of genus, the sale is permissible both equally and with disparity. Hence, selling kafri for tamr is permissible in both ways. 'Wa al-kafri 'adadi...' etc. is a response to a question. The question is: When kafri (spathe) is not of the same genus as tamr, then salam sale (advance payment) should be permissible for kafri, such that tamr is the capital (ra's al-mal) and kafri is the subject matter (muslam fih), yet salam is not permissible. The answer: Because kafri is numerically disparate, i.e., its sale is counted, and its individual units differ in value due to size, therefore the subject matter (kafri) is unknown, so salam is not permissible. Even if dates are sold for kafri on credit, the sale is not permissible due to kafri being unknown. Because kafri come in small and large sizes, so on credit they cannot be identified. At the time of delivery, dispute would arise: the buyer would hand over small kafri and the seller would demand large kafri. Since that which leads to dispute corrupts the sale, the sale is invalid (fasid) in this case.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the book Al-Hidayah. The author presents the ruling on selling unripe dates (busr) for dry dates (tamr) with disparity: it is not permissible. The reasoning is that busr is considered tamr – it shares the same genus – and the prohibition of riba applies to exchanges of the same genus with inequality. However, an exception is made for kafri (the spathe or initial unsheathed cluster of dates). Since kafri is not yet tamr (the name 'tamr' only applies after the fruit forms), it is a different genus, so selling kafri for tamr with disparity is permissible. The author then addresses a potential question: if kafri is a different genus, why is salam (advance sale) not allowed for it? The answer is that kafri is 'adadi mutafawit' – it is sold by count, and individual units vary in size and value, leading to ignorance (jahalah) which invalidates salam and also credit sales. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that riba applies to same genus items measured by weight or volume, and that jahalah can invalidate sales. The passage carefully distinguishes between busr (which is tamr) and kafri (which is not), and explains the implications for riba and salam.

Key Terms
بسر (busr): Unripe dates that have just formed after the cluster opens; in the text, considered to be of the same genus as tamr.
كفرى (kafri): The spathe or unsheathed cluster of dates before the fruit forms; not considered tamr.
تمر (tamr): Dry dates, the fully ripe and dried fruit, a ribawi item measured by weight/volume.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling unripe dates (busr) for dry dates (tamr) with disparity not permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because busr is not a ribawi item.
B) Because busr is considered the same genus as tamr, so inequality constitutes riba fadl.
C) Because busr is not measured by weight.
D) Because the sale involves ignorance (jahalah) about the quantity of busr.

Key Takeaway
Busr and tamr are the same genus for riba, so disparity is prohibited; kafri is a different genus, so disparity is allowed, but its variable nature prohibits credit sales due to ignorance.
